validateRouted coerces any malformed tier to 3, silently escalating model noise into a queued claude -p run with a mismatched spoken reply

lib/router.ts:869-877 · reviewer: router-model-engine-seam
What it is
validateRouted maps every tier value that is not exactly the number 1 or 2 to tier 3: `const tier = parsed.tier === 1 || parsed.tier === 2 ? parsed.tier : 3;`. A Haiku response with a string tier (`"tier": "1"` — a common LLM slip; the Haiku path has no grammar enforcement, unlike the local Ollama path whose ROUTE_SCHEMA constrains tier to an integer enum), a missing tier, or any other garbage is treated as an intentional tier-3 classification. Because the skill guard runs only `tier === 1 && parsed.skill`, a response like {"tier":"1","skill":"inbox-brief","reply":"Running the inbox brief now."} becomes {tier:3, skill:undefined, reply:"Running the inbox brief now."}. dispatchTranscript (lib/voiceDispatch.ts:135-143) then queues a `voice-ask` intent — a real headless `claude -p` run — while speaking the tier-1 ack. The `String(parsed.reply ?? "Done.")` default has the same shape of problem: a tier-3 result with a missing reply speaks "Done." as the ack for a run that has only just been queued.
Why it matters
A truncated or malformed router response should degrade to the next engine or the rules fallback (returning null does exactly that — pickEngine already handles it at lines 110-114). Instead it silently escalates: model formatting noise spends a full background Claude session, and the user hears an ack for the skill they asked for while a different, generic run executes — the exact 'voice quietly misroutes' failure mode CLAUDE.md warns about. The tier/skill/reply triple handed to the HUD is internally inconsistent (tier-1 wording, tier-3 behavior).
How to fix
In validateRouted, treat an unrecognized tier as invalid rather than tier 3: coerce numeric strings (`Number(parsed.tier)`) and return null when the result is not 1, 2, or 3, so the caller's existing `?? rulesRoute(...)` / next-engine fallback takes over. Only pass tier 3 through when the model actually said 3. Optionally replace the "Done." default with a tier-appropriate ack ("Working on it") or bounce null on a missing reply.
Expected improvement
Garbage model output falls back to the local engine or rules instead of queuing an unintended tier-3 claude -p run; spoken replies always match what was actually dispatched.
Evidence
const tier = parsed.tier === 1 || parsed.tier === 2 ? parsed.tier : 3;
...
if (tier === 1 && !skill) return null;
...
return { tier, skill, reply: String(parsed.reply ?? "Done."), engine, panels };
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Confirmed in current code. lib/router.ts:870 reads exactly `const tier = parsed.tier === 1 || parsed.tier === 2 ? parsed.tier : 3;` — strict equality means string "1", missing, or garbage tier coerces to 3; the skill guard (871-873) runs only for tier===1, so the coerced result carries skill:undefined plus the model's tier-1 reply verbatim, and line 877 has the `String(parsed.reply ?? "Done.")` default. haikuRoute (934-938) is regex+JSON.parse with no schema enforcement, so malformed tiers are reachable there; the local Ollama path's ROUTE_SCHEMA (953-962) enforces integer enum tier and required reply, so the bug is Haiku-path-only in practice — the "any malformed tier" headline slightly overstates the local side. pickEngine (106-114) confirms null would degrade to next engine/rules as the proposed fix assumes. lib/voiceDispatch.ts:133-147 confirms tier-3 with a >=3-word ask queues a real voice-ask (claude -p) while speaking the passed-through reply. Scope narrower than worst case: in default auto mode Haiku only runs after rules fallthrough (line 108), so the escalation needs a skill ask that the tier-1 regex missed plus a Haiku formatting slip — but the consequence (spent background claude session + internally inconsistent tier/skill/reply ack, the CLAUDE.md "voice quietly misroutes" mode) justifies keeping medium. Not covered by ADR-0006 (tiering) or any excluded known item.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read lib/router.ts (validateRouted at 869-878, pickEngine at 89-115, haikuRoute at 907-939, localRoute + ROUTE_SCHEMA at 949-1014), lib/voiceDispatch.ts:125-155, and scripts/test-router.ts. The code is exactly as quoted: line 870 coerces any tier that is not the number 1 or 2 to tier 3, and the skill guard at 871-873 drops the skill, so a parseable Haiku response with `"tier":"1"` plus a valid skill becomes {tier:3, skill:undefined} while keeping the tier-1 ack as reply; dispatchTranscript (voiceDispatch.ts:135-143) then queues a real voice-ask claude -p run behind that mismatched ack. Confirmed asymmetry: the local Ollama path is grammar-enforced (ROUTE_SCHEMA at 953-962 constrains tier to integer enum [1,2,3], required), so only the Haiku path (free-text + regex JSON extraction at 936-938, no schema) is exposed. No test covers validateRouted with malformed model output, and the comment at 867-868 documents only the tier-1-without-skill bounce, not the coercion — so this is not an asserted intentional design. Corrections that lower severity to low: (a) the finding's "truncated response" example is wrong — a truncated/garbage response fails JSON.parse, throws, and is already caught by engineFail → rules fallback; only well-formed JSON with a wrong-typed or missing tier hits the coercion; (b) in the default VOICE_ROUTER=auto mode, haikuRoute only runs after rulesRoute fell through, and rules catch the common skill phrasings (test-router.ts's tier-1 cases all resolve via rules), so the failure needs BOTH an unusual phrasing that rules missed AND Haiku emitting a mistyped tier for a tier-1 intent — a double precondition making it rare. The proposed fix (Number-coerce, return null on anything not 1/2/3 so pickEngine's ?? fallback takes over) is correct and safe: haikuRoute returning null falls to localRoute then rules per lines 109-114. The "Done." default reply nit is real but cosmetic.

todos.ts CHECKBOX regex silently drops indented sub-tasks, `*` bullets, and non-x task states

lib/todos.ts:27-47 · reviewer: vault-markdown-parsers
What it is
parseTodos matches checkbox lines with `const CHECKBOX = /^- \[( |x|X)\] (.*)$/` — anchored at column 0, dash bullet only, state char limited to space/x/X. Three legitimate Obsidian task forms fail to match and are silently omitted from the parse: (1) indented sub-tasks, which Obsidian creates with a single Tab press, e.g. `\t- [ ] follow up with recruiter` or ` - [ ] send thank-you note`; (2) asterisk bullets, `* [ ] prep STAR stories`; (3) alternate task states some Obsidian themes/plugins write, e.g. `- [-] cancelled` or `- [/] in progress`. Unmatched lines are skipped with no diagnostic (`if (!m) continue;`), so those items never appear in GET /api/todos, never render on the jobs tab tile, and cannot be toggled. The file header explicitly says "Obsidian edits and HUD edits act on the same file", so hand-nesting a sub-task is expected usage. toggleTodo uses the same regex for its line walk, so indexes stay consistent (no mis-toggle) — the failure mode is pure invisibility. The live vault file currently contains zero such lines (verified), so this is latent, not active.
Why it matters
An item Daniel nests under a parent task in Obsidian vanishes from the HUD tile with no error and no count discrepancy he can notice — the exact 'silently vanish' failure the tile is supposed to prevent. Because both parse and toggle skip the same lines, nothing ever surfaces the omission.
How to fix
Widen the regex to tolerate leading whitespace and either bullet, e.g. `/^\s*[-*] \[(.)\] (.*)$/`, treating any state char other than a space as done (or mapping `-` to done/cancelled). toggleTodo already re-derives the checkbox prefix from the match, so preserve the original indentation/bullet when rewriting the line (`lines[i].replace(/\[(.)\]/, ...)` style) instead of hard-coding `- [x] `. Add the variant lines to scripts/test-todos.ts fixtures.
Expected improvement
Nested and asterisk-bulleted Obsidian tasks appear in the tile and are toggleable; no task authored in normal Obsidian syntax can silently disappear from the HUD.
Evidence
const CHECKBOX = /^- \[( |x|X)\] (.*)$/;  ...  const m = line.match(CHECKBOX);
    if (!m) continue;
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read lib/todos.ts in full. Line 27 is exactly `const CHECKBOX = /^- \[( |x|X)\] (.*)$/;` — column-0 anchored, dash bullet only, state limited to space/x/X — and line 38-39 (`const m = line.match(CHECKBOX); if (!m) continue;`) silently skips non-matching lines, so indented sub-tasks, `* [ ]` bullets, and alternate states like `- [-]` / `- [/]` are omitted from parseTodos with no diagnostic. Cited line range 27-47 is accurate (regex at 27, skip at 39; toggleTodo's reuse of the same regex is at 59, and line 61 hard-codes the `- [x] ` prefix as the fix note says, which would strip indentation if the regex were widened naively — the finding's how_to_fix correctly anticipates this). Both parse and toggle use the same regex, so no mis-toggle occurs; failure mode is invisibility only, as claimed. Verified the live vault file ~/Projects/Vault/jobs/todos.md contains zero indented/asterisk/alt-state checkbox lines (grep count 0), confirming the finding's own "latent, not active" caveat. Not covered by any ADR (files-as-database is intentional but the parser silently dropping valid Obsidian task syntax is not) and not in the known/excluded list. Severity: suggest low rather than medium — purely latent (zero affected lines today), single-user tool, and the file header/comment describes the format narrowly as `- [ ]` / `- [x]` lines, so this is arguably a documented format constraint that Obsidian usage could drift out of, not an active bug. The description itself is accurate in every checked particular.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Confirmed against current code. lib/todos.ts line 27: CHECKBOX = /^- \[( |x|X)\] (.*)$/ — column-0 anchored, dash-only bullet, space/x/X states; line 39 silently skips non-matching lines. Indented sub-tasks, `* [ ]` bullets, and alternate states (`- [-]`, `- [/]`) are invisible to GET /api/todos and untoggleable, exactly as described. toggleTodo uses the same regex so indexes stay consistent (no mis-toggle) — finding is correct that the failure is pure invisibility. scripts/test-todos.ts fixtures have no such variant lines. Corrections/downgrades: (a) the module header (lines 7-8) documents the file format as flat `- [ ]`/`- [x]` dash lines, making this a weakly-documented invariant rather than a plain oversight; (b) the finding admits the live vault file currently has zero such lines — latent; (c) no data loss: the markdown file is never corrupted, items stay visible in Obsidian; single-user tool. Severity medium is inflated → low. The proposed fix is sound, and its caution about preserving indentation/bullet in toggleTodo is essential — line 61 hardcodes `- [x] `, so widening the regex without a replace-in-place rewrite would mangle indented lines on toggle.
lowConfirmed backend effort: trivial

stateAnswer schedule branch shadows subject-specific 'what's next' questions

lib/router.ts:720 · reviewer: bugs-router
What it is
The schedule branch fires on /schedule|next today|what'?s next|whats next|next up/ anywhere in the utterance and sits above the Morphy-board branch (line 753) and after only the metric branches. 'what's next on the morphy board' or 'what's next for michael' therefore answers from the daily-note schedule ('Coming up at 3 PM — …' or 'You're clear for the rest of the day') instead of the Morphy board, and never reaches the morphy/michael lane or the model engines. The github branch has an explicit ordering comment for exactly this shadowing class ('before the Morphy-board lane on purpose'), but the schedule branch's broad 'what's next' net has no subject guard.
Why it matters
Order-dependent shadowing: a confident, wrong tier-2 answer about the wrong subject, with no fallthrough for a smarter engine to correct it. 'What's next' is a natural way to ask about any workstream, not just today's calendar.
How to fix
Require the bare phrasings to be subject-free: either move the schedule branch below the morphy branch, or exclude utterances that also match /morphy|michael/ (mirroring the isMorphySync exclusion pattern at line 752), keeping /schedule/ and 'next today' as-is.
Expected improvement
'What's next on the morphy board' answers about the board; the daily-schedule answer keeps firing for genuine schedule asks.
Evidence
if (/schedule|next today|what'?s next|whats next|next up/.test(t)) {
    const d = state.daily;
    if (!d || d.schedule.length === 0) return { text: "Nothing's on the schedule.", panels: ["schedule"] };

Evidence snippet matches verbatim. Not a duplicate of any excluded item; does not conflict with ADR-0006 (tiering intentional — this is a shadowing bug within tier-2 rules). Severity low is appropriate: wrong-subject answer for a natural phrasing, but recoverable by rephrasing and no side effects. Bare 'okay'/'ok' after a standing offer is swallowed by smalltalk as 'Standing by.'

lib/router.ts:185-194 · reviewer: bugs-router
What it is
AFFIRM_RE does not include 'ok'/'okay' as a standalone affirmation, though the composition-stripper does (isAffirm strips a leading '(?:yes|yeah|yep|sure|ok(?:ay)?)' — so 'okay, do it' works but bare 'okay' does not). After the briefing offer ('Want me to run the daily inbox audit…?'), a bare 'okay' fails isAffirm/isDecline, skips the pendingOffer block entirely, and lands in smalltalk's bare-ack rule (line 328, which lists ok/okay) returning 'Standing by.' — the exact same reply the explicit-decline path uses. Similarly 'yes, run it' fails: stripping 'yes,' leaves 'run it', which is not in AFFIRM_RE, so the whole utterance bypasses the offer block and falls to tier-3.
Why it matters
'Okay' is among the most natural spoken consents. The user believes they accepted the offer; nothing runs, and the reply gives no hint the consent was dropped. Because smalltalk answers tier-2, not even the model engines get a chance to interpret it against the convo context.
How to fix
In rulesRoute, when pendingOffer() returns a skill, treat the bare-ack set (ok/okay/sure/sounds good) as affirmative before the smalltalk pass — i.e. check pendingOffer first for short ack-shaped utterances, or add ok|okay to AFFIRM_RE's leading alternation (the offer block only consults pendingOffer within its 3-minute window, so 'okay' outside an offer still reaches smalltalk).
Expected improvement
Natural one-word consent dispatches the offered skill instead of silently no-oping.
Evidence
const AFFIRM_RE =
  /^(yes|yeah|yep|sure|absolutely|go ahead|do it|let'?s do it|please do|yes please|go for it|sounds good)( please)?,?( helm)?$/;  …  if (/^((ok(ay)?|cool|nice|got it|sounds good|great|perfect|alright|sweet|then|one|man|helm)\s*){1,4}$/.test(t)) {
    return "Standing by.";
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read lib/router.ts lines 170-359. All mechanics check out as described. (1) AFFIRM_RE (lines 185-186) lists yes|yeah|yep|sure|absolutely|go ahead|do it|let's do it|please do|yes please|go for it|sounds good — no ok/okay. (2) isAffirm's stripper (line 194) is /^(?:yes|yeah|yep|sure|ok(?:ay)?)[\s,]+/ which requires trailing whitespace/comma, so bare 'okay' is left unchanged and fails AFFIRM_RE, while 'okay, do it' strips to 'do it' and passes — the asymmetry is real. (3) The offer block (lines 234-246) is only entered when isAffirm||isDecline, so bare 'okay' skips it entirely and reaches smalltalk (called at line 285), whose bare-ack rule at line 328 includes ok(ay)? and returns 'Standing by.' — the identical string the explicit-decline path returns at line 245, so the user gets no signal the consent was dropped. Being tier-2, no model engine sees it. (4) 'yes, run it' strips to 'run it', which matches neither AFFIRM_RE nor (per the code path) any bare-alias dispatch, so it bypasses the offer block and falls through to tier-3 (lines 303-310) — technically tier-3 fallthrough hands it to model engines with convo context, so that half of the finding is slightly less dead-end than the bare-'okay' case, but the routing claim is accurate. Cited lines 185-194 correct; smalltalk ack rule is at line 328 as claimed. Proposed fix is sound; note 'sounds good' appears in both AFFIRM_RE and the smalltalk ack list, and works only because the offer block runs first — adding ok|okay to AFFIRM_RE would resolve the bare-'okay' case the same way without affecting no-offer 'okay' (pendingOffer's 3-minute window gates it). Not a duplicate of any known/excluded item.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read lib/router.ts (AFFIRM_RE lines 185-186, isAffirm 193-195, rulesRoute offer block 234-246, smalltalk bare-ack 328-329, pickEngine 89-115) and scripts/test-router.ts offer-coupling section (lines 315-360). Core claim CONFIRMED: bare "okay"/"ok" fails isAffirm — AFFIRM_RE lacks ok/okay, and the leading-token stripper requires trailing [\s,]+ so a bare "okay" is unchanged. isDecline also fails, so the pendingOffer block at line 234 is skipped entirely, and the utterance matches smalltalk's bare-ack rule (line 328, which explicitly lists ok(ay)?) returning tier-2 "Standing by." — byte-identical to the decline reply, with fallthrough unset, so in auto mode (pickEngine line 108) the model engines never see it. No test covers "okay" after an offer (tests exercise only yes / yes please / yes do it / no variants), so this is a gap, not documented intent. Corrections: (1) the "yes, run it" sub-claim is overstated — that utterance sets fallthrough:true, so in auto mode haiku/local engines DO get a chance to interpret it against convo context before tier-3; only the smalltalk-swallowed acks bypass the engines. (2) how_to_fix lists "sure/sounds good" among the swallowed acks, but both are already in AFFIRM_RE and work; the actually-swallowed set is ok/okay/cool/got it/great/perfect/alright/sweet. (3) Impact is further muted if this machine pins VOICE_ROUTER=local (memory notes an Ollama router), since rulesRoute then only runs as failure fallback — but the auto path is the code default. Severity low is right: natural spoken consent silently dropped within a 3-minute window, self-recoverable by rephrasing. Fix option B (add ok(?:ay)? to AFFIRM_RE's alternation) is safe: the offer block only fires when pendingOffer returns a skill within 3 minutes, so "okay" outside an offer still reaches smalltalk. Note the offer-wording coupling (CLAUDE.md coupling #2) is untouched by that fix.
lowConfirmed backend effort: trivial

inFlightGuard strips the first alias that matches the transcript, not the alias of the guarded skill

lib/router.ts:152-160 · reviewer: bugs-router
What it is
When rerouting a tier-1 result for an in-flight skill, the residue computation removes 'the alias' from the transcript via SKILL_ALIASES.find(([re]) => re.test(t)) — the first alias regex matching the transcript in list order, with no reference to r.skill. If the sentence mentions two skills ('once the morning report is done, run the morphy sync' while morphy-sync is in flight), the guard strips 'morning report' (list position 0) instead of the morphy-sync alias, so the residue still contains the guarded skill's own name and the word count is inflated. For a model-engine tier-1 result whose transcript used phrasing not in SKILL_ALIASES at all, alias is undefined and nothing is stripped, also inflating residue.
Why it matters
Residue length is the discriminator between 'bare re-dispatch → already running' (tier 2) and 'real ask riding along → background voice-ask' (tier 3). Miscounting pushes borderline bare re-dispatches into tier 3, spawning an unnecessary headless claude session whose prompt is essentially the skill name.
How to fix
Select the alias whose skill matches: SKILL_ALIASES.find(([re, s]) => s === r.skill && re.test(t))?.[0], falling back to a regex built from r.skill.replace(/-/g, '[ -]?') so model-engine phrasings ('morphy sync') are also stripped.
Expected improvement
Residue reflects only the genuine extra ask, so bare repeats get the cheap 'already running' reply instead of a background run.
Evidence
const alias = SKILL_ALIASES.find(([re]) => re.test(t))?.[0];
  const residue = t
    .replace(alias ?? /$^/, " ")
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Confirmed in current code. lib/router.ts line 153 reads `const alias = SKILL_ALIASES.find(([re]) => re.test(t))?.[0];` — it selects the FIRST alias regex matching the transcript in list order, with no reference to r.skill (the guarded in-flight skill). SKILL_ALIASES (lines 59-66) lists morning-report first, so a two-skill sentence like the finding's example strips the wrong alias, leaving the guarded skill's own name ('morphy sync') in the residue and inflating the word count toward the >=3 tier-3 threshold (line 161). The second claim also holds: for a model-engine (haiku/local) tier-1 result whose phrasing matches no alias (e.g. 'update the morphy board' → morphy-sync), alias is undefined and `.replace(alias ?? /$^/, " ")` (line 155) strips nothing — RESIDUE_FILLER (line 138) removes some verbs ('run', 'refresh', 'brief', 'report') but not the skill's content words ('morphy', 'sync', 'board'), so a bare re-dispatch can miscount as a real ask and escalate to tier 3 (an unnecessary background voice-ask). Impact is partially mitigated: the tier-3 path only produces a wasted headless run, and skill names in transcripts overlap RESIDUE_FILLER for some skills ('inbox brief' → 'brief' is filler, 'inbox' remains 1 word). Cited line range 152-160 is accurate (the flawed find is at 153); evidence snippet matches the file verbatim. Suggested fix (match alias by skill, fall back to a name-derived regex) is sound. Severity low is appropriate — behavior degradation, no security or data impact. Not covered by the ADRs' intentional designs (the guard itself is not contract-tested for this case) and not in the known/excluded list.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Confirmed in current lib/router.ts:153 — the alias lookup ignores r.skill and takes the first SKILL_ALIASES regex matching the transcript; evidence snippet matches current code. One correction: the finding's headline example ("once the morning report is done, run the morphy sync") does NOT actually flip the tier — buggy residue is ["morphy","sync"] (2 words) vs correct ["morning"] (1 word), both below the >=3 threshold, so both yield tier 2. The inflation is real but only wordier two-skill sentences cross the line. The second claim (alias undefined for model-engine phrasings not in SKILL_ALIASES, e.g. hyphenated "clean-up" which /clean ?up/ misses since alias-matching happens before punctuation stripping) concretely flips a bare re-dispatch to tier 3 (residue 4 words), spawning an unneeded background voice-ask. No mitigation: scripts/test-router.ts covers only the single-skill bare re-ask and the "again" bypass; not covered by ADRs or the excluded/known lists. Proposed fix (find alias by skill match, fall back to a regex from r.skill) is sound. Severity low is appropriate: worst case is one wasted headless claude run in a corner case.
lowConfirmed frontend effort: small

deltaWeek is computed over the 24-point display history, so hourly metrics' "week delta" actually spans at most 24 hours

lib/vault.ts:219-243 · reviewer: bugs-vault-state
What it is
readMetrics() keeps up to HISTORY_CAP*4 = 96 raw points per metric (line 219), slices the last HISTORY_CAP = 24 into `history` (line 225), and then searches for the week-ago anchor INSIDE that 24-point slice: `const weekAgo = history.find((p) => ... t >= weekCutoff)` (lines 230-233). For a daily-bucketed metric (uscf rating, job apps — feeds run 07:00-08:30 ET) 24 points span 24 days and the oldest point within 7 days is found correctly. But claude-tokens writes HOURLY rows (feeds/claude-tokens.py line 131 uses hour_bucket, launchd "hourly :00"), so `history` spans only ~24 hours: every point satisfies `t >= weekCutoff`, weekAgo becomes the 23-hour-old point, and deltaWeek is a one-day delta labeled as weekly. Even searching the full `points` array can't fix it alone — the 96-row retention cap holds only 4 days of hourly data. The mislabeled value reaches the tier-2 LLM context as "week delta N" (lib/router.ts line 808), which the local model can then speak back as a weekly change.
Why it matters
The claude_code usage metrics get a "week delta" fact fed to the router LLM that is really a 24-hour delta — a plausible-sounding wrong number in spoken answers about token usage trends. Any future hourly metric wired to statTileProps would show the same wrong "/wk" trend chip.
How to fix
Search for weekAgo over the full `points` array instead of the truncated `history`, and raise the retention multiplier for the week window to cover 7 days of hourly rows (HISTORY_CAP * 8 = 192 ≥ 168), or track the week anchor during the parse loop instead of retaining rows for it. Alternatively set deltaWeek to null when the retained window is shorter than 7 days so the label stays honest.
Expected improvement
deltaWeek is either a true 7-day delta or null; no mislabeled trend fed to the router prompt or tiles.
Evidence
if (bucket.points.length > HISTORY_CAP * 4) bucket.points.splice(...)
const history = points.slice(-HISTORY_CAP);
const weekAgo = history.find((p) => { ... t >= weekCutoff; });  — feeds/claude-tokens.py: `ts = hour_bucket(datetime.now(timezone.utc))`; router.ts:808: `week delta ${m.deltaWeek}`
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Verified in current code. lib/vault.ts:148 sets HISTORY_CAP = 24; line 219 caps raw retention at HISTORY_CAP*4 = 96 rows per metric; line 225 slices `history = points.slice(-HISTORY_CAP)`; lines 230-233 find `weekAgo` as the first point inside that 24-point slice with timestamp >= now-7d; line 242 sets deltaWeek from it. feeds/claude-tokens.py:131 buckets timestamps hourly (`ts = hour_bucket(...)`) and its own header comment (line ~26) confirms hourly cadence, so for that metric the 24-point history spans ~24h, every point passes the >= weekCutoff test, weekAgo is the ~23-hour-old point, and deltaWeek is a one-day delta. The inline comment at vault.ts:228-229 shows the timestamp-based fix was written for the opposite failure (daily feeds spanning >7d) and never considered sub-daily cadence. Exposure is slightly WIDER than the finding states: besides the tier-2 LLM context at lib/router.ts:808 ("week delta N"), lines 391-394 speak it directly as "up/down about N this week", and lib/vitals.ts:45/79 surfaces deltaWeek to the HUD stat tiles — so the mislabeled "/wk" value is both spoken and displayed. Also true as claimed that searching the full `points` array alone wouldn't fix it: the 96-row cap holds only 4 days of hourly rows. Not covered by the excluded #36-#44 review era (the comment shows that fix shipped but addressed only the daily case). Cited lines are accurate (219, 225, 230-233; claude-tokens.py:131; router.ts:808). Severity low is right — wrong-but-plausible trend number on a personal dashboard, no correctness/security impact beyond that.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Confirmed by reading lib/vault.ts:148 (HISTORY_CAP = 24), 219 (retention cap HISTORY_CAP*4 = 96 rows), 225-242 (history = last 24 points; weekAgo = first point in that slice with t >= weekCutoff), feeds/claude-tokens.py:131 (ts = hour_bucket(...), and .helm-config.json confirms "hourly :00 (com.helm.tokens)" for claude_code pct_5h/pct_7d/pct_7d_fable), and lib/router.ts:391-394 + 808 (deltaWeek spoken as "up/down about N this week" and fed to the tier-2 LLM as "week delta N" for ALL metrics in stateSummary). Mechanics are exactly as described: for an hourly metric the 24-point history spans ~24h, every point passes the weekCutoff test, weekAgo is the ~23h-old point, and deltaWeek is a one-day delta labeled weekly. The code comment at vault.ts:228-229 shows the timestamp-based search was added to fix the daily-feed case; the hourly case is the unhandled inverse, so this is a residual bug, not intentional design, and it is not covered by the known/excluded lists. Two scope corrections: (1) the HUD "/wk" trend chip impact is currently hypothetical — statTileProps callers (app/chess, app/jobs, app/morphy) all use daily-bucketed metrics; no hourly metric is wired to a stat tile today, so the live impact is only the router path (LLM context line 808 and the spoken weekDelta helper). (2) For pct_5h/pct_7d these values are rolling utilization percentages that fluctuate, so a "week delta" is of marginal informational value even when computed correctly — which supports keeping severity at low, not raising it. The finding's proposed fixes are sound; the "deltaWeek = null when retained window < 7 days" option is the cheapest honest fix given the 96-row cap only holds 4 days of hourly data.
lowConfirmed runner effort: trivial

processOne 'exit'+drain finalize leaves stdout/stderr listeners attached — late output is appended after the run .md's closing fence and never reaches the spoken summary

runner/runner.js:681-699, 756-761, 781-783 · reviewer: bugs-runner
What it is
When a grandchild inherits the stdio pipes and holds 'close' open, the 'exit' handler finalizes the run after a 5s drain window. finalize computes the summary from `out` and rewrites the run .md with the closing ``` fence and footer — but the `proc.stdout.on("data")` / `proc.stderr.on("data")` handlers are never removed. Any output flushed after the drain window keeps `appendFileSync(runMdPath, chunk)`-ing BELOW the already-written footer (garbling the note) and pushes into `out` after `summaryFromOutput` already ran, so a slow-flushing run can get a "(no output)" or truncated spoken summary while its real first line lands only in the corrupted .md tail.
Why it matters
The run .md is pitched as a self-consistent vault record (frontmatter status + footer), and the first stdout line is the TTS contract; both are quietly wrong in exactly the hang scenarios the exit+drain path was added to handle.
How to fix
In finalize, before writing the footer, detach the handlers: `proc.stdout.removeAllListeners("data"); proc.stderr.removeAllListeners("data");` (or gate the handlers on the existing `settled` flag).
Expected improvement
Run .md files stay well-formed and the spoken summary reflects what actually streamed, even when a grandchild holds the pipes open past the drain window.
Evidence
`proc.on("exit", (code) => { drainTimer = setTimeout(() => finalize(code), 5000); });` while `proc.stdout.on("data", (chunk) => { … out.push(chunk.toString()); appendFileSync(runMdPath, chunk); … })` is never removed and finalize writes `finalizeRunMd(md, …) + "\n\`\`\`\n\n---\n*exit code=…*"`
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read runner/runner.js lines 620-830. Confirmed in current code: proc.stdout.on("data") (lines 682-690) and proc.stderr.on("data") (693-700) both appendFileSync(runMdPath, chunk) and (stdout only) push into `out`; they are never removed. finalize (729-775) sets `settled` but only guards re-entry of finalize itself — the data handlers do not check it. The 'exit' path (781-783) fires finalize via a 5s drainTimer precisely in the grandchild-holds-pipes scenario; finalize computes summaryFromOutput(out.join("")) at 747 and rewrites the .md with closing fence + footer at 754-761. Any chunk flushed after finalize is appended below the footer and lands in `out` too late for the summary — exactly as claimed. Also note the same corruption applies via the 'error' handler path, and the hard-timeout out.push at 705 has the same post-footer race, but the exit+drain path is the main one. Minor line correction: handlers are 682-700 (finding said 681-699); footer write is 754-761 (finding said 756-761) — immaterial. Proposed fix (removeAllListeners or gating handlers on `settled`) is correct; gating on `settled` is the cleaner option since it also covers the error path. Not covered by the known/excluded list (exit+drain finalize is current code, not a pre-publication-era finding). Impact limited to slow-flushing/hang scenarios of an already-degraded run — severity low is right.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Confirmed in runner/runner.js (read lines 650-800). stdout/stderr 'data' handlers (682-700) append to the run .md and push into `out`; they are never detached. The 'exit' handler (781-783) schedules finalize after a 5s drain precisely for the grandchild-holds-pipes case, so the pipes are live when finalize (729-775) computes summaryFromOutput(out.join("")) at 747 and rewrites the .md with closing fence + footer at 755-761. Late flushes then append below the footer and arrive after the summary snapshot; the later 'close' hits the `settled` guard with no cleanup. No mitigation found: no second .md rewrite, timeout/stall paths killTree but the drain path targets a surviving grandchild, no test covers post-finalize output, and it duplicates none of the excluded items. Proposed fix is correct; gating the handlers on `settled` is slightly cleaner than removeAllListeners. Corrections: handlers start at line 682 (finding says 681); "(no output)" only occurs if all output lands post-drain — truncated summary is the likelier symptom. Severity low is right: needs a rare pipe-inheriting grandchild flushing >5s after exit, damage is one corrupted run note + degraded spoken summary.

runOutcome's deliverable-missing guard is vacuous for plan-today/plan-tomorrow because the daily note usually pre-exists (MERGE contract)

runner/runner.js:434-439, 287 · reviewer: bugs-runner
What it is
runOutcome flags `exit 0` as error when the deliverable is absent: `if (code === 0 && deliverable && !existsSync(join(VAULT_ROOT, deliverable)))`. But the plan-today prompt explicitly says 'If the note already exists, MERGE', and plan-tomorrow creates tomorrow's note in advance — so daily-notes/<date>.md typically exists BEFORE the run starts. A claude session that exits 0 having written nothing (permission hiccup, model declined) still passes the existsSync check and is recorded status:ok with a success banner, because the check only proves the file exists, not that this run touched it.
Why it matters
The guard's own comment says 'the promised deliverable has to actually be on disk, or the success banner points at a 404' — for the two SERIAL skills that share the daily note, the stronger failure (banner points at an unchanged note) is undetected, and the voice layer announces a plan that was never written.
How to fix
Capture statSync(deliverablePath).mtimeMs (or absence) before spawning and treat exit 0 with an unchanged mtime as the `missing` outcome for skills whose deliverable can pre-exist.
Expected improvement
A no-op plan-today run surfaces as an error run record instead of a false success notification.
Evidence
`if (code === 0 && deliverable && !existsSync(join(VAULT_ROOT, deliverable))) { return { status: "error", missing: true }; }` vs the plan-today prompt: 'If the note already exists, MERGE: fill only empty Top 3 slots'
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Verified against current runner/runner.js. runOutcome (lines 434-439) is exactly as quoted: `if (code === 0 && deliverable && !existsSync(join(VAULT_ROOT, deliverable))) return { status: "error", missing: true }` — a pure existence check, no mtime/content comparison. deliverablePathFor (lines 240-263) gives plan-today `daily-notes/${date}.md` and plan-tomorrow `daily-notes/${tomorrowDate()}.md` — date-keyed with NO per-run id suffix, unlike every other skill which embeds id8 (making those paths run-unique, so the guard is meaningful for them). The plan-today prompt at line 287 does say "If the note already exists, MERGE: fill only empty Top 3 slots", explicitly anticipating a pre-existing deliverable (e.g. created the prior evening by plan-tomorrow), and SERIAL_SKILLS (line 332) confirms these two are the note-sharing pair. So for plan-today/plan-tomorrow, an exit-0 run that wrote nothing still passes the existsSync check and is recorded status:ok with the run-complete banner (line 816). Not in the excluded/known list; not covered by any ADR (ADR-0008 covers feeds, not runner skills). Line citations in the finding are accurate; the proposed pre-spawn mtime capture fix is sound. Minor caveat: an mtime-based fix could false-positive on a legitimate no-op MERGE (note already fully filled), but that's a fix-design nuance, not an existence issue. Severity low is right — failure mode requires claude to exit 0 without writing, and the impact is a stale-plan announcement, not data loss.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Verified in runner/runner.js. runOutcome (lines 434-439) only checks existsSync on the deliverable. deliverablePathFor (240-263) gives every other skill a per-run id8-suffixed path, so the guard is real for them; only plan-today (daily-notes/<today>.md) and plan-tomorrow (daily-notes/<tomorrow>.md) use stable date-only paths that can pre-exist. plan-tomorrow pre-creates tomorrow's note and the plan-today prompt (line 287) explicitly says MERGE if the note exists, so on normal cadence the file exists before the run — an exit-0 no-op run passes the check, is recorded status:ok (line 743), and fires the run-complete voice banner (816-819). No test or other mitigation covers this; SERIAL_SKILLS only serializes the runs. Line references in the finding are correct. Severity low is right: it only triggers when claude exits 0 without writing (rare), and the harm is a false success record plus stale note, not corruption. Correction to the proposed fix: unchanged-mtime would false-positive a legitimate MERGE that finds nothing to change; better to treat unchanged mtime as a distinct no-write outcome or verify the "SAVED <path>" trailer in the child's output instead of reusing the missing outcome.

Pidfile singleton check is a TOCTOU race — two runners booting concurrently both pass the check and both run

runner/runner.js:1262-1278 · reviewer: bugs-runner
What it is
main() does existsSync(PIDFILE) → read → pidAlive → pidLooksLikeRunner, then unconditionally `writeFileSync(PIDFILE, String(process.pid))`. Two runners started near-simultaneously (e.g. `launchctl kickstart -k com.helm.runner` racing a manual `node runner/runner.js`) can both pass the liveness probe before either writes the pidfile, and both proceed to run. Intent execution stays safe (the atomic `renameSync` claim in processOne means only one wins each file), but both daemons then run duplicate morphySync/agendaSync intervals, duplicate fleet passes (double launchctl kicks for the same staleness episode, since each keeps its own in-memory view and both read the same prev fleet-health.json in the same window), and fight over runner-status.json / runner.log.
Why it matters
The one-kick-per-episode watchdog contract and the heartbeat's pid/busy fields silently stop being trustworthy while two runners coexist; the loser's exit later deletes nothing (the pid-matching exit handler guards that correctly) so the state self-heals only when one process is manually killed.
How to fix
Acquire the lock atomically: `openSync(PIDFILE, "wx")` and on EEXIST run the existing stale-pid probe, unlink, and retry once — collapsing check and claim into one syscall.
Expected improvement
At most one live runner regardless of how boots race; heartbeat and fleet kick accounting stay single-writer.
Evidence
`if (existsSync(PIDFILE)) { … pidAlive(otherPid) && pidLooksLikeRunner(otherPid) … } writeFileSync(PIDFILE, String(process.pid), "utf8");` — no atomic create-exclusive between check and write
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read runner/runner.js lines 1230-1335. Confirmed: main() does existsSync(PIDFILE) at 1262, reads/probes the other pid (pidAlive + pidLooksLikeRunner) at 1264-1269, then unconditionally writeFileSync(PIDFILE, String(process.pid)) at 1278 — no openSync(..., "wx") or other atomic create-exclusive, so the check-then-claim TOCTOU race exists as described. Downstream consequences verified: renameSync claim in processOne (line 523) keeps intent execution single-winner; duplicate setInterval loops for morphySync (1305), agendaSync (1311), and fleetCheck (1331) would run in both processes; the pid-matching exit handler (1281-1282) means the loser never cleans up the winner's pidfile, matching the "self-heals only on manual kill" claim. One nuance the finding slightly overstates: the primary launchd path (`launchctl kickstart -k`) kills the existing instance first, so the realistic race is launchd respawn vs. a manual `node runner/runner.js` — narrow window, single-user machine, hence low severity is right. Proposed fix (openSync "wx", on EEXIST run stale-probe + unlink + retry once) is correct and minimal. Not a duplicate of the excluded #36-#44 review items or open follow-ups.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read runner/runner.js:1230-1310. Confirmed: check (existsSync → read → pidAlive → pidLooksLikeRunner, the last shelling to `ps`, widening the window) and claim (plain writeFileSync, no wx/O_EXCL) are separate; no other lock exists in the repo, and CLAUDE.md documents both launchctl and manual-node start paths, making the concurrent-boot scenario realistic. A second race variant needs no pidfile at all: two boots in the same window both skip the if-block. Impact stated correctly and not overstated — intent execution stays single-winner via the atomic renameSync claim in processOne; the harm is duplicated morphySync/agenda intervals, duplicate fleet kicks, and contended runner-status.json/runner.log. The pid-matching exit handler (lines 1281-1282) is correctly described. Line range 1262-1278 is exact. Proposed fix (openSync "wx", on EEXIST run stale probe + unlink + retry once) is correct and preserves the existing recycled-pid/stale-file recovery. Severity low is right for a personal single-machine daemon.
lowConfirmed frontend effort: trivial

Wake-listener crash mid-capture leaves the HUD stuck in the hands-free 'listening' state

lib/voiceClient.ts:151-157 · reviewer: bugs-voice
What it is
When the wake thread dies (wakeword.py _run's outer `except Exception` at lines 83-89 — e.g. sounddevice stream.read raising after a device change), it emits `{"type": "hello", "wake": False}` so connected HUDs learn hands-free is gone. But if the crash happens during _capture — i.e. after `{"type":"wake"}` already fired and the HUD called `this.listeningCb(true)` — the client's `hello` branch in handleWakeEvent only un-latches `disabled` and logs; it never calls `this.listeningCb(false)`. The only other paths that clear listening are wake_timeout/wake_error/transcript (which the dead thread will never send) and ws.onclose (which never fires — the FastAPI server and its /events socket are still healthy, only the wake thread died). The HUD's listening indicator therefore stays on indefinitely.
Why it matters
The user sees a permanently 'listening' orb that will never deliver a transcript — the exact stuck-listening failure the wake event protocol (wake_timeout/wake_error) exists to prevent — with no recovery short of reloading the tab or restarting the voice server.
How to fix
In handleWakeEvent's `hello` branch, call `this.listeningCb(false)` when `e.wake` is false (or unconditionally — a hello always means no capture is in flight). Alternatively, have wakeword.py's death handler also emit a `wake_error` before the hello.
Expected improvement
A wake-listener crash mid-capture degrades cleanly to push-to-talk instead of freezing the listening indicator.
Evidence
voiceClient.ts: `if (e.type === "hello") { this.disabled = false; this.log(...); }` — no listeningCb call; wakeword.py: `except Exception as e: ... self.emit({"type": "hello", "wake": False})` after `self.emit({"type": "wake", ...}); self._capture(stream, noise)`
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read lib/voiceClient.ts (full file), voice-server/wakeword.py (full file), and grepped server.py's emit/hello wiring. All claims check out exactly as cited. (1) wakeword.py: _run's wake branch emits {"type":"wake"} then calls self._capture(stream, noise) (lines 79-80); if stream.read inside _capture (line 99) raises, the exception propagates to _run's outer except (lines 83-89), which emits only {"type":"hello","wake":False} — no wake_error/wake_timeout. (2) voiceClient.ts handleWakeEvent hello branch (lines 151-157) only sets this.disabled=false and logs; it never calls this.listeningCb(false). (3) The only paths that clear listening are the wake_timeout/wake_error/transcript branches (lines 163-167, dead thread never sends them) and ws.onclose (line 130-134) — and server.py confirms the wake thread is a daemon thread inside the FastAPI server (WakeListener constructed with emit_event; /events socket lives on the uvicorn loop), so the socket stays open when only the thread dies and onclose never fires. So the HUD's listening indicator stays latched on until tab reload or server restart. Line/file cites are accurate. Minor addendum, not a correction: the same hello also logs "voice link up — push-to-talk" mid-session, a second small consequence. Severity low is right — wake word is opt-in (no model ships; WAKE_MODEL + WAKE_WORD=on required per ADR-10 intentional PTT default) and the trigger is a rare mid-capture device failure. Both proposed fixes are sound; calling listeningCb(false) unconditionally in the hello branch is the simpler one (a hello always means no capture is in flight, including the reconnect hello at ws open in server.py line 156).
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read lib/voiceClient.ts (lines 100-230), voice-server/wakeword.py (whole file), voice-server/server.py (event plumbing), and components/shell/Shell.tsx consumers. Every link in the chain checks out: (1) wakeword.py _capture's stream.read at line 99 is NOT inside a try/except (only transcribe_pcm at 120-124 is, and that path emits wake_error) — so a mic/device exception mid-capture propagates to _run's outer except at lines 83-89, which emits only {"type":"hello","wake":False}. (2) voiceClient.ts handleWakeEvent's hello branch (lines 151-157) only clears `disabled` and logs; it never calls listeningCb(false). (3) The only clearing paths are wake_timeout/wake_error/transcript (163-167, never sent by the dead thread) and ws.onclose (130-138), which won't fire because only the daemon thread died — the FastAPI /events socket stays healthy. (4) Shell.tsx line 259 wires onListening to setWakeListening and line 415 ORs it into the orb/chip state with no timeout, so the listening indicator sticks until tab reload or server restart. Refutation attempts failed: no watchdog, no timeout on the client, no test covering this path. Proposed fix is correct and safe — the connect-time hello (server.py:156) is per-connection, and a reconnecting client already cleared listening via onclose, so calling listeningCb(false) unconditionally in the hello branch cannot wrongly clear an in-flight capture. Mitigating context that justifies keeping severity low: wake word is opt-in (no model ships; WAKE_MODEL unset by default and this instance is push-to-talk per CLAUDE.md), and the vulnerable window is only the ≤8s _capture span (MAX_UTTERANCE_S) — a crash in the outer loop's stream.read (line 72) happens before any wake fired and leaves no stuck state. Line references in the finding are accurate.
lowConfirmed frontend effort: small

Concurrent getUserMedia during the first PTT press orphans a live mic stream that is never stopped

lib/voiceClient.ts:322-330 · reviewer: bugs-voice
What it is
startCapture() calls getUserMedia only when `!this.micStream`. On the very first capture the browser permission prompt keeps that promise pending for seconds; if the user releases Space and presses it again (natural while a dialog steals focus), finishCapture bumps captureGen (cancelling capture A) and the second startCapture — seeing micStream still null — issues a second parallel getUserMedia. When the user approves, both resolve with distinct live streams: A's assigns `this.micStream = streamA`, then fails the `gen !== this.captureGen` check and returns; B's then overwrites `this.micStream` with streamB. streamA's tracks are never stopped anywhere (nothing in the class ever calls track.stop()), so an orphaned, actively-capturing MediaStream persists for the life of the page.
Why it matters
A duplicate hot microphone capture leaks OS/browser mic resources permanently. The class deliberately keeps ONE stream alive between captures (documented at lines 316-317), but this path leaves a second unreferenced one recording with no way to release it.
How to fix
After the `await navigator.mediaDevices.getUserMedia(...)` resolves, check whether `this.micStream` was set meanwhile (or whether `gen !== this.captureGen`) and if so stop the just-acquired stream's tracks before discarding it; or memoize the pending getUserMedia promise so concurrent startCapture calls share one acquisition.
Expected improvement
Exactly one mic stream ever exists; a double-press during the permission prompt no longer leaks a second live capture.
Evidence
if (!this.micStream) { this.micStream = await navigator.mediaDevices.getUserMedia({ audio: true }); ... } ... if (gen !== this.captureGen) return false;
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read lib/voiceClient.ts:280-399 and grepped file + repo for micStream/track.stop. Confirmed: startCapture (line 322-330) issues getUserMedia only when micStream is null; finishCapture with no recorder (line 384) or cancelCapture (line 369) bumps captureGen while the first getUserMedia is pending at the permission prompt; a second press then issues a parallel getUserMedia (micStream still null). Call A resolves first, assigns this.micStream=streamA, fails the gen!==captureGen check (line 333) and returns; call B then overwrites micStream with streamB. No track.stop() exists anywhere in the class (only getTracks at line 324 to install onended handlers, which merely null cached fields), and no other file references micStream — streamA's live tracks are never stopped, leaking a hot mic capture until page unload. The line-318 !active cache check does not mitigate this. Cited lines and evidence match current code exactly. Minor addition: streamA's installed onended handlers would also incorrectly null the cache fields belonging to streamB if streamA's tracks ever end. Suggested fix in the finding (stop just-acquired tracks when superseded, or memoize the pending getUserMedia promise) is correct. Severity low is appropriate: needs the first-permission-prompt race window and costs one duplicate capture per occurrence.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Confirmed against current lib/voiceClient.ts. Lines 322-330 as cited: getUserMedia guarded only by !this.micStream, assignment happens before the gen check at line 333. finishCapture (line 384) and cancelCapture (line 369) bump captureGen while getUserMedia is pending, and a re-press issues a second parallel getUserMedia since micStream is still null. Grepped the whole file: no MediaStream track is ever stopped anywhere (only MediaRecorder.stop and TTS stop), and onended/!active handlers merely null references, so the losing stream of the micStream overwrite race leaks with live tracks until page reload. One correction/addition: in the ordering where call A resolves LAST, the leak also leaves this.micStream pointing at streamA while the recorder and analyser are wired to streamB, desyncing the stream cache from the audio graph — slightly broader impact than described, but still low severity (first-permission-prompt race only, single-user tool, cleared by reload). Proposed fix is sound; memoizing the pending getUserMedia promise is the cleaner variant.
lowConfirmed backend effort: trivial

normalizeForSpeech misreads lowercase money suffixes: "$5m" is spoken as "five dollars"

lib/spokenText.ts:57-68 · reviewer: bugs-voice
What it is
The money-suffix rule accepts `k|K` but for millions/billions/trillions only the full word or the UPPERCASE single letter: `(k|K|[mM]illion|[bB]illion|[tT]rillion|M|B|T)`. "$5m", "$2b", "$1.5t" — common in mined headlines, which this module's header names as a source — fail that rule and fall through to the plain-dollar rule `\$\s?(\d{1,3}(?:,\d{3})+|\d+)(?:\.\d+)?(?!\d)`, which matches the digits, leaves the trailing letter, and produces "five dollars m" — spoken as five dollars, off by six orders of magnitude. The bare-count rule at line 71 has the same uppercase-only gap (`([MBT])\b`), so "5m subscribers" also passes through unexpanded, though that case is more forgivable since lowercase m could mean meters; after a $ sign the meaning is unambiguous.
Why it matters
The whole point of this module (per its own header) is that Kokoro must not mangle money figures from "router replies, mined headlines, run summaries"; a headline like "raises $5m" being voiced as "five dollars" is a factual misstatement, worse than the mispronunciation it was built to fix.
How to fix
Add lowercase single-letter forms to the suffix alternation for the $-prefixed rule (e.g. `k|m|b|t` case-insensitively via [kK]|[mM](?:illion)?|[bB](?:illion)?|[tT](?:rillion)?), keeping the bare-count rule uppercase-only if lowercase ambiguity is a concern there.
Expected improvement
"$5m" reads "five million dollars" instead of "five dollars" followed by a stray letter.
Evidence
t = t.replace(/\$\s?(\d+(?:\.\d+)?)\s?(k|K|[mM]illion|[bB]illion|[tT]rillion|M|B|T)\b/g, ...)
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read lib/spokenText.ts in full. Line 57 regex is exactly as quoted: suffix alternation is (k|K|[mM]illion|[bB]illion|[tT]rillion|M|B|T) — lowercase bare m/b/t do not match ([mM]illion requires 'illion'). "$5m" therefore falls to the plain-dollar rule at line 65, which consumes "$5" and emits "five dollars", stranding the "m"; the bare-count rule at line 71 is uppercase-only ([MBT]) so nothing rescues it. Rule order 57→65→71 confirms the failure path. Cited lines and evidence are exact. Module header (lines 2-5) names mined headlines as a source, so "$5m" inputs are in-scope. Not covered by any ADR or excluded item. Proposed fix is sound; only nit: keep a word-boundary/lookahead after the lowercase single letter so "$5min" doesn't become "five million dollars in". Severity low is appropriate (wrong spoken magnitude only, screen unaffected).
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Confirmed by reading lib/spokenText.ts (lines 57-73) and executing normalizeForSpeech via tsx. Actual outputs are even slightly worse than described: "raises $5m in seed" -> "raises five dollarsm in seed" (no space — the plain-dollar rule replaces "$5" and the "m" concatenates), "a $2b deal" -> "a two dollarsb deal", "$1.5t market" -> "one dollart market" (the decimal is consumed and cents dropped, so $1.5 trillion is voiced as "one dollar t" — off by 12 orders of magnitude). Uppercase "$5M" works ("five million dollars"), and bare "5m subscribers" indeed passes through unexpanded as the finding says. No mitigation exists: the only test coverage is scripts/test-capture.ts lines 61-68 (from the prior review-#40 fix), which tests only uppercase "$200M" and comma/decimal plain amounts — no lowercase-suffix case; nothing upstream normalizes case before TTS (lib/tts.ts calls normalizeForSpeech directly). This is not a duplicate of the shipped review-#40 finding (that fix was about comma-less amounts/partial matches; its test explicitly asserts suffix amounts "untouched by the fix" but only for uppercase). Proposed fix is sound; keeping the bare-count rule at line 71 uppercase-only is a reasonable ambiguity call (lowercase m = meters/minutes). Severity low is right: voice-only factual misstatement, screen text stays correct, and it depends on lowercase suffixes appearing in mined headlines — plausible but not guaranteed frequent.
lowConfirmed frontend effort: trivial

calendar-agenda.py: overnight events that started yesterday render as late-today events with the wrong-day start time

feeds/calendar-agenda.py:108-122 · reviewer: bugs-feeds
What it is
day_bounds() asks the Calendar API for events overlapping [today 00:00, tomorrow 00:00) local, and events.list returns any event that intersects that window — including a timed event that started yesterday and spills past midnight (e.g. Fri 23:00–Sat 01:00). to_events() renders only _hhmm(start['dateTime']) with no date component and sorts timed events by that HH:MM string (line 122: `(1, e["time"])`), so on Saturday that event appears as time '23:00' at the very bottom of Saturday's agenda — reading as an upcoming late-night event even though it ended at 01:00 that morning. Nothing distinguishes it from a genuine 23:00 event today.
Why it matters
Silent wrong data on the agenda tile: the morning briefing and planner consume this list and would treat an already-finished overnight event as tonight's last item. It's exactly the 'silent wrong number beats a crash' class the feed's own docstring guards against elsewhere.
How to fix
In to_events (or a wrapper taking date_str), compare the start's local date to the agenda date: for events that began before today, either skip them or render a marker like time '00:00' / item prefix '(cont.)' so they sort first and read as carry-overs rather than late-night entries.
Expected improvement
Overnight/carry-over events can no longer masquerade as future late-evening events on the day tile.
Evidence
t = _hhmm(start["dateTime"], zone)
...
out.sort(key=lambda e: (0, "") if e["allDay"] else (1, e["time"]))
Verifier notes (2)

  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read all of feeds/calendar-agenda.py and grepped feeds/test_calendar_agenda.py for any overnight/midnight/carry-over handling. _metrics.py: row_exists check then append is not atomic — concurrent runs of the same feed can write duplicate rows

feeds/_metrics.py:75-79 · reviewer: bugs-feeds
What it is
append_metric_row() guards the frozen 'a (source, metric, timestamp) row is written at most once' contract with a read-then-append: row_exists() scans the file, and only then the row is appended in a separate open('a'). Two concurrent invocations of the same feed for the same bucket — e.g. a `launchctl kickstart` racing the scheduled launchd fire, or a manual `python3 feeds/uscf-rating.py` while the agent runs — can both see row_exists()==False and both append, producing a duplicate (source, metric, ts) row. The file-creation race one line above was explicitly hardened with open('x') per review 59, but the append-side TOCTOU was not. The docstring's at-most-once contract is therefore only best-effort.
Why it matters
Duplicate rows violate the module's own frozen contract and skew whatever the metrics reader does with the series (the sparkline's last-24-points cap means a duplicated day displaces a real one). It is rare (needs same-bucket concurrency) but silent when it happens.
How to fix
Hold an exclusive lock across the check+append — e.g. fcntl.flock(fh, LOCK_EX) on the opened append handle before calling row_exists, or open with 'a+' and do the scan and write under one flock. macOS-only deployment makes flock safe here.
Expected improvement
The at-most-once-per-bucket contract holds even under concurrent manual + scheduled runs.
Evidence
if row_exists(csv_path, ts, source, metric):
        return False
    with csv_path.open("a") as fh:
        fh.write(f"{ts},{source},{metric},{value},{status},\n")
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read feeds/_metrics.py in full (79 lines). The cited code is exactly as quoted at lines 75-79: append_metric_row() calls row_exists() (a full read/scan, lines 49-58) and then appends in a separate csv_path.open("a") with no lock spanning the check and the write. The header-creation race one line above (lines 70-74) was indeed hardened with open(csv_path, "x") citing "review 59", while the check-then-append TOCTOU was not — so this is not a duplicate of the already-shipped review-fix era; the current code still has it. Two same-bucket concurrent invocations (e.g. manual `python3 feeds/<feed>.py` racing the launchd fire — launchd serializes runs of the same label, so the realistic race is manual-vs-agent, a minor overstatement in the finding's kickstart example) can both see row_exists()==False and both append, producing duplicate (source, metric, ts) rows, violating the module docstring's "written at most once" contract (lines 10-13). The suggested fcntl.flock fix is sound for the macOS-only deployment. Severity low is right: the window is milliseconds, requires same-bucket concurrency, and the consequence is a duplicate sparkline point, not data loss.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read feeds/_metrics.py (lines 61-79), all four callers (feeds/uscf-rating.py, morphy-github.py, job-applications.py, claude-tokens.py), and the reader lib/vault.ts readMetrics() (lines 200-246). The TOCTOU is real exactly as described at lines 75-79: row_exists() reads the whole file, then the append happens in a separate open('a') with no lock; nothing elsewhere serializes it — no flock in the module, no lockfile in the callers, and the feeds are independent processes launched by separate launchd agents. The file-creation race one line above was indeed hardened with open('x') (comment cites review 59) while the check+append was not, so the docstring's 'at most once' contract is best-effort only. Impact claim also verified: readMetrics() in lib/vault.ts does NOT dedupe by timestamp — every parsed row is pushed into points, and history = points.slice(-HISTORY_CAP), so a duplicate row occupies a sparkline slot and displaces a real point, and makes the point-over-point delta read 0. Materiality caveats keeping this at low: launchd will not run two instances of the same label concurrently, so the race requires a manual `python3 feeds/<feed>.py` (or launchctl kickstart -k) overlapping the scheduled fire in the same hour/day bucket AND both interleaving in the microseconds between scan and append — rare, and the consequence is one cosmetic duplicate sparkline point with identical value, not data corruption (values in the same bucket are the same fetch, or at worst two nearby fetches). The proposed flock fix is correct and safe for this deployment (local APFS, writes only ever happen on the Mac; Syncthing peers don't write metrics.csv). Severity 'low' as filed is right — do not raise it.
lowConfirmed deploy effort: small

install-launchd.sh sed substitution breaks silently when $ROOT or $HOME contains sed-special characters

scripts/install-launchd.sh:15 · reviewer: deploy-infra
What it is
Template rendering uses `sed -e "s|__HELM_ROOT__|$ROOT|g" -e "s|__HOME__|$HOME|g"` with the paths interpolated raw into the sed program. A checkout path containing `|` breaks the expression outright, and one containing `&` (e.g. `~/Projects/R&D/helm`) expands to the matched placeholder text, producing plists whose ProgramArguments point at garbage paths like `.../com.helm.hudRoot__/...`. The corrupted plists are then bootstrapped without any validation, so the agents fail to spawn with no error from the installer.
Why it matters
`&` in directory names is common enough on personal Macs, and the failure mode is the worst kind: `installed com.helm.hud` prints success while every agent is broken. For a public repo, other users' clone locations are uncontrolled.
How to fix
Escape the replacement (`ROOT_ESC=$(printf '%s' "$ROOT" | sed 's/[&|\\]/\\&/g')`) before substituting, or drop sed for parameter expansion in a shell loop / `plutil`-based rendering; also consider validating each rendered plist with `plutil -lint "$out"` before bootstrapping.
Expected improvement
Template rendering is correct for any checkout path, and invalid renders fail loudly at install time.
Evidence
Line 15: `sed -e "s|__HELM_ROOT__|$ROOT|g" -e "s|__HOME__|$HOME|g" "$tpl" > "$out"`.
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read scripts/install-launchd.sh in full (19 lines). Line 15 is verbatim as cited: `sed -e "s|__HELM_ROOT__|$ROOT|g" -e "s|__HOME__|$HOME|g" "$tpl" > "$out"` with no escaping of $ROOT or $HOME anywhere in the script. Classic sed-replacement injection: `|` in the path terminates the s-command (sed errors out, and with `set -e` on line 6 the script dies mid-loop); `&` in the path (e.g. a "R&D" directory) expands to the matched placeholder text, yielding valid-XML plists with garbage paths; `\` also misbehaves. The rendered plist is bootstrapped (line 17) with no `plutil -lint` or path-existence validation, and `echo "installed $label"` prints success — launchctl bootstrap accepts a syntactically valid plist whose Program path is bogus, so the agents fail only at spawn time with no installer error. Two corrections to the finding text: (1) the `|` case is not fully "silent" — sed exits nonzero and set -e aborts the script, so only the `&`/`\` cases are truly silent-success; (2) the example garbage path "com.helm.hudRoot__" is illustrative rather than exact (a path like /x/R&D/helm renders as /x/R__HELM_ROOT__D/helm), but the mechanism is correct. Not covered by any KNOWN/EXCLUDED item or ADR. Severity low is right: only triggers on clone paths containing sed-special chars, single-user tool, but repo is public so clone locations are uncontrolled. Suggested fix (escape replacement or use shell parameter expansion, plus plutil -lint) is sound.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read scripts/install-launchd.sh in full (19 lines). Line 15 is exactly as quoted; $ROOT (line 7, checkout-derived) and $HOME are interpolated raw into the sed program with no escaping and no post-render validation (no plutil -lint), and the script is the canonical documented installer per CLAUDE.md. The '&' scenario is confirmed and truly silent: sed expands '&' to the matched placeholder, producing a valid plist with a garbage path; launchctl bootstrap succeeds and the script prints 'installed <label>'. Correction: the '|' scenario is NOT silent — sed errors and 'set -e' (line 6) aborts the script loudly, so only the '&' case matches the 'prints success while broken' claim. Fix refinement: sed-escaping '&' alone still yields invalid plist XML (literal & needs &amp;), so the suggested 'plutil -lint "$out"' before bootstrap is the essential part of the fix, not just the escaping. Not a duplicate of any excluded item. Severity low is appropriate: one-time setup script, owner's path unaffected, but repo is public and clone paths are uncontrolled.
lowConfirmed deploy effort: trivial

smoke-fly.sh parses HELM_API_KEY from ~/.claude/.env without stripping quotes, unlike helm-watchdog.sh

scripts/smoke-fly.sh:16 · reviewer: deploy-infra
What it is
smoke-fly.sh extracts the key with `sed -n 's/^HELM_API_KEY=//p' "$HOME/.claude/.env" | tail -1` and sends the raw result as X-HELM-KEY. helm-watchdog.sh, reading VAULT_ROOT from the same file, additionally pipes through `tr -d '"'` because the repo's own tooling anticipates quoted values in that .env. If HELM_API_KEY is ever written quoted (`HELM_API_KEY="abc"` — the natural dotenv style), the smoke test sends `"abc"` including quote characters, the real chat turn gets 401, and the post-deploy smoke reports FAIL against a perfectly healthy deployment.
Why it matters
A false-negative smoke test after `fly deploy` sends the operator debugging a healthy VM. Two scripts in the same directory parsing the same file with different rules is exactly the kind of drift that costs an evening.
How to fix
Match the watchdog's parsing: `HELM_API_KEY=$(sed -n 's/^HELM_API_KEY=//p' "$HOME/.claude/.env" | tail -1 | tr -d '"')` — or better, factor a tiny shared read-env helper both scripts source.
Expected improvement
Smoke results reflect the deployment's health regardless of .env quoting style; the two scripts stop disagreeing about the file format.
Evidence
smoke-fly.sh line 16: `HELM_API_KEY=$(sed -n 's/^HELM_API_KEY=//p' "$HOME/.claude/.env" | tail -1)` vs helm-watchdog.sh line 11: `VAULT_ROOT="${VAULT_ROOT:-$(sed -n 's/^VAULT_ROOT=//p' "$HOME/.claude/.env" | tr -d '"' )}"`.
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Verified against current code. scripts/smoke-fly.sh line 16 reads `HELM_API_KEY=$(sed -n 's/^HELM_API_KEY=//p' "$HOME/.claude/.env" | tail -1)` — no quote stripping — and sends it raw as X-HELM-KEY on line 40. scripts/helm-watchdog.sh line 11 parses VAULT_ROOT from the same file WITH `tr -d '"'`, confirming the intra-repo drift. Crucially, the app side (lib/homeEnv.ts line 22) explicitly strips surrounding quotes: `process.env[m[1]] = m[2].replace(/^["']|["']$/g, "")` — so a quoted `HELM_API_KEY="abc"` in ~/.claude/.env is valid and works for the HUD/server, while smoke-fly.sh would send `"abc"` including quotes and the authed /api/chat turn would 401, making the smoke test report FAIL against a healthy deploy. The failure is latent (only triggers if the key is written quoted; the smoke script's comment even claims "same resolution as the app", which is not true), so low severity is right. Not covered by the known/excluded list (issues #36-#44, PR #14, issue #2, or the Fly-secret follow-up). Suggested fix in the finding is correct; note homeEnv also strips single quotes, so an exact match would be `tr -d '"'"'"'` or sed, but `tr -d '"'` matches the watchdog precedent.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read scripts/smoke-fly.sh (line 16 confirmed verbatim: `HELM_API_KEY=$(sed -n 's/^HELM_API_KEY=//p' "$HOME/.claude/.env" | tail -1)` with no quote stripping), scripts/helm-watchdog.sh line 11 (does pipe through `tr -d '"'`), and both canonical .env parsers: lib/homeEnv.ts line 22 and runner/env.js line 20 — both strip surrounding single AND double quotes (`.replace(/^["']|["']$/g, "")`), and runner/env.js's header comment explicitly documents "quotes stripped" as part of the accepted-key rule. So the divergence is real and material: a quoted HELM_API_KEY would be accepted by the app (auth.ts compares the stripped value via homeEnv) but smoke-fly.sh would send it quotes-and-all as X-HELM-KEY → 401 → false FAIL against a healthy deploy. The script's own comment on line 14 ("same resolution as the app: env first, then ~/.claude/.env") makes the parity claim it fails to honor. Not covered by the KNOWN/EXCLUDED items (the Fly follow-up is about moving the key to a Fly secret, not this parsing drift; issue #44's shared parser work covered the JS side, per scripts/test-runner.ts line 257, not this shell script). Corrections: (a) the finding is conditional — the failure only manifests if the .env value is ever quoted; today it presumably is not, since smoke runs pass, hence low is right, not higher; (b) the proposed fix `tr -d '"'` matches the watchdog but is still narrower than the canonical parsers, which also strip single quotes and trim whitespace around `=` — a fuller match would be `tr -d "\"'"` or the suggested shared read-env helper; (c) smoke-fly's sed additionally fails on `HELM_API_KEY = value` (spaces around =), which homeEnv.ts tolerates — same drift family, worth folding into the fix.

Count Both alongside Daniel: `["Daniel", "Both"].includes(t.assignee)` in the tasks path and `(open_by_assignee?.Daniel ?? 0) + (open_by_assignee?.Both ?? 0)` in the fallback; extend the deriveStatus fixture test with a Both-assigned open card. lib/voiceDispatch.ts:95-96, 133-147 · reviewer: bugs-router
What it is
extractModelOverride strips 'use opus'/'use fable' from every transcript before routing, but the override is only applied when the result is tier 3 (args.model on the voice-ask intent). If the stripped ask routes tier 1 ('use opus, run the inbox brief' → writeIntent(result.skill, source) with no model arg) or tier 2, the override is discarded with no acknowledgment — the ack is the ordinary 'On it — inbox brief coming up.' Why it matters
The user hears a normal confirmation and reasonably believes the run will use the requested model; the skill runs on the runner's default instead. How to fix
When override is non-null and result.tier !== 3, either pass override.model through writeIntent args for tier-1 skills (runner already re-validates against its own allowlist), or append a one-clause disclaimer to the reply ('— note, model overrides only apply to open-ended asks').

Dockerfile `COPY . .` bakes gitignored machine-private files (.helm-config.json, fly-deploy.local.md, runner.log) into the Fly image

Dockerfile:10 · reviewer: deploy-infra
What it is
The build stage does `COPY . .` and the runtime stage then copies the whole tree (`COPY --from=build /app ./`). The .dockerignore only excludes node_modules, .next, .git, .env.local, logs, .playwright-mcp, *.png, and the voice venv. It does NOT exclude files that .gitignore deliberately keeps out of the public repo but which exist on disk: `.helm-config.json` (3.8 KB — the record of how this machine is wired: vault path, launchd inventory), `docs/fly-deploy.local.md` (983 B — the real Fly app name, gitignored precisely because it is machine-private), `runner/runner.log` (244 KB of runner output, which can include vault-derived skill content), and `runner/runner.pid`. All of these get shipped into the image layers pushed to Fly's registry on every `fly deploy`.
Why it matters
The repo went through two history rewrites specifically to scrub machine/private identifiers before publication, yet every deploy re-exports the same class of data — plus a large runtime log of what the runner actually did — into Fly's image registry. The whole point of gitignoring these files (private paths, real app name, vault content in logs) is defeated by the build context including them. It also bloats the image and makes builds non-reproducible (image content depends on local runtime state).
How to fix
Extend .dockerignore to cover the gitignored machine-local set: `.helm-config.json`, `docs/fly-deploy.local.md`, `runner/runner.log*`, `runner/runner.pid`, `*.tsbuildinfo`, `docs/audits`, `.cate`. Simplest robust option: mirror .gitignore's entries into .dockerignore (they diverge today — .gitignore has 11 entries .dockerignore lacks).
Expected improvement
Fly image layers no longer contain private machine configuration or runner logs; deploys become reproducible from a clean checkout.
Evidence
Dockerfile: `COPY . .` … `COPY --from=build /app ./`. .dockerignore (entire file): `node_modules / .next / .git / .env.local / logs / .playwright-mcp / *.png / voice-server/.venv / voice-server/**/__pycache__`. On-disk check: `.helm-config.json` (3854 B), `docs/fly-deploy.local.md` (983 B), `runner/runner.log` (244209 B) all present and unignored.
Verifier notes (2)
