job-applications.py writes a false '0 applications' ok-row when the store exists but cannot be read

feeds/job-applications.py:104-107 · reviewer: unswept-feeds
What it is
iter_application_records() catches `except (FileNotFoundError, OSError): return`, i.e. ANY I/O error — permission denied, a transient disk/Syncthing error, an unmounted vault subpath — is treated identically to a missing store. main() then unconditionally writes `jobs,applications,0,ok` and `jobs,applied_7d,0,ok` rows to metrics.csv. The docstring only justifies the missing-file-equals-zero case ('A missing store is treated as zero applications'); a read error on an existing store is a genuinely different condition that gets silently converted into wrong data. Contrast with the two sibling network feeds in this same sweep (uscf-rating.py line 85-87, morphy-github.py line 237-239), which on any fetch failure log to stderr and exit 1 WITHOUT writing a row so 'the tile keeps its last good value'.
Why it matters
This is the silent-bad-data failure mode ADR-0008's typed-fallback contract exists to prevent, and it is doubly undetectable: (1) the per-day idempotency in _metrics.append_metric_row means a later same-day re-run with the store readable again is skipped — the false 0 is locked in for the whole UTC day; (2) fleet.js only checks row FRESHNESS for the `jobs` source (runner/fleet.js line 156-158), so a fresh-but-wrong 0 row keeps the fleet dot green. Daniel's top-directive number (SWE job applications) drops from N to 0 on the HUD with no error signal anywhere.
How to fix
In iter_application_records(), keep `FileNotFoundError -> yield nothing` (the documented configured-empty state) but let other OSError propagate — or return a sentinel — and have main() print the error to stderr and return 1 without writing rows, matching the uscf/morphy contract of 'bail without writing so the tile keeps its last good value'.
Expected improvement
An unreadable store produces a stale-row condition fleet.js can actually detect (red dot after 26h) instead of a fresh, wrong, uncorrectable 0 in the metrics history.
Evidence
except (FileNotFoundError, OSError):
        return
...
total, week = job_stats(iter_application_records(store), now_dt.timestamp())
...
w1 = append_metric_row(csv, ts, SOURCE, METRIC_TOTAL, total)
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Confirmed at feeds/job-applications.py lines 104-107: iter_application_records() does `except (FileNotFoundError, OSError): return` (note FileNotFoundError is a subclass of OSError, so the tuple is effectively `except OSError` — any read error on an existing store, e.g. PermissionError, silently yields zero records). main() (lines 133-142) then unconditionally writes both rows via append_metric_row and returns 0, so a read failure becomes a fresh `jobs,applications,0,ok` row. The module docstring (lines 28-31) only sanctions the missing-file-equals-zero case and explicitly says 'We only bail without writing on a real error' — so this is a violation of the file's own stated contract, not an intentional design. Sibling contrast verified: uscf-rating.py (~line 82-86) and morphy-github.py (~line 233-239) both catch fetch exceptions, print to stderr, and return 1 without writing a row. Per-day idempotency lock-in verified via the docstring (lines 23-26, 'skip the write if a row already exists for that (source, metric, day)') and the w1/w2 skipped-idempotent handling. fleet.js verified: the jobs-feed check (lines ~156-165) only tests row freshness (newestRowTs + age limit), so a fresh false-0 row keeps the check green. Finding's cited line range, evidence, and fix direction (let non-FileNotFoundError OSError propagate or bail with stderr+exit 1, matching the sibling contract) are all correct. Not a duplicate of any excluded/known item, and ADR-0008's typed-fallback intent supports rather than excuses it. Medium severity is right: wrong data on a top-directive tile for a full UTC day, but only under an unusual local I/O failure.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read feeds/job-applications.py in full, feeds/_metrics.py, feeds/uscf-rating.py (main), feeds/morphy-github.py (main), runner/fleet.js lines 130-180, and grepped feeds/test_job_applications.py. All factual claims verified. (1) iter_application_records lines 104-107 catch `(FileNotFoundError, OSError)` — FileNotFoundError is a subclass of OSError, so the tuple is effectively bare OSError; PermissionError, EIO, unmounted-path errors all silently yield zero records, and main() (lines 134-139) then writes `jobs,applications,0,ok` and `jobs,applied_7d,0,ok`. (2) This violates the file's OWN documented contract, not just ADR-0008: the module docstring at lines 29-31 says "We only bail without writing on a real error" and justifies zero only for "A missing store" — so this is a bug against a stated invariant, not intentional design. (3) Sibling contrast confirmed: uscf-rating.py lines 85-87 and morphy-github.py lines 237-239 both log to stderr and return 1 without writing a row on any failure. (4) Lock-in confirmed: _metrics.append_metric_row skips when a (source, metric, day-bucket) row exists, so a later same-day re-run cannot correct the false 0 until the next UTC day. (5) fleet.js line 156-158 checks only newest-row freshness for the jobs source, so the fresh-but-wrong 0 keeps the fleet check green. No test pins the OSError-as-empty behavior (test file has no OSError/PermissionError coverage), and no caller guards against it. Materiality is real but bounded: the failure requires an existing-but-unreadable store (permission/disk/mount error), which is rare on this single-user Mac vault; wrong data is confined to one UTC day per incident and self-heals next day. Medium is the right severity — silent wrong data on the top-directive metric with green fleet status, but low probability of trigger.

/api/todos whole-file read-modify-write can silently drop a concurrent Obsidian/Syncthing edit; "add" has no conflict guard at all

app/api/todos/route.ts:44-62 · reviewer: bugs-vault-state
What it is
Both todo actions read jobs/todos.md, transform the full document in memory, and rewrite the whole file (writeTodosFile → atomicWriteFileSync, lib/todos.ts lines 89-92). toggleTodo's index+text check (lib/todos.ts lines 53-66) only validates the CLIENT's view against the snapshot just read — it does not detect a write landing between readTodosFile() and writeTodosFile(). The add path has no guard of any kind: `writeTodosFile(addTodo(readTodosFile() ?? "# Job TODOs\n", text))`. The file is explicitly dual-mastered ("Obsidian edits and HUD edits act on the same file", lib/todos.ts header) and lives in the Syncthing-synced part of the vault (.stignore only excludes /system/queue and /system/runs), so an Obsidian autosave or a sync delivery from another device that lands inside the read→write window is wholly overwritten by the stale in-memory document. The window is small (the read-transform-write span is synchronous in one Node process), but it exists on every write and the loss is silent — no 409, no log. Side note: toggleTodo also rewrites the file with `lines.join("\n")` after `split(/\r?\n/)`, silently converting a CRLF file to LF.
Why it matters
A lost update here silently deletes a todo Daniel just typed in Obsidian or on the phone — exactly the class of bug that erodes trust in a file-as-database design, and there is no signal it happened.
How to fix
Capture fs.statSync(TODOS_ABS).mtimeMs alongside the read, and re-check it immediately before the rename inside a small write helper (retry once or return 409 on mismatch). Since the whole cycle is synchronous, a single stat check closes essentially the entire window at trivial cost. Preserve the file's original line-ending style on rewrite while there.
Expected improvement
Concurrent external edits produce a visible 409/refetch instead of silent overwrite; round-trip no longer rewrites line endings.
Evidence
writeTodosFile(addTodo(readTodosFile() ?? "# Job TODOs\n", text));  — lib/todos.ts: `atomicWriteFileSync(TODOS_ABS, md);` and `return lines.join("\n");`; entrypoint.sh:44: `printf '/system/queue\n/system/runs\n' > /data/vault/.stignore`
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read app/api/todos/route.ts (all 69 lines) and lib/todos.ts (all 92 lines). All cited evidence is real and current: add path (route.ts:47) is an unguarded read-transform-write; toggleTodo's null→409 guard (lib/todos.ts:53-66, route.ts:57-60) validates only the client's view against the snapshot just read, not writes landing between readTodosFile (route.ts:51) and writeTodosFile (route.ts:61); writeTodosFile whole-file rewrites via atomicWriteFileSync (lib/todos.ts:89-92), which prevents torn writes but not lost updates. jobs/todos.md is Syncthing-synced (.stignore excludes only /system/queue and /system/runs) and dual-mastered per the lib/todos.ts header, so external writers (Obsidian, Syncthing) can land in the window. CRLF→LF side note also confirmed (split /\r?\n/ then join "\n", lib/todos.ts:56/62). Finding is accurately scoped — it already concedes the window is microseconds because the read-modify-write span is synchronous in one Node process, so intra-process HUD requests cannot interleave; only external processes are exposed. Nuance: the common real-world conflict (client toggling against a file Obsidian edited seconds earlier) IS caught by the existing 409, so the residual risk is the tiny in-flight window plus the guardless add — 'low' is correct, do not raise. Not a duplicate of the excluded #36-#44 era, issue #2, or the two tracked follow-ups; ADR-0001 does not make lost-update acceptable (the code's own 409 path shows conflict safety is an in-scope goal). Proposed fix (stat mtimeMs alongside read, recheck before rename, 409/retry on mismatch; preserve line endings) is sound.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read app/api/todos/route.ts (lines 43-63) and lib/todos.ts in full. The code matches the finding exactly: add is `writeTodosFile(addTodo(readTodosFile() ?? "# Job TODOs\n", text))` (route.ts:47), toggle re-reads then whole-file-rewrites (route.ts:51-61), writeTodosFile is atomicWriteFileSync of the full document (todos.ts:89-92), and toggleTodo joins with "\n" after splitting /\r?\n/ (todos.ts:56,62), so a CRLF file would be normalized to LF. The file does live in the Syncthing-synced vault region (.stignore only excludes /system/queue and /system/runs). So the race exists as described and nothing elsewhere closes it — exists=true. However, the severity is inflated even at "low", and the finding's own framing overstates the exposure. Two mitigations narrow it to a sub-millisecond window: (1) both actions do a FRESH readFileSync at request time, so any Obsidian/Syncthing edit that landed before the request is preserved, not clobbered — the common dual-master scenario (edit in Obsidian, later act in HUD) is safe; (2) the multi-second staleness window (HUD rendered stale state, user clicks) is exactly what the existing toggleTodo index+text check → 409 handles (route.ts:57-60, todos.ts:50-55, unit-tested in scripts/test-todos.ts). The only unguarded window is the synchronous read→transform→rename span inside one Node event-loop turn — microseconds — and losing an update requires an external writer to land inside it. For a single-user tool the user cannot type in Obsidian and hit the HUD simultaneously; only a Syncthing delivery coinciding to the microsecond loses data, and Syncthing would then surface its own conflict/sync-back. "add has no conflict guard at all" is technically true but misleading — add appends to a fresh read, so a guard only matters for that same microsecond span. The CRLF note is real but moot: the file was seeded from Obsidian on macOS and is LF. The proposed fix (stat mtimeMs before rename, 409 on mismatch) is sound and cheap, though mtime resolution caveats apply on non-APFS filesystems; a fine hardening, not a needed one. Suggest downgrading low → info.

feeds/morphy-github.py:183-199 · reviewer: unswept-feeds
What it is
fetch_list() walks up to MAX_PAGES (10 pages x 100 = 1000 items); when the loop exhausts with a full final page it prints a stderr warning — the comment says 'say so instead of letting truncation masquerade as data' — but then returns the capped list anyway. main() rolls that capped list up and writes it to metrics.csv with status 'ok'. The stderr warning goes to the com.helm.morphy launchd log, which nothing monitors, so the capped value does masquerade as data in the one place that is read (the Vitals tile and the metrics history).

How to fix
On MAX_PAGES exhaustion with a full final page, raise RuntimeError (main() already converts any exception into the log-and-exit-1-without-writing path), or thread a truncated flag through and write the row with a non-ok status. Alternatively, if capping is acceptable, fix the comment to say the count is intentionally capped.

toggleTodo rewrites the whole file with LF endings, discarding original CRLF and hard-coding the bullet form

lib/todos.ts:58-64 · reviewer: vault-markdown-parsers
What it is
toggleTodo splits on `/\r?\n/` and rejoins with `lines.join("\n")`, and rewrites the matched line as `` `- [${done ? "x" : " "}] ${m[2]}` ``. If the file ever arrives with CRLF endings (the vault is Syncthing-synced; a Windows peer or a paste from a Windows editor produces CRLF), a single checkbox toggle silently rewrites every line ending in the file. That turns a one-character edit into a whole-file change: Syncthing sees a full-content rewrite, maximizing the window for a sync conflict with a concurrent Obsidian edit on another device, and git/Obsidian diffs show the entire file touched.
Why it matters
The 409 stale-check in toggleTodo exists precisely because concurrent Obsidian/Syncthing edits are expected; a toggle that rewrites all N lines instead of 1 makes the conflict surface as large as possible. It is silent — the content is semantically identical, so nothing flags the normalization.
How to fix
Detect the file's dominant line ending once (`md.includes("\r\n") ? "\r\n" : "\n"`) and join with it, or better: locate the target line by index and splice only that line's `[ ]`/`[x]` characters into the original string, leaving every other byte untouched.
Expected improvement
A toggle changes exactly one character on disk regardless of the file's line-ending convention, minimizing Syncthing conflict surface and keeping diffs honest.
Evidence
const lines = md.split(/\r?\n/);
...
      lines[i] = `- [${done ? "x" : " "}] ${m[2]}`;
      return lines.join("\n");
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read lib/todos.ts in full. toggleTodo (lines 53-66) splits on /\r?\n/ (line 56), rewrites the matched line as `- [${done ? "x" : " "}] ${m[2]}` (line 61), and rejoins with lines.join("\n") (line 62) — exactly as the evidence quotes. A CRLF-ended file would have every \r stripped on one toggle, so the claim is accurate. The bullet "hard-coding" is milder than it sounds: the CHECKBOX regex (line 27) only matches lines already of the form `- [ |x|X] `, so the rewrite only canonicalizes `[X]`→`[x]` — no other bullet variants can reach that branch. One overstatement: the write path is atomicWriteFileSync (writeTodosFile, line 91), which replaces the whole file on every toggle regardless, so "one-character edit becomes whole-file change" is about content diff size (every line's bytes changing, larger Syncthing delta / noisier git+Obsidian diffs), not about whole-file-write vs in-place-write. Same LF-join pattern exists in parse-side callers only here; addTodo (line 71) appends "\n" too but doesn't rewrite existing lines. Practical likelihood is low (single-user macOS vault, file seeded locally with LF), consistent with the finding's own low severity. Fix suggestion in the finding is correct and cheap.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read lib/todos.ts fully; code at lines 56-62 matches the evidence — split on /\r?\n/, rejoin with "\n", so a CRLF file is silently LF-normalized on first toggle. However the impact argument is materially overstated: (a) writeTodosFile already uses atomicWriteFileSync, so EVERY toggle is a whole-file replace; Syncthing conflict detection is per-file, so the LF normalization adds nothing to the conflict window — the finding's central "maximizes the sync conflict surface" claim is wrong; (b) "hard-coding the bullet form" affects only the one toggled line, whose form the CHECKBOX regex already required (only [X]→[x] is normalized); (c) CRLF is hypothetical on this single-user macOS vault (Obsidian/macOS writes LF; peers are a read-only Fly Linux VM and a phone). Remaining real impact is a one-time cosmetic whole-file diff in git/Obsidian if CRLF ever appears. Proposed fix is fine. Real but downgrade low → info.

intent.source is write-only metadata: six writer values, zero reader branches, and it is dropped from the run record

runner/runner.js:598-611 · reviewer: intent-json-contract
What it is
Writers stamp six distinct source values into intent files — 'vault-hud' (app/api/queue/route.ts:36), 'voice-ptt' (app/api/voice/route.ts:50), 'voice-wake' (app/api/voice/text/route.ts:35), 'chat' (CHAT_SYSTEM prose), 'schedule' (scripts/queue-intent.mjs:28 default, also the plist arg), and 'runner' (retryIntent fallback, runner.js:354) — but the only consumer of intent.source in the entire codebase is retryIntent's passthrough. The run record `status` object built at runner.js:598-611 (id, skill, args, ts_queued, ts_started, ts_completed, status, exit_code, summary, md_path, log_path, deliverable_path) omits source entirely, and processNative's copy (runner.js:1099-1112) does too, so once an intent is consumed its origin is unrecoverable: a system/runs/*.json cannot tell a scheduled weekly-review from a voice-dispatched one, and a stall-retried run loses both its origin (source becomes 'runner' only if the original omitted it — otherwise it is carried, but the new id has no pointer back to the original run's id). No reader branches on a value no writer emits, so there is no active taxonomy bug — the field is simply dead on arrival.
Why it matters
When debugging duplicate side-effectful runs (the exact scenario the dedupe layers exist for), the first question is 'which front door queued this?' — and the run records cannot answer it. The taxonomy also has no single definition, so a new writer inventing a seventh string would be indistinguishable from a typo.
How to fix
Either carry source into both run-record shapes (one field added to the status objects at runner.js:598-611 and 1099-1112, plus a `retried_from: <original id>` on retryIntent output for lineage), or delete the field from the intent contract and its writers. If kept, define the legal values once (e.g. exported from lib/skills.ts next to writeIntent).
Expected improvement
Run records become self-explanatory about origin, and stall-retry lineage is traceable from the retry's run record instead of only from runner.log.
Evidence
runner.js:598-611 status object has no `source` key; only non-writer use of the field is runner.js:354 `source: intent.source || "runner"` inside retryIntent; writers grep: app/api/queue/route.ts:36 `writeIntent(skill, "vault-hud", args)`, voice routes pass "voice-ptt"/"voice-wake", queue-intent.mjs:28 `process.argv[3] || "schedule"`.
Verifier notes (2)

Error handling & robustness (10)

highConfirmedverifier suggests: medium backend effort: small

app/api/chat runClaude has no SIGKILL escalation or process-group kill — a wedged claude turn hangs the request and locks the thread forever

app/api/chat/route.ts:145-173 · reviewer: error-handling
What it is
runClaude()'s 5-minute timeout does only `proc.kill()` — a single SIGTERM to the direct child, with no SIGKILL follow-up and no process-group kill (the spawn is not detached). The promise resolves only on 'close' or 'error'. If the headless claude ignores SIGTERM, or a grandchild (MCP server, shell tool) inherited the stdio pipes and holds them open after the child dies, 'close' never fires and the promise never settles. runner/runner.js defends against exactly this with killTree() on the process group + a SIGTERM→10s→SIGKILL escalation + an 'exit'-plus-5s-drain fallback (runner.js:704-711, 777-783, with a comment saying a grandchild "can hold it open after the child died") — the chat route has none of the three.
Why it matters
When runClaude never settles, the POST handler is stuck on the await: the HTTP request hangs indefinitely, and `releaseThread(threadId)` in the `finally` block never runs. The in-process `busy` set (lib/chat.ts:95) then rejects every later turn on that thread with 409 "thread busy" until the whole Next server is restarted. From the phone the chat tab just dies silently. The runner's own history (the 2026-06-28 weekly-review that wedged with zero output, per the STALL_TIMEOUT_MS comment) shows wedged `claude -p` processes are a real, observed failure mode, not hypothetical.
How to fix
Mirror the runner's pattern: spawn with `detached: true`, kill the group (`process.kill(-proc.pid, sig)`) with SIGTERM then a 10s SIGKILL escalation on timeout; additionally listen on 'exit' with a short drain timer so the promise settles even if a grandchild holds the pipes, and make the resolve idempotent (settled flag). Alternatively, race the runClaude promise against a hard deadline so the route always returns and releaseThread always runs, even if the child lingers.
Expected improvement
A wedged chat turn degrades to a clean 504 and the thread stays usable, instead of a permanently hung request plus a thread that 409s until server restart.
Evidence
const timer = setTimeout(() => {
  timedOut = true;
  try {
    proc.kill();
  } catch { /* ignore */ }
}, HARD_TIMEOUT_MS);
...
proc.on("close", (code) => { clearTimeout(timer); resolve({ stdout, stderr, code, timedOut }); });
— vs runner.js: "'close' waits for the stdio pipes to drain — a grandchild that inherited them can hold it open after the child died."
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read app/api/chat/route.ts in full and cross-checked lib/chat.ts and runner/runner.js. Confirmed exactly as described: runClaude (route.ts:145-174, finding said 145-173 — one line off, immaterial) spawns without detached:true, its 5-min timeout does only proc.kill() (bare SIGTERM to the direct child), and the promise resolves solely on 'close' or 'error'. No SIGKILL escalation, no process-group kill, no 'exit'+drain fallback. If claude ignores SIGTERM or a grandchild holds the inherited stdio pipes open, 'close' never fires, the POST await hangs, and releaseThread(threadId) in the finally block (route.ts:141) never runs — the in-process busy Set (lib/chat.ts:95, acquireThread at :98) then 409s every subsequent turn on that thread until server restart. The contrast with runner.js is real: killTree on the detached process group (runner.js:451-454, detached at :676), SIGTERM→10s SIGKILL escalation (:706-710, again at :720-721 and :1040-1041), and the exit+drain comment about a grandchild holding pipes open after the child died (:779). Not covered by the excluded/known lists; the ADR-0009 acceptance covers the skip-permissions flag, not missing kill hygiene. Fix suggestion in the finding is sound; the simplest robust variant is the 'race against a hard deadline so the route always settles' option, since it guarantees releaseThread even if the child lingers.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Confirmed in current code. app/api/chat/route.ts:145-174 runClaude() timeout does only proc.kill() (bare SIGTERM, spawn not detached, no group kill, no SIGKILL escalation) and the promise settles only on 'close'/'error' — no 'exit'+drain fallback, no settled flag. runner/runner.js has all three defenses (killTree SIGTERM→10s→SIGKILL, exit+5s drainTimer, settled flag) plus the exact comment quoted in the evidence, so the failure mode is one the author treats as real; the chat spawn site was simply not hardened. Impact chain verified: unsettled promise → await hangs at route.ts:91 → finally (line 141) never runs → busy set (lib/chat.ts:95) holds threadId → 409 on that thread until Next restarts. No mitigation found: nothing races the await, no busy-set sweep, com.helm.watchdog covers runner/fleet, not Next handlers. Line/description/fix all accurate. Severity correction: busy is per-thread, so only the wedged thread locks — a new thread works immediately and the old thread recovers on restart; blast radius is one thread + one hung request, not the whole chat surface. That argues medium rather than high, though on the Fly VM /api/chat is the only mutating route so a wedged default thread reads as "chat is dead" from the phone.
mediumConfirmed runner effort: small

morphySync/agendaSync stamp a fresh last_sync_ts on FAILURE, so the fleet watchdog can never detect a persistently broken agenda feed or Notion sync

runner/runner.js:917-934, 1074-1090 · reviewer: bugs-runner
What it is
morphySync's error path writes `{ ...(prev||{}), ok: false, reason, last_sync_ts: new Date().toISOString() }` and agendaSync's no-valid-cache fallback likewise writes `last_sync_ts: new Date().toISOString()`. The fleet watchdog's staleness check for both producers looks ONLY at the age of `last_sync_ts` (fleet.js lines 110-133: `stale: agendaAge > agendaLimit`, `stale: morphyAge > AGE_LIMIT_MIN["morphy-board"]`) and never inspects `ok`. Because both wrappers run on setInterval inside the runner and refresh last_sync_ts even when they fail, a permanently broken producer — revoked NOTION_TOKEN, or agenda's python spawn ENOENT-ing forever (AGENDA_PYTHON defaults to /usr/local/bin/python3, only env-overridable) — keeps fleet-health.json green indefinitely. The watchdog's kick path for these two producers (KICK_TARGETS agenda→agendaSync, morphy-board→morphySync) is therefore unreachable except when the runner's own scheduler dies.
Why it matters
This is exactly the silent-failure mode issue #58's watchdog exists to surface: the HUD red dot stays green while agenda/board data is frozen at its last good state (or a typed ok:false the user only notices by opening the tile). 'The wrapper ran' is being measured where 'the producer produced' was intended — the other seven producers all measure real output (files, metric rows).
How to fix
Either (a) only bump last_sync_ts on success and add a separate last_attempt_ts for the failure paths, or (b) have deriveFleetHealth also treat `ok === false` persisting across N consecutive passes (using prev's producer record) as stale-with-reason, without kicking (a kick can't fix auth). Option (a) is smaller and makes the existing age math correct.
Expected improvement
A dead Notion token or missing python interpreter turns the fleet dot red within one cadence instead of never, matching the watchdog's contract for every other producer.
Evidence
runner.js morphySync error path: `ok: false, reason: String(e.message||e).slice(0,160), last_sync_ts: new Date().toISOString()`; agendaSync fallback: `ok: false, reason: … , last_sync_ts: new Date().toISOString()`; fleet.js: `stale: agendaAge > agendaLimit` (ok never consulted)
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Confirmed. runner/runner.js: morphySync failure paths stamp fresh last_sync_ts on ok:false — actually TWO paths, lines 903-914 (no NOTION_TOKEN) and 921-926 (queryTasks throw), so the correct range is 903-934, wider than the cited 917-934. agendaSync fallback (lines 1074-1091) likewise writes ok:false with a fresh last_sync_ts; spawn ENOENT funnels there via finish(-1). runner/fleet.js deriveFleetHealth (lines 110-133) computes stale for agenda/morphy-board purely from last_sync_ts age and never reads .ok; KICK_TARGETS (line 36) maps both to the same sync wrappers, so the kick path is unreachable while the runner scheduler lives — exactly as claimed. Minor corrections: (1) env override for the python path is PYTHON_BIN, not AGENDA_PYTHON (AGENDA_PYTHON is the constant name, runner.js line 99); (2) the fleet.js comment "stale = last sync older than 2x the sync interval" hints the author may have deliberately scoped these two checks to scheduler liveness, but the asymmetry with the seven output-measuring producers and the frozen-green red dot are real; proposed fix (a) — bump last_sync_ts only on success, add last_attempt_ts — is correct and small. Not a duplicate of any excluded item. Medium severity stands.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Confirmed in current code. runner/runner.js: morphySync stamps fresh last_sync_ts on ok:false in BOTH the no-NOTION_TOKEN path (903-914) and the catch path (921-926); agendaSync's fallback (1074-1084) does the same. runner/fleet.js 110-133 computes staleness for agenda/morphy-board solely from last_sync_ts age and never reads ok, so a persistently failing producer keeps fleet-health green and the KICK_TARGETS path for these two is unreachable unless the runner's scheduler itself dies. Finding actually understates the agenda case: feeds/calendar-agenda.py:132 also writes a fresh last_sync_ts on its own ok:false fallback, so feed-level failures (revoked OAuth) are green too, not just spawn failures. Corrections: the env override for AGENDA_PYTHON is PYTHON_BIN, not AGENDA_PYTHON (runner.js:99); fix (a) would also need applying to calendar-agenda.py's failure writer for full coverage. Refutations tried: no fleet test asserts this as intended behavior; ADR-0008's typed ok:false tile display is a partial mitigation (failure is visible on the tile), but the issue-#58 watchdog/red-dot was added precisely to surface such failures, so severity medium stands.

voiceClient.finishCapture calls rec.stop() unguarded and awaits a 'stop' event that may never fire — a dead mic makes PTT release fail silently

lib/voiceClient.ts:381-395 · reviewer: error-handling
What it is
finishCapture() does `rec.addEventListener("stop", () => res(), { once: true }); rec.stop();` with no guard on recorder state. If the MediaRecorder already stopped itself — the mic track ended mid-hold (device unplugged, macOS input switch; the code even installs `t.onended` handlers for this at startCapture:325-328) — `rec.stop()` throws InvalidStateError inside the Promise executor, rejecting the promise; and even if stop() were wrapped, the once-listener for an already-fired 'stop' event never fires, so the promise never settles. The caller is `void voice.finishCapture()` (components/shell/Shell.tsx:278), so the rejection is unhandled and nothing reaches `this.log` — the user releases Space and simply nothing happens, with no "microphone unavailable" line. cancelCapture() at line 374-377 wraps its own `rec.stop()` in try/catch, showing the hazard is known but the fix wasn't applied to the path that actually ships the clip.
Why it matters
Push-to-talk is the primary input surface of the HUD. In the mic-died-mid-capture case the failure is completely silent: no error in the voice log, no transcript, an unhandled promise rejection in the console nobody watches, and `this.recorder` was already nulled so retrying looks identical. The codebase's own convention (dispatchText, startCapture) is to surface every voice failure through this.log.
How to fix
In finishCapture, check `rec.state`: if it is already "inactive", skip the stop/await and proceed straight to building the blob from the collected chunks (or log 'microphone lost' and return). Wrap `rec.stop()` in try/catch like cancelCapture does, and log a `this.log("err", ...)` line on failure so the user sees why nothing transcribed.
Expected improvement
A mic that dies during a hold produces a visible 'microphone unavailable' log line (or still ships the partial clip) instead of a silent no-op with an unhandled rejection.
Evidence
await new Promise<void>((res) => {
  rec.addEventListener("stop", () => res(), { once: true });
  rec.stop();
});
— vs cancelCapture: if (rec) { try { rec.stop(); } catch {} }
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Verified against current code. lib/voiceClient.ts:389-392 does exactly what the finding claims: rec.stop() called unguarded inside a Promise executor with a once 'stop' listener; no rec.state check, no try/catch. cancelCapture (lines 373-377) wraps its own rec.stop() in try/catch, confirming the contrast. startCapture's t.onended handlers (lines 324-328) null micStream/micSource but not this.recorder, so a mid-hold track death leaves this.recorder pointing at an already-stopped recorder. Call site confirmed: components/shell/Shell.tsx:278 is `void voice.finishCapture();` — rejection is unhandled and no this.log line fires. Both failure modes are real depending on engine: Blink throws InvalidStateError on stop() of an inactive recorder (promise rejects, unhandled); spec-current no-op behavior means the 'stop' event fired before the listener attached, so the promise never settles. Either way PTT release fails silently. Minor line corrections only: cancelCapture block is 373-377 (finding said 374-377), onended handlers 324-328 (finding said 325-328). Fix suggestion is correct; refinement: when rec.state === "inactive", the pre-stop chunks are already in this.chunks, so the blob can still be built and shipped rather than just logging. Not covered by the excluded #36-#44 review-era fixes — this is current code.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read lib/voiceClient.ts:280-440 and grepped call sites. Confirmed: finishCapture (lines 381-395) does `await new Promise<void>((res) => { rec.addEventListener("stop", () => res(), { once: true }); rec.stop(); })` with no rec.state guard and no try/catch, while cancelCapture (373-377) wraps its stop() in try/catch. Sole caller is `void voice.finishCapture()` at components/shell/Shell.tsx:278, so any rejection is unhandled and nothing reaches this.log. The trigger is real: MediaRecorder stops itself when its source stream's tracks end (mic unplugged/input switch), and startCapture:318-328 explicitly anticipates dead tracks (t.onended handlers, inactive-stream cache invalidation), so the scenario is within the code's own threat model. No test covers voiceClient (browser-API code, no references in scripts/). Two corrections: (1) The "rec.stop() throws InvalidStateError, rejecting the promise" branch is per-MDN but the current MediaStream Recording spec makes stop() a no-op on an inactive recorder (modern Chrome/Firefox follow the spec), so in practice the more likely failure mode is the finding's second branch — the once-listener is attached after 'stop' already fired, stop() no-ops, and the promise never settles, hanging finishCapture forever. Either branch yields the same observable outcome the finding describes: user releases Space, no "transcribing …" log, no transcript, silent. (2) "retrying looks identical" slightly overstates it: this.recorder is nulled before the await and startCapture re-acquires an inactive micStream, so the NEXT press-and-hold works — only the in-flight utterance is silently dropped, plus one leaked pending promise. Proposed fix (guard rec.state === "inactive", try/catch stop(), this.log on failure) is correct and matches the file's own error-surfacing convention (startCapture logs "microphone unavailable"). Severity: suggest low rather than medium — requires the mic device to die mid-hold (rare), single-user personal tool, self-recovering on the next Space press; the cost is one silently lost utterance, not a stuck pipeline.

app/api/speak returns String(e) to the client and logs nothing server-side — TTS generation failures leave no trace anywhere

app/api/speak/route.ts:30-35 · reviewer: error-handling
What it is
stream()'s catch-all returns `NextResponse.json({ error: String(e) }, { status: 502 })` with no `console.error`. Every other route in the codebase does the opposite — logs the detail server-side and returns a generic message, with explicit comments ("String(e) leaks vault paths" in /api/queue and /api/todos, "detail stays server-side" in /api/voice and /api/chat). Worse for diagnosability: /api/speak's main consumer is an `<audio src=...>` element (lib/voiceClient.ts playOne:518), which cannot read a JSON error body — the client only ever sees "audio element error". So when Kokoro starts 500ing or the 20s fetch timeout in lib/tts.ts speak() fires, the error string is sent to a consumer that discards it and is recorded nowhere on the server.
Why it matters
A degraded voice-server (generating errors while its cached /health probe still passes — the exact scenario the `kokoroAliveUntil = 0` comment in lib/tts.ts anticipates) is undiagnosable: the HUD log shows only 'voice playback failed: Error: audio element error' and the server console shows nothing. It also breaks the repo's own stated error-detail policy, though the leak here is minor (a 'kokoro 500' or localhost fetch error, not vault paths).
How to fix
Match the sibling routes: `console.error("[/api/speak]", e)` in the catch, and return a generic `{ error: "tts failed" }` body. The VoiceConfigError branch above it is fine as-is (its message is intentionally user-facing).
Expected improvement
Mid-flight TTS failures become visible in the server log (the only place they can be seen, given the audio-element consumer), and the route stops being the one exception to the error-detail policy.
Evidence
} catch (e) {
    if (e instanceof VoiceConfigError) {
      return NextResponse.json({ ok: false, error: e.message }, { status: 503 });
    }
    return NextResponse.json({ error: String(e) }, { status: 502 });
  }
— vs /api/queue: console.error("[/api/queue]", e); // detail stays server-side — String(e) leaks vault paths

atomicWriteFileSync leaves orphaned .tmp-<pid> files in Syncthing-synced vault dirs after a crash, with no cleanup path

lib/atomicWrite.ts:8-12 · reviewer: bugs-vault-state
What it is
atomicWriteFileSync writes `${file}.tmp-${process.pid}` then renames. If the process dies between writeFileSync and renameSync (crash, SIGKILL from launchd, power loss), the tmp file is orphaned forever — nothing scans for or removes stale `*.tmp-*` files. For queue/runs this is harmless (the runner's UUID_JSON_RE ignores them and .stignore keeps those dirs out of sync), but the helper is also used for jobs/todos.md (lib/todos.ts:91), system/voice/memory.jsonl (lib/voiceMemory.ts:44), and the chat sidecar (app/api/chat/route.ts:127) — all inside the Syncthing-synced portion of the vault (the .stignore written by entrypoint.sh covers only /system/queue and /system/runs). An orphan like `jobs/todos.md.tmp-4242` replicates to every peer and lingers in Obsidian's file tree indefinitely. The write is also never fsync'd, so rename-atomicity protects readers but not crash durability — acceptable for memory/todos, but a queue intent acked to the user via /api/queue (lib/skills.ts:38) can evaporate on power loss after the HTTP 200.
Why it matters
Orphaned tmp litter propagates through Syncthing to all devices and never self-heals; the missing durability on queue intents means a spoken command can be acknowledged and then silently lost across a crash, with nothing in system/runs to show it ever existed.
How to fix
On process start (or in each writer's mkdir step) sweep sibling `<name>.tmp-*` files older than a few minutes; optionally add `*.tmp-*` to the vault .stignore lines written by entrypoint.sh and kept on the Mac vault. If queue-intent durability is wanted, fsync the tmp fd (fs.fsyncSync on an opened fd) before rename for that one call site only.
Expected improvement
No permanent tmp litter syncing across devices; acked queue intents survive a crash if the fsync option is taken.
Evidence
const tmp = `${file}.tmp-${process.pid}`;
fs.writeFileSync(tmp, data, "utf-8");
fs.renameSync(tmp, file);  — no fsync, no cleanup of orphans; entrypoint.sh:44 stignore covers only /system/queue and /system/runs
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read lib/atomicWrite.ts (lines 8-12 match the evidence verbatim: write tmp-${pid}, renameSync, no fsync, no cleanup). Verified every cited call site at the exact lines claimed: lib/todos.ts:91, lib/voiceMemory.ts:44, app/api/chat/route.ts:127, lib/skills.ts:38. Repo-wide greps found zero fsync calls and zero orphan-sweep logic; scripts/test-vault.ts:246 only asserts the happy path leaves no temp file. entrypoint.sh:44 confirms .stignore covers only /system/queue and /system/runs, so tmp orphans beside jobs/todos.md, the voice memory file, and the chat sidecar are in Syncthing-synced territory as claimed. Minor correction/extension: the finding understates scope — runner/runner.js:209 and runner/fleet.js:231 use the same pattern with a bare `.tmp` suffix (no pid), so the runner side has the same orphan gap plus a potential cross-process tmp-name collision, though those writes target system/ paths that are mostly stignored. Severity low is right: cosmetic litter plus a narrow power-loss window on acked queue intents in a single-user system. Not covered by any ADR or the known/excluded list.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read lib/atomicWrite.ts (lines 8-12 exactly as quoted: write `${file}.tmp-${process.pid}` then renameSync, no fsync), entrypoint.sh line 44 (`printf '/system/queue\n/system/runs\n' > /data/vault/.stignore` — only those two dirs excluded from sync), and all four call sites: lib/todos.ts:91 (jobs/todos.md), lib/voiceMemory.ts:44 (system/voice memory file), app/api/chat/route.ts:127 (chat sidecar), lib/skills.ts:38 (queue intent). The only tmp-related guard is scripts/test-vault.ts:246, which asserts the happy path leaves no temp file — it does not cover crash orphans. So a crash between write and rename orphans e.g. jobs/todos.md.tmp-<pid> inside the Syncthing-synced vault with no self-healing path; the .stignore mitigation covers only queue/runs, exactly as the finding says. The no-fsync durability point is also accurate (rename-atomicity protects readers only; a queue intent acked via HTTP 200 can vanish on power loss), though the crash window is a few ms and this is a single-user Mac, so 'low' is the right severity — do not raise it. Minor addition (out of scope of the cited file): runner/runner.js:208-211 writeJson and runner/fleet.js:231 have the same pattern with a plain `.tmp` suffix, so any sweep fix should cover `*.tmp` too, not just `*.tmp-*`. Nothing in ADRs 0001-0009 or the known-excluded list covers this; not intentional-by-design.

handleVoiceResponse latches voice off with the wrong diagnosis ('TTS key missing') when a 503 actually means STT is down

lib/voiceClient.ts:412-415 · reviewer: bugs-voice
What it is
A 503 from /api/voice or /api/voice/text is produced by lib/stt.ts's VoiceConfigError when the voice-server's STT is unreachable ("no STT engine: the voice-server stt on :3108 is down"), but handleVoiceResponse logs `voice offline — TTS key missing` and latches `this.disabled = true`. The message is doubly wrong: the failing component is STT, not TTS, and there is no TTS key at all — the stack is fully local Kokoro (the ElevenLabs fallback was removed per lib/tts.ts's header). The latch also mutes all subsequent speak() calls (run announcements from Shell.tsx line 345) until a wake-WS hello or a PTT re-probe un-latches it, even though TTS may be fine.
Why it matters
When STT hiccups, the user is told to hunt for a nonexistent API key, and unrelated TTS announcements go silent — misdirected debugging for the owner of a personal tool whose whole voice stack is keyless.
How to fix
Change the message to reflect reality (e.g. "voice offline — voice-server STT on :3108 is down", or surface the server's error field from the 503 JSON body), and consider not latching `disabled` for an STT-side 503 since TTS availability is probed independently.
Expected improvement
Accurate failure diagnosis in the HUD log; TTS announcements keep working when only STT is briefly down.
Evidence
if (res.status === 503) { this.disabled = true; this.log("err", "voice offline — TTS key missing"); return; }
Verifier notes (2)

The 503 is produced by app/api/voice/route.ts line 52-53 when it catches VoiceConfigError, and lib/stt.ts line 35-36 throws that with "no STT engine: the voice-server stt on :3108 is down …" — so the failing component is indeed STT, not TTS. lib/tts.ts's header (lines 4-10) confirms the stack is fully local Kokoro with the ElevenLabs fallback removed 2026-06-12, so no TTS key exists anywhere; even the TTS-side VoiceConfigError (lib/tts.ts line 61) says "voice-server on :3108 is down", not a key. The latch effect is also real: speak() at line 225-227 silently returns when this.disabled is true, so run announcements are muted; un-latch happens only via the wake-WS hello (line 152-153) or a PTT re-probe (lines 300-310). Minor additions the finding missed: the same stale diagnosis exists at line 51 (field comment "// 503 — no key on the server"), line 503 ("503 means key vanished"), and there is a second 503 latch around lines 565-566 worth checking when fixing. The proposed fix (surface the 503 body's error field, which stt.ts already makes accurate and actionable) is sound. Severity low is right — cosmetic/diagnostic, single-user tool, self-heals on re-probe.

claude-tokens.py: main() catches only URLError/TimeoutError/ValueError, so mid-body read failures crash with a raw traceback

feeds/claude-tokens.py:121-125 · reviewer: bugs-feeds
What it is
fetch_usage() does json.load(resp) directly on the HTTP response body. urlopen() failures surface as URLError and malformed JSON as ValueError — both caught — but errors raised while *reading* the body (http.client.IncompleteRead, which is an HTTPException, or a raw ConnectionResetError/OSError from a connection dropped mid-transfer) are not URLError subclasses and escape the except clause, terminating the feed with an unhandled traceback instead of the clean one-line 'usage endpoint failed: ...' stderr message. Every other feed in the directory (uscf-rating.py line 85, morphy-github.py line 237, calendar-agenda.py line 276) deliberately uses a broad `except Exception` with a '# noqa: BLE001 — log and bail' comment; this one is the odd one out. No row is written either way, so the metrics contract survives, but the launchd log gets a stack trace where a diagnosable one-liner was intended.
Why it matters
Inconsistent with the sibling feeds' explicit log-and-bail contract; a flaky network moment produces a traceback in the runner/launchd log that looks like a code bug rather than the transient network failure it is.
How to fix
Match the other feeds: `except Exception as e: # noqa: BLE001` around the fetch+parse in main(), keeping the same 'usage endpoint failed: {e}' message and return 1.
Expected improvement
All transient network failures produce the same clean one-line stderr diagnostic as the other four feeds instead of an occasional traceback.
Evidence
try:
        pcts = usage_pcts(fetch_usage(token))
    except (urllib.error.URLError, TimeoutError, ValueError) as e:
        print(f"usage endpoint failed: {e}", file=sys.stderr)
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read feeds/claude-tokens.py in full. Lines 121-125 match the quoted evidence exactly: main() wraps usage_pcts(fetch_usage(token)) in `except (urllib.error.URLError, TimeoutError, ValueError)`. fetch_usage() (lines 99-105) does json.load(resp) inside the urlopen context, so body-read failures happen inside the try. The exception-taxonomy claim is correct: http.client.IncompleteRead is an HTTPException (not a URLError subclass), and a mid-transfer ConnectionResetError/OSError raised during read() is not wrapped into URLError by urllib (wrapping happens only during connection setup in urlopen). URLError subclasses OSError, not the reverse, so catching URLError does not catch bare OSError. Such an escape would produce an unhandled traceback instead of the intended one-line stderr message; no metrics row is written either way, so impact is log noise only, matching the low severity. Verified the sibling-consistency claim with grep: uscf-rating.py:85, morphy-github.py:237, calendar-agenda.py:276 all use `except Exception as e: # noqa: BLE001` broad log-and-bail handlers — claude-tokens.py is indeed the outlier. Not covered by the excluded/known lists. Proposed fix (broad except Exception with same message and return 1) is appropriate; one nuance: keeping HTTPError visible is unaffected since HTTPError is a URLError subclass and would still be caught by the broader handler. Line citation 121-125 is accurate.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read feeds/claude-tokens.py in full and grepped the sibling feeds. Confirmed: lines 121-125 catch only (URLError, TimeoutError, ValueError); json.load(resp) at line 105 reads the body inside urlopen's context, and mid-body read failures (http.client.IncompleteRead — an HTTPException — or raw ConnectionResetError/OSError from a dropped connection) are not URLError subclasses, so they escape as an unhandled traceback. Sibling feeds confirmed at exactly the cited lines: uscf-rating.py:85, morphy-github.py:237, calendar-agenda.py:276 all use `except Exception as e: # noqa: BLE001` log-and-bail. Materiality is correctly scoped by the finding itself: the crash still exits nonzero and writes no metrics row, so only the log output degrades (traceback instead of the intended one-line 'usage endpoint failed' message). Proposed fix (broad except Exception matching siblings) is correct and safe — usage_pcts is pure. No mitigation elsewhere; no ADR or excluded item covers this. Severity low is right (could argue info, but the deliberate log-and-bail contract in every other feed makes the inconsistency worth low).

app/api/chat: a transcript-mirror write failure after a completed turn discards the session_id — the next turn silently forks a fresh claude session

app/api/chat/route.ts:110-134 · reviewer: error-handling
What it is
After the claude turn succeeds, the route first writes the human transcript (writeFileSync/appendFileSync on inbox/chats/<threadId>.md, lines 112-123) and only then persists the session-id sidecar (atomicWriteFileSync, line 127). Neither write is individually guarded; a throw from the transcript append (disk full, inbox/chats unwritable, Syncthing lock) lands in the outer catch, which returns 502 "internal error". At that point the turn already ran and `parsed.session_id` exists, but the sidecar was never written — on the user's retry, readSidecar() returns the stale (or empty) state and the route spawns claude WITHOUT --resume pointing at the completed turn, silently dropping that turn from the thread's memory. The sidecar comment at line 125-126 identifies exactly this consequence ("silently forks a new claude session and loses the thread's memory") but only defends against torn writes, not against the ordering.
Why it matters
The whole point of the sidecar (per the route's own header comment) is that the session-id is the thread's continuity. An incidental failure in the cosmetic transcript mirror shouldn't be able to sever it — the user gets a 502, retries, and the conversation quietly loses a turn (or the whole thread context on turn 1) with no signal that memory was dropped.
How to fix
Reorder: write the sidecar (the load-bearing state) immediately after parsing the claude output, before the transcript mirror; wrap the mirror writes in their own try/catch that logs and continues, since the transcript is best-effort. Then a mirror failure still returns the reply and preserves continuity.
Expected improvement
Transcript-mirror I/O failures degrade to a missing markdown line instead of a lost session-id and a silently forked conversation.
Evidence
appendFileSync(
      transcript,
      `\n**You** · ${ts}\n\n${message}\n\n**HELM** (${model}) · ...` 
    );

    // atomic — a torn sidecar makes readSidecar() return {} next turn, which
    // silently forks a new claude session and loses the thread's memory
    atomicWriteFileSync(sidecarPath(threadId), ...)
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read app/api/chat/route.ts in full. Confirmed: transcript mirror writes (writeFileSync line 113, appendFileSync line 119) precede the sidecar atomicWriteFileSync (line 127) and neither is individually guarded — a mirror-write throw hits the outer catch (lines 137-139) and returns 502 after the turn completed, so parsed.session_id is never persisted. readSidecar (lines 49-55) then serves stale/empty state on retry, spawning claude without --resume to the completed turn's session. The comment at 125-126 defends only against torn sidecar writes, not this ordering. Cited lines and evidence are accurate. Minor precision: on non-first turns the retry resumes the stale prior sessionId (drops one turn of memory), not a fully fresh session; full fork only on turn 1 — the finding already acknowledges this. Fix (sidecar-first, best-effort mirror) is correct. Severity low is appropriate: requires a mirror-write failure at exactly that window, single-user tool.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read app/api/chat/route.ts in full. Confirmed: transcript mirror writes (lines 112-123, writeFileSync/appendFileSync, unguarded) precede the sidecar persist (atomicWriteFileSync, lines 127-134); a throw from the mirror hits the outer catch (line 137) → 502, and the just-completed turn's session_id (line 107) is never persisted. Retry then reads the stale sidecar: on turn 1 it spawns without --resume (whole context lost); on turn N it resumes the previous turn's session id (that turn's memory silently dropped). The comment at 125-126 names exactly this consequence but only guards torn writes, not ordering. No mitigation in lib/chat.ts or scripts/test-chat.ts; not sanctioned by any ADR — it violates the route's own header invariant ("the session-id is the thread's continuity"). Not a duplicate of excluded items. Minor correction: on turn ≥2 the retry resumes the stale session rather than forking a completely fresh one, so it loses one turn, not the whole thread — the description slightly overstates that sub-case; turn 1 loses everything as stated. Proposed fix (sidecar first, mirror best-effort in its own try/catch with logging) is correct and low-risk. Severity low is appropriate: requires a filesystem failure on a single-user machine; blast radius is one thread's memory.

helm-watchdog.sh with unset/missing VAULT_ROOT kickstarts the runner and posts a notification every 10 minutes forever

scripts/helm-watchdog.sh:11-27 · reviewer: deploy-infra
What it is
If VAULT_ROOT is not in the environment and `~/.claude/.env` is missing or lacks the line, the fallback sed yields an empty string, making `HB="/system/runner-status.json"` — a path that never exists. The script then takes the 'no heartbeat file' branch every 10 minutes (com.helm.watchdog.plist StartInterval=600): it kill-restarts com.helm.runner (`kickstart -k`) and posts a macOS notification, indefinitely. A runner that IS healthy but writing its heartbeat to the real vault gets forcibly killed mid-skill-execution every 10 minutes, and the misconfiguration is never named — the log just says 'no runner heartbeat file'.
Why it matters
The watchdog exists to add reliability; under this misconfig it becomes the thing that repeatedly kills a healthy runner (potentially mid claude -p run) and spams notifications, while the log message points at the runner instead of the actual problem (unresolvable VAULT_ROOT).
How to fix
Fail fast on an empty resolution: after line 11, `[ -n "$VAULT_ROOT" ] || { echo "watchdog: VAULT_ROOT unresolved — not kicking runner"; exit 1; }`.
Expected improvement
A config problem produces one clear log line instead of an infinite kill/notify loop against a healthy runner.
Evidence
Line 11-12: `VAULT_ROOT="${VAULT_ROOT:-$(sed -n 's/^VAULT_ROOT=//p' "$HOME/.claude/.env" | tr -d '"' )}"` then `HB="$VAULT_ROOT/system/runner-status.json"` with no emptiness check; line 27: `launchctl kickstart -k "gui/$(id -u)/com.helm.runner"`. com.helm.watchdog.plist: `<key>StartInterval</key><integer>600</integer>`.
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read scripts/helm-watchdog.sh (29 lines), scripts/com.helm.watchdog.plist, scripts/com.helm.runner.plist, runner/runner.js config section, and runner/env.js. All cited evidence is real and current: line 11 does the sed fallback from ~/.claude/.env with no emptiness check, line 12 builds HB="$VAULT_ROOT/system/runner-status.json" (empty VAULT_ROOT -> "/system/runner-status.json", which never exists), lines 22-27 take the 'no runner heartbeat file' branch, `launchctl kickstart -k gui/$(id -u)/com.helm.runner`, and osascript notification; com.helm.watchdog.plist has StartInterval=600 and neither plist injects VAULT_ROOT, so both processes depend on the same .env line. One scope correction: in the simplest misconfig (.env missing or line absent) the runner ALSO fails to resolve VAULT_ROOT and exits (runner.js:53-57 via env.js, which reads the same file), so the watchdog is kicking an already-dead runner — notification spam every 10 min, but no healthy runner killed. The 'healthy runner forcibly killed mid-run' scenario in the finding DOES exist via parser divergence, which I verified: runner/env.js trims leading whitespace and strips single OR double quotes, while the watchdog's `sed -n 's/^VAULT_ROOT=//p' | tr -d '"'` requires the key at column 0 and only strips double quotes — so a line like ` VAULT_ROOT=/path` or `VAULT_ROOT='/path'` gives the runner a valid vault while the watchdog resolves empty/wrong and kill-loops a healthy runner. Also true if the runner was started manually with VAULT_ROOT exported in the shell. Line numbers cited (11-12, 27) are exact. Proposed fix (fail fast on empty resolution) is correct and minimal; aligning the watchdog's parse with env.js semantics (or at least tolerating leading whitespace/single quotes) would close the divergence case too. Not covered by the KNOWN/EXCLUDED list (fleet-watchdog issue #58 shipped this script; this is a residual edge in it). Severity low is appropriate for a single-user tool with a working .env.

Mechanics CONFIRMED: line 11's sed fallback yields empty string when VAULT_ROOT is unset and ~/.claude/.env is missing/lacks the line, HB becomes "/system/runner-status.json" (never exists), the plist sets no EnvironmentVariables and StartInterval=600, so the script kickstarts com.helm.runner and posts a notification every 10 minutes with a log message ("no runner heartbeat file") that never names the real problem. The proposed fail-fast fix is correct and harmless. However the headline impact — "a runner that IS healthy ... gets forcibly killed mid-skill-execution every 10 minutes" — is materially wrong on two counts: (1) the runner resolves VAULT_ROOT from the exact same sources (process env + loadEnvFile() of ~/.claude/.env, runner.js:50-64) and exits fatally when it's unset, and com.helm.runner.plist sets no VAULT_ROOT either, so under this misconfig the launchd runner cannot be healthy — it is genuinely dead, making the watchdog's alarm directionally correct; (2) a manually started runner that got VAULT_ROOT from an interactive shell export is not the com.helm.runner launchd service, and `launchctl kickstart -k gui/UID/com.helm.runner` only kills/restarts that service instance, not the unrelated manual process — so no healthy runner is ever killed. What remains is a diagnostics/noise defect: indefinite futile kickstarts + notification spam with a misleading log line in a system that is already fully broken (no vault path anywhere). No test covers helm-watchdog.sh. Suggest downgrading low -> info; the fail-fast line is still worth adding for the clearer error message.

haikuRoute's greedy JSON extraction plus unguarded JSON.parse turns model formatting quirks into thrown errors that engineFail logs indistinguishably from network failures

lib/router.ts:936-938 · reviewer: router-model-engine-seam
What it is
haikuRoute extracts JSON with the greedy `text.match(/\{[\s\S]*\}/)` — first `{` to LAST `}` in the whole response — then calls JSON.parse with no try/catch. If Haiku wraps the JSON in prose that contains any brace after the object (an explanation, a second object, a code fence remark), the greedy match spans both and JSON.parse throws; the exception is only caught by the callers' `.catch(engineFail("haiku"))` (lines 97, 110), which logs it as 'haiku engine failed — falling back to rules', the same message as an HTTP 4xx or timeout. localRoute has the same unguarded `JSON.parse(text)` at line 1013 — its grammar-enforced `format` schema constrains token choice but not truncation: `num_predict: 200` can cut the output mid-object, producing invalid JSON that likewise surfaces as a generic 'ollama engine failed'.
Why it matters
Behavior degrades safely (fallback to the next engine/rules works), but the diagnostics are misleading: a systematic prompt-format regression (e.g. after a HAIKU_MODEL bump) would show up in logs as intermittent 'engine failed' noise identical to network blips, exactly the silent-dumbing failure the engineFail comment says it exists to prevent. In `pref === "haiku"` mode a parse failure also skips the local engine entirely and drops straight to rules.
How to fix
Use a non-greedy/balanced extraction or try the whole trimmed text first, wrap JSON.parse in try/catch returning null with a distinct log line ('haiku returned unparseable JSON: <first 120 chars>'), and do the same in localRoute. Returning null instead of throwing also lets the pref=haiku path keep its documented degrade-to-rules semantics while making the cause visible.
Expected improvement
Parse regressions become diagnosable from logs instead of blending into network-failure noise; multi-brace Haiku responses that contain a valid leading object still route instead of falling back.
Evidence
const m = text.match(/\{[\s\S]*\}/);
if (!m) return null;
return validateRouted(JSON.parse(m[0]) as RoutedJson, "haiku");
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read lib/router.ts lines 88-125 and 900-1014. Verified: (1) haikuRoute lines 936-938 match the evidence verbatim — greedy `text.match(/\{[\s\S]*\}/)` followed by unguarded `JSON.parse(m[0])`; (2) localRoute line 1013 has unguarded `JSON.parse(text)` with `num_predict: 200` at line 1002 (truncation risk is real despite the comment at lines 944-945 claiming 'parsing never fails' — the `format` grammar constrains tokens, not truncation); (3) the only catches are `.catch(engineFail("haiku"|"local"))` at lines 97, 101, 110, 113. One correction to the description: the 'indistinguishable from network failures' claim is overstated — engineFail (line 122) appends `${e}` to the log line, so a parse failure logs 'SyntaxError: Unexpected token ...' while an HTTP failure logs 'Error: haiku 429' and a timeout logs a TimeoutError; the prefix is identical but the error text differentiates the cause. What's genuinely missing is the offending raw model output (nothing shows WHAT Haiku returned), which is the real diagnosability gap the fix addresses. Also, the pref=haiku 'drops straight to rules' behavior applies to ANY failure in that mode by design (line 98), not specially to parse failures. Core finding stands; severity low is right.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read lib/router.ts lines 85-125 and 880-1014. Code facts confirmed: greedy /\{[\s\S]*\}/ + unguarded JSON.parse at lines 936-938 (haikuRoute), unguarded JSON.parse(text) at line 1013 (localRoute) with num_predict:200 making the line-945 comment "parsing never fails" not strictly true under truncation. All callers catch via engineFail, so nothing crashes and fallback works. CORRECTION that lowers severity: the central "why it matters" claim is wrong — engineFail logs `${e}`, so a parse failure appears as "SyntaxError: ..." while HTTP/timeout failures appear as "Error: haiku 4xx"/"TimeoutError"; the causes ARE distinguishable in logs, contrary to the finding. The pref=haiku drop-to-rules path is the documented preference semantics, not a defect. What remains is a minor robustness nit (greedy match can discard a recoverable response containing a valid object plus trailing braced prose; a truncated-JSON snippet isn't logged) with safe degradation and adequate diagnostics — info, not low.

AudioMeter runs an uncapped requestAnimationFrame loop at full display refresh even when idle

components/panels/AudioMeter.tsx:18-31 · reviewer: bugs-frontend
What it is
The VU-meter effect starts a rAF loop that runs continuously for as long as the Today tab is mounted, at the display's native refresh (120Hz on ProMotion), including in idle standby where `raw` is null and `smooth` has long converged to 0 — it still calls levelToBars and writes 37 `--h` custom properties every frame. This sits on the same page as GraphCore, whose own loop is deliberately capped to 30fps with a comment explaining that an uncapped loop on an always-open HUD "cooks the GPU"; the meter ignores both that cap and the document.hidden early-out.
Why it matters
The HUD is designed to stay open all day; a 120Hz style-write loop doing nothing visible in the idle state is sustained wasted main-thread and style/recalc work on battery.
How to fix
Skip the per-bar style writes once smooth is ~0 and the target is 0 (idle short-circuit), and/or apply the same frame-interval cap (24-30fps) and document.hidden guard GraphCore uses; alternatively only run the loop while mode is speaking/listening (the effect already re-runs on mode change).
Expected improvement
Removes constant 120Hz layout/style churn while the HUD idles, matching the power posture GraphCore already established.
Evidence
`const loop = () => { raf = requestAnimationFrame(loop); const raw = mode === "speaking" ? voice.getLevel() : ... : null; const target = raw ?? 0; ... for (let i = 0; i < heights.length; i++) barsRef.current[i]?.style.setProperty("--h", ...) };` — no frame cap, no hidden check, no idle short-circuit.

Chat page message array grows unbounded within a session with full-list re-render

app/chat/page.tsx:22, 98-103 · reviewer: bugs-frontend
What it is
The chat thread keeps every message of the rolling per-device thread in a single state array with no cap, and every send re-renders the entire list (index keys, no virtualization). The shell feed by contrast is capped at 30 lines (Shell.tsx slice(-30)). Because the thread persists via localStorage threadId and is only reset by the New button, a long-lived thread accumulates for the whole session. The in-file ponytail comment already acknowledges deferred rendering work ("no markdown renderer... no token streaming yet").
Why it matters
For a single-user tool this is acceptable today, but a multi-week rolling thread on the always-open HUD will slowly grow render cost per message; recording it so it's a known deferral like the other ponytail items.
How to fix
No action strictly needed now; if it bites, cap the rendered window (e.g. last 200 messages) or memoize message rows with stable keys.
Expected improvement
Bounded render cost for long chat sessions.
Evidence
`const [messages, setMessages] = useState<Msg[]>([]); ... {messages.map((m, i) => (<div key={i} className={`msg ${m.role}`}>` — no slice/cap anywhere in the file.

Model allowlist triplicated across lib/chat.ts, runner/runner.js, and lib/modelOverride.ts with no contract test guarding drift

lib/chat.ts:13-18 · reviewer: dedup-simplify
What it is
The set of four allowed Claude model ids exists in three files: lib/chat.ts MODEL_ALLOWLIST (lines 13-18, commented 'Mirror of runner.js MODEL_ALLOWLIST'), runner/runner.js MODEL_ALLOWLIST (lines 112-117), and lib/modelOverride.ts MODEL_PHRASES ids (lines 11-16). The modelFor() validator is also duplicated verbatim: lib/chat.ts lines 53-55 and runner/runner.js lines 119-122 are the same three lines. Unlike the ADR-0007 skills triplication, which scripts/test-tabs.ts and test-skill-contract.ts assert stays in sync, nothing asserts these three lists match — grep of scripts/test-*.ts finds no MODEL_ALLOWLIST or MODEL_PHRASES assertion (test-chat.ts only checks two ids pass through modelFor, and test-capture.ts only exercises phrase extraction).
Why it matters
This is exactly the coupling class the repo's own ADR-0007 exists to guard, but without the guard. If a model id is added or renamed in lib/modelOverride.ts (the spoken 'use opus' path) but not in runner/runner.js, the runner's modelFor() silently falls back to CLAUDE_MODEL — the user hears 'running this one on Opus' while the run executes on the default model, with no error anywhere. Same silent-downgrade for chat if lib/chat.ts drifts. The runner comment calls its re-validation 'defense in depth', which makes the drift mode quiet by design.
How to fix
Define the allowlist once in a dependency-free module the runner can import (runner.js already imports from lib-adjacent JS like runner/env.js; alternatively keep the copies but add an assertion to scripts/test-skill-contract.ts — it already imports runner/runner.js, which exports nothing for this today, so export MODEL_ALLOWLIST from runner.js and assert it equals lib/chat.ts MODEL_ALLOWLIST and the set of MODEL_PHRASES ids in lib/modelOverride.ts).
Expected improvement
A model-id rename or addition that misses one of the three copies turns npm test red instead of silently running voice/chat asks on the wrong model.
Evidence
lib/chat.ts: '// Mirror of runner.js MODEL_ALLOWLIST … export const MODEL_ALLOWLIST = new Set(["claude-sonnet-4-6", "claude-opus-4-8", …])'; runner/runner.js:112 'const MODEL_ALLOWLIST = new Set(["claude-opus-4-8", …])'; lib/modelOverride.ts:11 'const MODEL_PHRASES: Record<string,…> = { opus: { id: "claude-opus-4-8", … } }'; identical modelFor(): 'return typeof m === "string" && MODEL_ALLOWLIST.has(m) ? m : DEFAULT_MODEL;' (chat.ts:54) vs '…: CLAUDE_MODEL;' (runner.js:121)

fleet.js METRIC_SOURCE mirrors the feeds' SOURCE constants unguarded — a renamed source makes the watchdog silently stop watching that feed

runner/fleet.js:28-33 · reviewer: contract-drift
What it is
runner/fleet.js:28 hardcodes METRIC_SOURCE = { 'uscf-feed': 'uscf', 'tokens-feed': 'claude_code', 'jobs-feed': 'jobs', 'morphy-github-feed': 'github' }, mirroring the SOURCE constants in feeds/uscf-rating.py:41 ('uscf'), feeds/claude-tokens.py:42 ('claude_code'), feeds/job-applications.py:46 ('jobs'), feeds/morphy-github.py:64 ('github'). Currently in sync, but nothing tests the pair, and fleet.js:154-158 deliberately treats 'a source with no rows EVER' as unconfigured and skips it (stale = ts !== null && ...). So if a feed's SOURCE string is renamed (or a new feed's fleet entry uses the wrong string), the watchdog sees zero rows for the old name and — by design — never flags it: the feed silently leaves fleet coverage, forever green.
Why it matters
The fleet watchdog (issue #58) exists specifically to catch producers that quietly stop writing. This unguarded mirror combined with the intentional 'no rows = unconfigured, skip' rule means the failure mode of drift is the watchdog itself going blind for that producer — the worst place for a silent coupling in this codebase.
How to fix
Add a scripts/test-fleet.ts (or test-skill-contract.ts) check that regex-extracts SOURCE = "..." from each feeds/*.py and asserts every METRIC_SOURCE value in runner/fleet.js matches its feed's constant — same source-literal technique the HUD_TZ contract check already uses.
Expected improvement
Renaming a metrics source turns npm test red instead of permanently removing that feed from watchdog coverage.
Evidence
runner/fleet.js:28-33: METRIC_SOURCE = { 'uscf-feed': 'uscf', 'tokens-feed': 'claude_code', ... }; feeds/uscf-rating.py:41: SOURCE = "uscf"; fleet.js:154-155 comment: "A source with no rows EVER is unconfigured ... not broken — skip it."
Verifier notes (2)

The skip rule is real: fleet.js:153-155 comment ("A source with no rows EVER is unconfigured ... not broken — skip it") and line 158 `const stale = ts !== null && ...`, so a renamed/mismatched source string yields ts===null forever and the producer stays permanently green. No guard exists: scripts/test-fleet.ts is pure-fixture only — its metricsRows (lines 31-36) hardcode the same source strings independently, never reading feeds/*.py, so a feed SOURCE rename passes every test while blinding the watchdog. grep found no other cross-check of METRIC_SOURCE anywhere (only reference is fleet.js itself). Minor line correction: the skip-rule evidence spans 153-158 (comment 153-155, logic 156-158), not 154-158 — immaterial. Not a duplicate of the pre-publication review era (fleet.js is issue #58, shipped 2026-07-05, after that review) and not covered by the excluded follow-ups. Proposed fix (source-literal regex extraction like the HUD_TZ contract check in test-skill-contract.ts) is apt. One material correction to the failure scenario: metrics.csv is append-only (no pruning in feeds/_metrics.py), so RENAMING an existing feed's SOURCE leaves old rows under the old name — the watchdog would then go loudly, permanently stale (red dot, one kick) rather than silently green. The truly silent forever-green case is narrower: a NEW feed whose METRIC_SOURCE entry uses a wrong string (zero rows ever under that name), or a rename on a fresh vault with no historical rows. So the finding is real but its headline scenario is half-wrong; the silent-blind window exists only for the new-feed/fresh-vault case. Severity low stands (personal single-user project, four constants, ADR-0007 shows the owner's own convention is to contract-test exactly this kind of triplicated literal — this pair just wasn't covered). scripts/queue-intent.mjs re-implements writeIntent() without the atomic write the shared contract requires

scripts/queue-intent.mjs:44-46 · reviewer: dedup-simplify
What it is
queue-intent.mjs (the launchd weekly-review scheduler) duplicates lib/skills.ts writeIntent(): same intent shape, same queue dir, but it writes with a plain writeFileSync(join(queueDir, `${id}.json`), …) — no temp-then-rename. lib/skills.ts:36-38 documents the atomic write as load-bearing: 'atomic: the runner fs.watch()es this dir and must never see a torn intent (the temp name fails the runner's UUID_JSON_RE, so it's invisible to it)'. The script's own header says it 'Writes the SAME intent shape the HUD's writeIntent() (lib/skills.ts) and /api/queue produce', but the atomicity half of that contract was dropped in the copy.
Why it matters
This is drift inside an explicitly documented duplicated contract. In practice the runner tolerates it (processOne retries the read with backoff and pickNext has POISON_SKIPS), so a torn read costs a delay at worst — but the divergence means one of the two write paths violates the invariant the other one documents as mandatory, and the mitigating retry machinery is the only thing between a launchd-scheduled weekly-review and a dead-lettered intent.
How to fix
Write to `${id}.json.tmp` (or any non-UUID name) and renameSync into place, mirroring lib/atomicWrite.ts / runner writeJson — a two-line change. Longer term the script could share runner/writeJson (runner.js already exports it), which it can import the same way it imports runner/env.js.
Expected improvement
Both intent writers honor the same torn-read invariant; the documented contract stops being half-true.
Evidence
