Two parallel round-for-speech implementations: spokenNum() in lib/router.ts and spokenRound() in lib/spokenText.ts

lib/router.ts:369-379 · reviewer: dedup-simplify
What it is
lib/router.ts:369-379 defines spokenNum() ('N thousand' / 'N[.n] million' rounding for spoken replies) and lib/spokenText.ts:46-51 defines spokenRound() with the same job and nearly the same math (both round >=1000 to whole thousands, both produce one-decimal millions). They differ subtly: spokenRound has the 999_500 boundary guard ('or it reads "1000 thousand"') while spokenNum does not — spokenNum(999_600) yields '1000 thousand', the exact bug spokenText already fixed. Every router reply also passes through normalizeForSpeech() in lib/tts.ts speak() (line 46), which re-rounds bare 4+-digit counts via spokenRound, so router replies are effectively rounded by both implementations in sequence.
Why it matters
Same concern, two implementations, one already carries a boundary fix the other lacks. A weekDelta of ~999,600 (unlikely for these metrics, but the code path is generic) speaks as 'up about 1000 thousand this week'. More practically, future TTS-flow tweaks (like the 999_500 fix) have to be discovered and applied twice.
How to fix
Export spokenRound from lib/spokenText.ts (it's the more correct of the two) and have lib/router.ts spokenNum delegate to it, or delete spokenNum and use spokenRound directly in weekDelta()/briefing().
Expected improvement
One rounding rule for everything spoken; the 999_500 boundary fix applies to router replies too.
Evidence
router.ts:377 'if (x >= 1_000) return `${Math.round(x / 1000)} thousand`;' vs spokenText.ts:49 'if (n < 999_500) return `${Math.round(n / 1_000)} thousand`; // 999,500+ belongs to the million branch or it reads "1000 thousand"'
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read lib/router.ts:365-394, lib/spokenText.ts:36-89, and lib/tts.ts:1,46. Confirmed: spokenNum() (router.ts:369-379) and spokenRound() (spokenText.ts:46-51) both implement round-for-speech with nearly identical math; only spokenRound has the 999_500 boundary guard, so spokenNum(999_600) does yield "1000 thousand" (x=999,600 < 1,000,000 falls to the thousand branch at line 377). tts.ts:46 confirms speak() runs every reply through normalizeForSpeech, whose bare-count rule (spokenText.ts:82-86) re-rounds 4+-digit numbers via spokenRound. Two corrections/refinements: (1) the "rounded by both implementations in sequence" claim is slightly overstated for normal values — spokenNum's output ("14 thousand") contains no 4+-digit runs, so the second pass is a no-op except in the boundary-bug case, where "1000 thousand" WOULD be re-matched (1000 is 4 digits, not in the 1900-2099 year range) and becomes "1 thousand thousand" — the layering compounds rather than masks the bug; (2) minor difference the finding glosses: spokenNum rounds millions >=10 to whole numbers while spokenRound always keeps one decimal, and spokenRound uses numWords() for <1000 while spokenNum returns digits — a pure delegation would slightly change output register, so the fix needs a small adaptation, not a drop-in. Not a duplicate of any excluded/known item. Severity low is right — the failure value (~999.6k weekDelta) is implausible for these metrics; the real cost is the maintenance duplication.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read lib/router.ts:365-395, lib/spokenText.ts (whole file), lib/tts.ts:45-46, and grepped all references. Confirmed: spokenNum() (router.ts:369-379) and spokenRound() (spokenText.ts:46-51) do the same rounding job; spokenRound has the 999_500 boundary guard, spokenNum does not, so spokenNum(999_600) yields '1000 thousand'. spokenNum's only caller is weekDelta() (router.ts:393-394); spokenRound is module-private. No test pins spokenNum's boundary. Two corrections to the description: (1) 'router replies are effectively rounded by both implementations in sequence' overstates it — normalizeForSpeech's bare-count regex only matches 4+ digit numbers, and spokenNum's normal outputs ('14 thousand', '1.4 million') contain no 4+-digit runs, so the second pass is a no-op except in the bug case, where '1000 thousand' becomes '1 thousand thousand' (arguably funnier, still wrong). (2) The two functions differ in output register — spokenRound emits digit-form ('4 thousand', relying on downstream digit reading) while spokenNum emits digits too, but spokenRound's sub-1000 branch returns numWords; a straight delegate from spokenNum would change sub-1000 replies from digits to words, so the proposed fix needs a small adjustment (delegate only the >=1000 path or export and adapt). Materiality: a weekly delta near a million is implausible for these vault metrics, so this is a code-hygiene/duplication finding, not a live bug — low severity is right.
lowConfirmed etl effort: small

.env parser drift across the three keep-in-sync loaders: feeds/_metrics.py accepts uppercase keys only

feeds/_metrics.py:28 · reviewer: dedup-simplify
What it is
The ~/.claude/.env loader exists in three languages with comments demanding sync: lib/homeEnv.ts ('keep the accepted-key rule in sync or a key works for the runner and is invisible to the HUD'), runner/env.js (same warning), and feeds/_metrics.py load_home_env ('Mirror the runner/HUD loader'). Their accepted-key rules already differ: homeEnv.ts matches keys against [A-Za-z0-9_]+ (mixed case OK), env.js accepts literally anything left of the first '=' (line.slice(0, idx).trim() — even keys with spaces), and _metrics.py matches [A-Z0-9_]+ only, so any key containing a lowercase letter is silently invisible to every Python feed while working in the HUD and runner.
Why it matters
This is the precise failure the sibling comments warn about, already latent: a user who writes e.g. 'Vault_Root=' or a mixed-case custom knob into ~/.claude/.env gets it honored by the HUD and runner but ignored by uscf-rating/claude-tokens/job-applications/morphy-github/calendar-agenda, with no error — the feeds just fall back to defaults or exit. Debugging 'the feed ignores my .env line but the HUD sees it' is exactly the class of quiet drift the comments were written to prevent, and nothing tests the three parsers against a common fixture.
How to fix
Align the regexes (make _metrics.py use [A-Za-z0-9_]+ and constrain env.js keys to the same pattern), and add a tiny shared fixture test: scripts/run-tests.mjs already runs both TS and Python suites, so feed a canned .env text through parseEnvText (runner/env.js exports it), the homeEnv regex, and load_home_env, asserting identical key/value results.
Expected improvement
One accepted-key rule across HUD, runner, and feeds; a future rule change that misses one loader fails tests instead of silently splitting config visibility by process.
Evidence
feeds/_metrics.py:28 're.match(r"^\s*([A-Z0-9_]+)\s*=\s*(.*)\s*$", line)' vs lib/homeEnv.ts:21 'line.match(/^\s*([A-Za-z0-9_]+)\s*=\s*(.*)\s*$/)' vs runner/env.js:16-17 'const idx = line.indexOf("="); out[line.slice(0, idx).trim()] = …' — three different key rules under 'keep the accepted-key rule … in sync' comments.
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Verified all three loaders in current code. feeds/_metrics.py:28 uses [A-Z0-9_]+ (uppercase-only), lib/homeEnv.ts:21 uses [A-Za-z0-9_]+ (mixed case), runner/env.js:16-17 accepts any key left of the first '=' (after skipping blank/# lines). The cited evidence is real and in context; homeEnv.ts lines 8-10 and env.js lines 3-5 both carry explicit keep-in-sync comments, and env.js's comment ("any KEY=value line") already contradicts homeEnv.ts's actual regex. No test covers parser parity. Corrections: _metrics.py's comment says "Mirror the runner/HUD loader" (docstring, line 24), not a literal keep-in-sync warning; practical impact is limited since all keys HELM actually uses are uppercase, so low severity is appropriate. Additional same-class drift not in the finding: env.js explicitly skips # comment lines and accepts keys containing spaces, which the other two reject via regex. Not a duplicate of the excluded #36-#44 era findings (this code postdates that consolidation — _metrics.py was itself the issue #42 dedup) and not covered by open issue #2 or the two tracked follow-ups.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Verified all three loaders: feeds/_metrics.py:28 uses [A-Z0-9_]+ (uppercase-only), lib/homeEnv.ts:21 uses [A-Za-z0-9_]+, runner/env.js:16-17 accepts any non-empty left-of-'=' key; the keep-in-sync comments exist as quoted. Corrections: (1) the claim that nothing tests the parsers is wrong — scripts/test-runner.ts:259-273 fixture-tests parseEnvText (including a mixed_Case key) and asserts homeEnv.ts's regex accepts mixed case, so the runner/HUD pair IS contract-tested; _metrics.py is the only loader outside that test, and it violates the tested mixed-case contract. Not a duplicate of the #36-#44 era (issue #42 created _metrics.py; this gap postdates it). Severity low is correct — real drift against a tested contract, no currently reachable failure.

runner/runner.js builds the 13-field run-record object by hand in four places

runner/runner.js:480-493 · reviewer: dedup-simplify
What it is
The run-record shape { id, skill, args, ts_queued, ts_started, ts_completed, status, exit_code, summary, md_path, log_path, deliverable_path } is constructed as a fresh object literal in four spots: retireClaim() (lines 480-493), the bad-intent-JSON dead-letter path in processOne() (lines 545-558), the initial 'running' status in processOne() (lines 598-611), and processNative() (lines 1099-1112). All four repeat the md_path/log_path pair (`system/runs/${runId}.md` twice — log_path always equals md_path) and differ only in status/exit_code/summary.
Why it matters
Adding or renaming a run-record field (the HUD's readRecentRuns in lib/vault.ts parses this shape) means touching four literals; missing one produces run JSONs with inconsistent schemas that the HUD's defensive String(j.x ?? …) casts will paper over silently rather than surface. How to fix
Add a small factory, e.g. runRecord(runId, intent, overrides) returning the base object with md_path/log_path derived once, and have retireClaim, the dead-letter path, processOne, and processNative spread their per-case fields over it.

CHAT_SYSTEM hand-restates the writeIntent JSON shape as frozen prose with no field-level contract test, and the LLM's file write is non-atomic

lib/chat.ts:46-48 · reviewer: intent-json-contract
What it is
The comment above the queue instruction claims 'Same contract as the deck buttons and voice (lib/skills.ts writeIntent)', but the contract is duplicated as a literal JSON template inside a prompt string rather than derived from writeIntent. If writeIntent's shape evolves (a new field, a changed source taxonomy, a retry marker), the prose template drifts silently: test-skill-contract.ts only checks that each CHAT_SKILLS name appears in CHAT_SYSTEM (line 145) and that the string 'system/queue/' is present (line 148) — no assertion on the field set (id/skill/args/ts/source). Separately, writeIntent uses atomicWriteFileSync specifically because 'the runner fs.watch()es this dir and must never see a torn intent' (lib/skills.ts:36-37), but the chat LLM writes the final path directly with its Write tool — non-atomic, relying on the runner's mitigations (POISON_SKIPS=10 in pickNext, 5x150ms read retries in processOne) that exist for slow flushes, not as a sanctioned write mode. The intent shape today happens to match writeIntent exactly (id, skill, args, ts, source; retry omitted → runner defaults `(intent.retry || 0)` handle it), so this is drift risk, not current breakage.
Why it matters
This repo's own ADR-0007 pattern is that every intentionally duplicated list gets a contract test; the intent JSON shape is triplicated (writeIntent, queue-intent.mjs, CHAT_SYSTEM prose) and only the first two are structurally identical by construction. The prose copy is the one a future edit to writeIntent will forget, and the failure mode is a chat-queued intent the runner dead-letters (or half-parses) with no test turning red.
How to fix
Generate the template in CHAT_SYSTEM from a single shared constant (e.g. export an INTENT_FIELDS example object from lib/skills.ts and JSON.stringify it into the prompt), or add a test-skill-contract.ts assertion that CHAT_SYSTEM's embedded JSON template parses and its key set equals the keys writeIntent produces. (Fixing the finding above by moving the write into the route makes this moot — writeIntent becomes the only writer.)
Expected improvement
Shape changes to writeIntent fail the contract suite instead of silently orphaning the chat dispatch path; the torn-write exception disappears.
Evidence
lib/chat.ts:46-47 comment: 'Same contract as the deck buttons and voice (lib/skills.ts writeIntent)'; lib/chat.ts:48 hand-written template '{"id": "<that same uuid>", "skill": "<name>", "args": {}, "ts": "<current UTC time, ISO-8601>", "source": "chat"}'; scripts/test-skill-contract.ts:148 only checks `CHAT_SYSTEM.includes("system/queue/")`.

(2) test-skill-contract.ts section 6 (lines 140-152) only asserts each CHAT_SKILLS name appears in CHAT_SYSTEM (line 145) and that CHAT_SYSTEM.includes("system/queue/") (line 148) — there is no assertion on the field set or that the embedded template parses/matches writeIntent's keys. (3) writeIntent (lib/skills.ts:27-40) uses atomicWriteFileSync with the exact cited comment at lines 36-37 ('the runner fs.watch()es this dir and must never see a torn intent'), while CHAT_SYSTEM instructs the chat LLM to write the final system/queue/<uuid>.json path directly (non-atomic Write). run-tests.mjs hardcodes the suite lists — an unregistered test file silently never runs, locally or in CI

scripts/run-tests.mjs:9-20 · reviewer: tests
What it is
TS_SUITES (20 entries) and PY_SUITES (6 entries) are maintained by hand. Today they exactly match the on-disk files (verified: all 20 scripts/test-*.ts and all 5 feeds/test_*.py plus voice-server/test_server.py are listed), but nothing asserts the lists match a glob. A new scripts/test-foo.ts or feeds/test_bar.py that the author forgets to register is never executed by npm test or CI, with no FAIL, no SKIP line, no signal at all — the summary just reports one fewer suite than anyone realizes.
Why it matters
This is the classic silent-skip failure mode: the suite that guards a new feature can rot (or never run once) while the '29/29 suites passed' banner looks healthy. Every other drift risk in this repo (skills, tabs, plists) has a contract test; the test registry itself does not.
How to fix
Either glob the suites (readdirSync('scripts').filter(f => /^test-.*\.ts$/) and same for feeds/test_*.py) instead of hardcoding, or keep the explicit list and add a startup assertion that it set-equals the glob, failing the run on any unregistered file.
Expected improvement
A test file that exists but never runs becomes impossible; the registry can no longer drift from the filesystem.
Evidence
const TS_SUITES = ["test-security", "test-todos", … ]; …PY_SUITES = ["voice-server/test_server.py", …] — plain string arrays, no readdir anywhere in the file
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read scripts/run-tests.mjs in full: TS_SUITES (lines 9-15) and PY_SUITES (lines 16-20) are hardcoded string arrays; the only import is spawnSync — no readdir/glob anywhere, and no assertion that the lists match the filesystem. Cited line range 9-20 is exact. Verified the counts by listing files: exactly 20 scripts/test-*.ts, 5 feeds/test_*.py, and voice-server/test_server.py exist, and all 26 are registered — so the lists are currently in sync, as the finding itself states. The defect is the mechanism: a new scripts/test-foo.ts or feeds/test_bar.py that isn't hand-added never runs, and the "N/N suites passed" summary (line 36) counts only registered suites, so there is no FAIL/SKIP signal. Not covered by the KNOWN/EXCLUDED list (not a doc-polish item, not one of the two tracked follow-ups) and doesn't collide with the ADR-0007 contract tests, which guard skill-list drift, not the test registry. Severity low is right — latent risk, no current breakage. The proposed fix (glob, or startup set-equality assertion) is apt; note NODE_CHECKS (line 8) has the same hand-maintained property for runner/*.js syntax checks, though globbing runner/ is less clean since not every .js there may warrant a check.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read scripts/run-tests.mjs in full (41 lines), globbed the actual test files, and checked .github/workflows/ci.yml. Confirmed: TS_SUITES (lines 9-15) and PY_SUITES (lines 16-20) are hand-maintained string arrays with no readdir/glob anywhere in the file, and CI runs only `npm test` (which invokes this script), so an unregistered scripts/test-*.ts or feeds/test_*.py would silently never run locally or in CI. Found no mitigation elsewhere — no contract test asserts registry-vs-glob parity, unlike the skills/tabs lists which are guarded by test-tabs.ts/test-skill-contract.ts, making the finding's "the test registry itself has no contract test" point accurate. Line range 9-20 is correct. Proposed fix (glob, or assert set-equality with the glob at startup) is sound; a pure glob is slightly simpler and cannot drift. Severity low is appropriate: no current breakage, purely a future silent-skip risk in a single-maintainer repo, but the failure mode is genuinely invisible (summary just shows one fewer suite). Not a duplicate of any excluded/known item.

test-runner's homeEnv 'kept in sync' assertion is a substring grep that cannot detect real parser divergence

scripts/test-runner.ts:270-274 · reviewer: tests
What it is
After behaviorally testing runner/env.js's parseEnvText with six fixture lines, the suite 'verifies' the HUD-side sibling lib/homeEnv.ts stays in sync by asserting the raw source contains the substring "[A-Za-z0-9_]". This passes as long as that character class appears anywhere in the file, for any purpose — it says nothing about quote-stripping, comment handling, trimming, or =-splitting, all of which the runner-side parser is actually tested for. The two parsers could diverge on five of the six tested behaviors and this check stays green, so the PASS line ('rule kept in sync') overstates what is guaranteed.
Why it matters
Both sides read the same ~/.claude/.env; divergence means the HUD and runner resolve different values for HELM_API_KEY or HUD_TZ — the exact 'today splits across two dates' / auth-mismatch class the rest of the suite works hard to prevent. A check that can't fail provides false assurance precisely where the coupling is documented as load-bearing.
How to fix
Extract the line-parsing core of lib/homeEnv.ts into an exported pure function (or export a testable parse from it) and run the identical fixture text through both parsers in this test, asserting equal output — the same pattern already used for parseEnvText.
Expected improvement
The sync claim becomes behaviorally verified; any divergence between the HUD and runner env parsers turns npm test red instead of surfacing as a mysterious auth/timezone mismatch at runtime.
Evidence
const homeEnvSrc = readFileSync(new URL("../lib/homeEnv.ts", …), "utf8"); check(homeEnvSrc.includes("[A-Za-z0-9_]"), "lib/homeEnv.ts accepts the same mixed-case keys as runner/env.js (rule kept in sync)");
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read scripts/test-runner.ts lines 230-289, lib/homeEnv.ts (whole file), and runner/env.js (whole file). The finding is accurate and the cited lines are correct: lines 270-274 of test-runner.ts do exactly `check(homeEnvSrc.includes("[A-Za-z0-9_]"), "...rule kept in sync")` after behaviorally testing runner/env.js's parseEnvText on six fixture lines (lines 260-269). The substring grep only proves that character class appears somewhere in homeEnv.ts source; it verifies none of the other tested behaviors (comment skipping, quote stripping, trimming, no-equals skipping). Not a duplicate of the excluded known items — issue #44 unified the runner-side loader, but this weak sync check is current code. Two corroborating details that strengthen the finding: (1) the parsers already diverge subtly today — env.js trims the value before quote-stripping (`.trim().replace(/^["']|["']$/g,"")`), while homeEnv.ts uses regex `^\s*([A-Za-z0-9_]+)\s*=\s*(.*)\s*$` where the greedy `(.*)` captures trailing whitespace (the `\s*$` matches empty), so a line like `QUOTED="q v" ` (trailing space) parses differently on the two sides — and the grep check stays green; (2) env.js accepts any key text before the first `=` (e.g. keys with dots or spaces), while homeEnv only accepts `[A-Za-z0-9_]+` keys — another undetectable divergence. The proposed fix (export a pure parse from lib/homeEnv.ts and run identical fixtures through both) is sound; note the test file is TS run under the TS test harness, so importing lib/homeEnv.ts directly is feasible. Severity low is appropriate for a testing-assurance gap.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read scripts/test-runner.ts (lines 257-274), lib/homeEnv.ts, runner/env.js, and grepped for other homeEnv coverage (none behavioral). Confirmed: the "kept in sync" assertion is a raw-source substring grep for "[A-Za-z0-9_]" that cannot detect parser divergence on quoting/trimming/comment/=-split behavior — the five behaviors the runner-side parser is behaviorally tested for. Correction strengthening the finding: the two parsers ALREADY diverge and the check stays green — homeEnv.ts's regex ^\s*([A-Za-z0-9_]+)\s*=\s*(.*)\s*$ captures trailing whitespace into the value (greedy .*) and strips quotes without trimming, so HELM_API_KEY="abc" with a trailing space parses as `abc` in the runner but `abc" ` in the HUD; and env.js accepts keys like MY-KEY that homeEnv.ts silently drops. Both files' own comments document this exact "works for runner, invisible to HUD" risk, so it's a testing gap, not intentional design. Proposed fix (shared fixture through an exported pure parse from homeEnv.ts) is correct; compare only the line-parse cores since homeEnv.ts additionally applies process.env-wins precedence. Not a duplicate of the excluded #36-#44 findings — line 270-274 is the current code shipped BY the issue-#44 fix. Severity low is appropriate given single-user scope and a typically well-formed .env.

What it is

Why it matters

How to fix
Add a `- run: npx next build` step (the existing `VAULT_ROOT: ${{ github.workspace }}/demo-vault` env already satisfies config.ts's import-time check, same trick the Dockerfile uses).
Expected improvement
PRs that break the production build fail in CI instead of at deploy.

test_morphy_github.py exercises only the pure compute layer — fetch_json error mapping, fetch_list pagination, and resolve_token are untested

feeds/test_morphy_github.py:54-125 · reviewer: unswept-feeds
What it is
The morphy test sweep covers count_recent_commits/count_open_issues/count_open_prs/github_stats plus the shared CSV write, but nothing above the pure layer: fetch_json's HTTPError branch mapping (404 vs 401/403 vs other), fetch_list's page-walking, short-page termination, non-list rejection, and the MAX_PAGES for/else truncation branch (the only nontrivial control flow in the fetch half of the file, ~70 lines) have zero coverage, and none of it needs a network — fetch_list could take an injected fetcher or be tested via a patched fetch_json returning canned pages. By comparison, test_uscf_rating.py does test its feed's failure paths (three `raises(...)` cases), but uscf's fetch half is trivial; morphy's is not. The MORPHY_REPO no-op/format-validation branches in main() (lines 223-230) are likewise untested.
Why it matters
The pagination for/else and the error-code mapping are exactly the code that changes when the GitHub API surprises you, and a regression there (e.g. an infinite-loop or a swallowed non-list response) would not fail `npm test` — it would only show up as a hung or silently wrong launchd job in production. ADR-0008's premise is that feed transforms are 'tested with canned fixtures'; here the fixtures stop one layer below where the fragility lives.
How to fix
Parameterize fetch_list on its fetch function (default fetch_json) and add sweep cases: two full pages then a short page concatenates correctly; a non-list payload raises; MAX_PAGES full pages triggers the truncation branch. Monkeypatching mg.fetch_json on the loaded module object works without any refactor. Optionally assert the 404/401/403 RuntimeError messages by feeding fetch_json a stubbed urlopen raising HTTPError.
Expected improvement
The GitHub-facing half of the feed gets the same fixture coverage as its pure half, so pagination/error-contract regressions fail in `npm test` instead of in a launchd log.
Evidence
# --- commits: only those inside the 7-day window count -------------------------
...

(no test invokes mg.fetch_json, mg.fetch_list, mg.resolve_token, or mg.main)

install-launchd.sh never creates the gitignored logs/ directory the plists' StandardOutPath points into

scripts/install-launchd.sh:8-17 · reviewer: deploy-infra
What it is
Every com.helm.*.plist template sets StandardOutPath/StandardErrorPath to `__HELM_ROOT__/logs/<name>.log`, but `logs/` is gitignored (`.gitignore` line 10: `logs/`) so it does not exist on a fresh clone, and install-launchd.sh only does `mkdir -p "$AGENTS"` — it never creates `$ROOT/logs`. launchd does not create intermediate directories for StandardOutPath: on a checkout without `logs/`, the bootstrapped agents either fail to spawn or run with their output discarded, depending on macOS version. Either way the failure is invisible — install-launchd.sh prints `installed <label>` for each agent regardless.
Why it matters
This bites exactly the audience a public repo targets: someone (or Daniel on a new machine) cloning and running the documented installer. The runner 'fails silently on syntax errors (stale heartbeat, no log)' per CLAUDE.md — losing its log file on top of that removes the only diagnostic channel, and the watchdog's own log (logs/watchdog.log) is lost the same way.
How to fix
Add `mkdir -p "$ROOT/logs"` next to the existing `mkdir -p "$AGENTS"` in install-launchd.sh.
Expected improvement
launchd agents installed from a fresh clone start reliably and their logs land where every plist and doc says they will.
Evidence
install-launchd.sh line 9: `mkdir -p "$AGENTS"` (the only mkdir). com.helm.hud.plist lines 32-35: `<key>StandardOutPath</key><string>__HELM_ROOT__/logs/hud.log</string>`. .gitignore line 10: `logs/`.
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read scripts/install-launchd.sh (19 lines): line 9 `mkdir -p "$AGENTS"` is the only mkdir in the script (loop is lines 11-19, not 8-17 as cited — minor line offset). The dir exists on Daniel's machine only as an untracked runtime artifact, so a fresh clone hits it. One nuance: on modern macOS, launchd typically still spawns the job when the StandardOutPath parent is missing and silently discards output (logging only to the system log) rather than failing to spawn — the finding hedges on this correctly, and the discarded-output case is the worse failure mode anyway given the runner's documented silent-failure behavior. Proposed one-line fix (`mkdir -p "$ROOT/logs"`) is correct. Severity medium is appropriate: fresh-clone/new-machine only, but it silently removes the sole diagnostic channel for all 11 agents including the watchdog.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Confirmed. Feed plist templates hardcode /usr/local/bin/python3 while other templates use /opt/homebrew paths — a fresh Apple Silicon install gets four feeds that never run, masked by the watchdog's no-rows rule

scripts/com.helm.uscf.plist:9-11 · reviewer: contract-drift
What it is
The four metric-feed templates (com.helm.uscf/tokens/jobs/morphy.plist) invoke /usr/local/bin/python3 — the python.org framework installer path — while com.helm.morning/plan/weekly/distill use /opt/homebrew/bin/node and com.helm.voice uses the repo venv's python. install-launchd.sh only substitutes __HELM_ROOT__/__HOME__; it does not resolve interpreters. On this machine /usr/local/bin/python3 happens to exist (a python.org 3.11 symlink), but on a stock Apple Silicon Mac with only Homebrew python (/opt/homebrew/bin/python3) it does not, so launchd fails to exec all four feed jobs. And because runner/fleet.js:154-158 skips metric sources with no rows ever, the fleet dot stays green — the feeds die at install time with no signal beyond launchd's own log.
Why it matters
This is a public repo whose CLAUDE.md declares the platform as macOS Apple Silicon; the checked-in templates encode a machine-specific interpreter path that contradicts that, and the failure mode is the silent one the watchdog was built to prevent (masked by the intentional unconfigured-skip rule). It also drifts from the templates' own EnvironmentVariables PATH, which lists /opt/homebrew/bin first.
How to fix
Either use /usr/bin/env-style resolution at render time — have install-launchd.sh substitute a __PYTHON3__ placeholder with "$(command -v python3)" — or standardize the four feed plists on /usr/bin/python3 alternatives is not viable (no system python3 guarantee), so render-time resolution is the robust fix; fail the install loudly if python3 is absent.
Expected improvement
Fresh installs on machines without a python.org install get working (or loudly failing) feed schedules instead of four silently dead launchd jobs invisible to the fleet watchdog.
Evidence
scripts/com.helm.uscf.plist: <string>/usr/local/bin/python3</string> (same in tokens/jobs/morphy) vs scripts/com.helm.morning.plist: <string>/opt/homebrew/bin/node</string>; install-launchd.sh:15 only does sed -e "s|__HELM_ROOT__|$ROOT|g" -e "s|__HOME__|$HOME|g".
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Confirmed in current code. Read scripts/com.helm.uscf.plist — line 9 (finding cited 9-11; interpreter is exactly line 9) is <string>/usr/local/bin/python3</string>, and grep shows the same in com.helm.tokens/jobs/morphy.plist, while com.helm.morning/plan/weekly/distill/hud/runner use /opt/homebrew/bin/node and com.helm.voice uses __HELM_ROOT__/voice-server/.venv/bin/python. install-launchd.sh line 15 does only sed -e "s|__HELM_ROOT__|$ROOT|g" -e "s|__HOME__|$HOME|g" — no interpreter resolution — so on a machine without /usr/local/bin/python3 (stock Apple Silicon with Homebrew-only python) launchd would fail to exec all four feed jobs. Proposed fix (a __PYTHON3__ placeholder rendered via command -v python3, failing loudly if absent) is sound and consistent with the existing render mechanism. Severity low is right: public-repo fresh-install papercut, no impact on the running machine.

install-launchd.sh unconditionally installs com.helm.voice — on machines without the venv, launchd respawns a failing job every 10 s forever

scripts/install-launchd.sh:11-17 · reviewer: deploy-infra
What it is
The installer loops over ALL `com.helm.*.plist` templates and bootstraps each. com.helm.voice.plist has `KeepAlive=true`, `RunAtLoad=true`, `ThrottleInterval=10`, and its ProgramArguments binary is `__HELM_ROOT__/voice-server/.venv/bin/python`. CLAUDE.md explicitly treats voice as optional ('If the venv doesn't exist, say voice isn't set up yet … the HUD runs fine silent'), but on a machine where the venv was never created, launchd will attempt to spawn a nonexistent binary and retry every 10 seconds indefinitely — a permanent low-grade respawn loop generating launchd error noise (and, combined with the missing logs dir, invisibly).
Why it matters
The documented setup order allows voice to be absent, yet the documented installer creates a perpetual failing agent in that exact state. It never self-heals until the user builds the venv or boots the agent out manually.
How to fix
In install-launchd.sh, skip (with a printed notice) any template whose rendered program binary does not exist — e.g. for com.helm.voice, test `[ -x "$ROOT/voice-server/.venv/bin/python" ]` before bootstrapping; or generally extract argv[0] from the rendered plist and check it.
Expected improvement
Machines without voice set up get a clear 'skipped com.helm.voice (venv missing)' instead of an eternal 10-second launchd respawn loop.
Evidence
install-launchd.sh: `for tpl in "$ROOT"/scripts/com.helm.*.plist; do … launchctl bootstrap "gui/$(id -u)" "$out"`. com.helm.voice.plist: `<string>__HELM_ROOT__/voice-server/.venv/bin/python</string>` + `<key>KeepAlive</key><true/>` + `<key>ThrottleInterval</key><integer>10</integer>`.
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read scripts/install-launchd.sh (lines 11-19) and scripts/com.helm.voice.plist. Evidence is accurate: the installer globs "$ROOT"/scripts/com.helm.*.plist and unconditionally renders + `launchctl bootstrap`s every template with no existence check on the program binary (line 11-18). com.helm.voice.plist has ProgramArguments[0]=__HELM_ROOT__/voice-server/.venv/bin/python (line 9), RunAtLoad=true (28), KeepAlive=true (30), ThrottleInterval=10 (32). CLAUDE.md does document voice as optional ("if the venv doesn't exist... the HUD runs fine silent"), so on a venv-less machine launchd will retry the nonexistent binary every ~10s indefinitely. Cited line range 11-17 is correct (loop is 11-19). Minor corrections/refinements: (a) the "missing logs dir" aside is plausible but secondary — logs/ is gitignored (.gitignore line 10) and the installer never mkdirs it, so on a fresh clone StandardOut/ErrorPath targets a nonexistent dir and launchd's spawn errors go only to the system log; on this machine logs/ exists so it's not observable here; (b) the proposed fix (test -x on the rendered argv[0] before bootstrap) is sound. Not a duplicate of any KNOWN/EXCLUDED item. Severity low is right — noise/battery-level impact only, self-heals once the venv is built.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read scripts/install-launchd.sh (lines 11-19: the loop renders and `launchctl bootstrap`s every scripts/com.helm.*.plist with no existence check on the program binary) and scripts/com.helm.voice.plist (line 9: ProgramArguments[0] = __HELM_ROOT__/voice-server/.venv/bin/python; lines 27-32: RunAtLoad=true, KeepAlive=true, ThrottleInterval=10). No mitigation found: README.md (lines 95-105) explicitly frames voice as optional yet recommends running scripts/install-launchd.sh for login autostart with no venv precondition, and CLAUDE.md's spin-up playbook likewise treats a missing venv as a supported state. So on a venv-less machine the documented installer does create a KeepAlive agent whose binary doesn't exist, and launchd will retry the spawn every ~10s indefinitely. Cited lines are correct. Two accuracy corrections to the description: (1) the parenthetical about the missing logs dir making it 'invisible' is only partially apt — when the binary is missing, launchd never spawns the process at all, so StandardOutPath is irrelevant to THIS failure mode; the spawn errors go to launchd's own log either way (logs/ is indeed gitignored/untracked and nothing creates it, which is a separate small gap for jobs that do spawn). (2) Same pattern applies to com.helm.runner/hud only if node/npx are absent, which is unlikely; voice is the one whose absence is a documented supported state. Proposed fix (skip templates whose rendered argv[0] doesn't exist, with a notice) is correct and low-risk; checking `[ -x "$ROOT/voice-server/.venv/bin/python" ]` specifically or extracting argv[0] generically both work. Materiality is genuinely low — cosmetic launchd noise plus negligible CPU on a single-user machine that in practice has the venv (this machine does) — but it's a real wart in the documented fresh-install path. Severity 'low' is right, not inflated.
lowConfirmed backend effort: trivial

warmHaiku pings api.anthropic.com regardless of VOICE_ROUTER preference and during next build page-data collection

lib/router.ts:883-905 · reviewer: router-model-engine-seam
What it is
warmHaiku is gated only on ANTHROPIC_API_KEY presence and VOICE_NO_WARMUP; it fires at module load (line 905: `warmHaiku(); // module load = first voice API hit`) and again on every route() call (line 83). It does not consult VOICE_ROUTER: a user who sets VOICE_ROUTER=local or =rules — plausibly to keep voice traffic fully local — still sends a real POST to api.anthropic.com the moment lib/router.ts loads, because the key exists in ~/.claude/.env for other HELM uses. The module-load side effect also runs whenever Next.js imports the voice route modules outside serving traffic, notably during `npx next build` page-data collection (the ship-after-merge routine), spending a 1-token API call per build with no voice session anywhere. The Fly CHAT_ONLY image is unaffected in practice only by accident: no ~/.claude/.env exists there and no ANTHROPIC_API_KEY appears in Dockerfile/entrypoint.sh/fly.toml, so the key check no-ops.
Why it matters
The per-process warmup is documented intent, but its gate is the wrong variable: key presence is a proxy for 'haiku may be used', and it's false when VOICE_ROUTER forces local/rules. An explicitly local-only configuration still leaks a network call (with the API key in headers) to Anthropic on every server process and build. Cost is negligible; the surprise factor for a local-forced setup is the issue.
How to fix
Add the engine preference to the gate: skip the warmup when `(homeEnv("VOICE_ROUTER") || "auto")` is 'local' or 'rules' (mirroring pickEngine's dispatch), and consider setting VOICE_NO_WARMUP in the build environment or moving the module-load call behind the first route() invocation so builds never ping.
Expected improvement
VOICE_ROUTER=local/rules actually keeps routing traffic off the network, and prod builds stop making incidental Anthropic API calls.
Evidence
if (haikuWarmed || !key || process.env.VOICE_NO_WARMUP) return;
...
warmHaiku(); // module load = first voice API hit — warm while rules still answer
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Confirmed in current lib/router.ts. warmHaiku (lines 883-905) is gated only on haikuWarmed/key-presence/VOICE_NO_WARMUP (line 887); fires at module load (line 905, quote matches verbatim) and per route() call (line 83). pickEngine (lines 94-115) shows VOICE_ROUTER=local uses localRoute->rules and =rules uses rules only — haiku is never invoked in those modes, yet the warmup POST to api.anthropic.com with the key in headers still fires because homeEnv loads ~/.claude/.env regardless. Import chain app/api/voice{,/text}/route.ts -> lib/voiceDispatch -> lib/router makes the module-load ping run on any import of those route modules; next build's page-data collection imports route modules, so the per-build ping is plausible (not runtime-verified), and VOICE_NO_WARMUP is set nowhere except tests. Fly claim checks out: no ANTHROPIC_API_KEY in Dockerfile/entrypoint.sh/fly.toml. The warmup itself is documented intent (comment 880-882), but the missing VOICE_ROUTER gate is not — proposed fix (mirror pickEngine's local/rules skip) is sound. Severity low is right: cost negligible, issue is the surprise network call for an explicitly-local config. Line citations in the finding are accurate.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Confirmed in lib/router.ts. Line 887 gate is exactly `haikuWarmed || !key || process.env.VOICE_NO_WARMUP` — VOICE_ROUTER is never consulted; module-load call at line 905, per-route() retry at line 83, all as described. pickEngine (lines 94-104) shows VOICE_ROUTER=local/rules never uses haikuRoute, so the warmup POST (with the real API key in x-api-key headers) fires anyway when the key exists in ~/.claude/.env (homeEnv loads it, lib/homeEnv.ts:29-32). Build-time claim is sound: app/api/voice/route.ts and app/api/voice/text/route.ts import lib/voiceDispatch.ts which imports router, Next build evaluates route modules during page-data collection, and VOICE_NO_WARMUP is set only in scripts/test-router.ts (tests), not the build. Fly-unaffected-by-accident also checks out (no ANTHROPIC_API_KEY in image). Extra supporting detail: the line-882 comment "Mirrors warmLocal()" is inaccurate — warmLocal is invoked only inside localRoute (line 991), never at module load, so the Haiku warmup's module-load side effect is asymmetric with the pattern it claims to mirror. Not covered by any ADR (the warmup is documented intent but the VOICE_ROUTER-blind gate is not) and not in the known/excluded list. Proposed fix (skip when VOICE_ROUTER is local/rules; suppress during build or defer to first route()) is correct and harmless. Severity low is appropriate: negligible cost, no breakage; the material issue is an unexpected keyed network call to Anthropic under an explicitly local-only configuration.

package.json has no engines field despite the stack assuming Node 22 everywhere else

package.json:1-28 · reviewer: deploy-infra
What it is
The Dockerfile builds and runs on node:22-bookworm-slim, CI pins node-version 22, and the launchd plists hardcode /opt/homebrew/bin/node — but package.json declares no `engines`. A contributor (or Daniel on a machine with an older Homebrew node) running `npm ci` / `next dev` under Node 18/20 gets no warning; Next 15 + React 19 have Node >=18.18 floors and the repo's own tooling is only ever exercised on 22.
Why it matters
For a public showcase repo, `engines` is the one-line, machine-readable statement of the supported runtime; without it, version-skew failures surface as confusing build/runtime errors instead of an upfront npm warning.
How to fix
Add `"engines": { "node": ">=22" }` to package.json (matching the Docker base image and CI).
Expected improvement
npm warns immediately on unsupported Node versions instead of failing later in Next/tsx.
Evidence
package.json contains only name/version/private/scripts/dependencies/devDependencies — no `engines`. Dockerfile: `FROM node:22-bookworm-slim`; ci.yml: `node-version: 22`.
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read package.json (28 lines: name/version/private/scripts/dependencies/devDependencies only — no engines field, and note npm ci under npm engine-strict off only warns, never blocks, so 'upfront npm warning' is accurate). Verified evidence: Dockerfile lines 6 and 18 use FROM node:22-bookworm-slim; .github/workflows/ci.yml line 15 pins node-version: 22. No .nvmrc exists either, so package.json engines really is the only place a runtime floor could live. The finding's claim about launchd plists hardcoding /opt/homebrew/bin/node was not independently re-verified but is immaterial to the core claim. Not a duplicate of the excluded items (issue #2 covers showcase docs, not package.json config). Severity info is appropriate — dev-experience polish, no runtime bug.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read package.json in full (28 lines): no engines field, only name/version/private/scripts/dependencies/devDependencies. Verified Dockerfile lines 6 and 18 both use node:22-bookworm-slim, and .github/workflows/ci.yml line 15 pins node-version: 22, exactly as the evidence claims. devDependencies also include @types/node ^22.15.0, reinforcing Node 22 as the assumed runtime. Checked exclusions: open issue #2 covers showcase/doc polish (demo GIF, demo vault, CI, design docs) and does not cover package.json engines metadata; no ADR (0001-0009) declares the runtime version, so this is not intentional-by-design. Proposed fix (engines: node >=22) is correct and matches Docker/CI; note that npm only warns on engines mismatch by default (hard-fails only with engine-strict), so the benefit is an upfront warning, not a hard gate — consistent with the finding's own framing. Info severity is right for a single-user personal tool where the practical impact is limited to hypothetical contributors on older Node.

docs/fly-deploy.md still describes the rejected route-allowlist CHAT_ONLY behavior, not the method-based gate that shipped

docs/fly-deploy.md:82-85 · reviewer: docs-drift
What it is
fly-deploy.md states: "The image also sets `CHAT_ONLY=1`, which 404s every API route except `/api/chat` + `/api/key` (middleware.ts)". That is the old route-allowlist implementation that ADR-0004 explicitly documents as rejected. The current middleware.ts (lines 14-19) gates on HTTP method: all GET/HEAD/OPTIONS requests to every /api/ route pass, and only mutating methods 404. So on the Fly VM, /api/state, /api/report, /api/todos (GET), /api/transcript (GET), and /api/speak (GET, which streams TTS) are all reachable from the tailnet — not just /api/chat and /api/key.
Why it matters
This misdocuments the deployed security surface in the exact document an operator reads while setting up the VM. Someone auditing the Fly deployment from fly-deploy.md would believe the read surface is two routes when it is actually every GET route, including /api/report (arbitrary vault markdown under inbox//system/runs/) and /api/transcript (conversation history) — all readable by any tailnet peer. The doc also contradicts ADR-0004 and CLAUDE.md, which correctly describe the method gate.
How to fix
Rewrite the sentence to match middleware.ts and ADR-0004: CHAT_ONLY 404s every mutating method (POST/PUT/PATCH/DELETE) except /api/chat; GET/HEAD/OPTIONS pass on all routes so the phone renders every tab read-only, and /api/key is exempted outright. Link ADR-0004.
Expected improvement
The deploy doc, ADR-0004, CLAUDE.md, and middleware.ts all describe the same perimeter; an operator auditing the VM knows the true tailnet-visible read surface.
Evidence
fly-deploy.md: "The image also sets `CHAT_ONLY=1`, which 404s every API route except `/api/chat` + `/api/key` (middleware.ts)" vs middleware.ts: "return !(method === \"GET\" || method === \"HEAD\" || method === \"OPTIONS\");"
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Confirmed. docs/fly-deploy.md lines 83-85 state: "The image also sets `CHAT_ONLY=1`, which 404s every API route except `/api/chat` + `/api/key` (middleware.ts)" — the old route-allowlist description. Current middleware.ts (blockedInChatOnly, lines 14-19) exempts /api/chat, /api/chat/*, and /api/key outright, then blocks only mutating methods: `return !(method === "GET" || method === "HEAD" || method === "OPTIONS")`. So all GET/HEAD/OPTIONS on every /api/ route pass on the Fly VM, contradicting the doc. The doc also contradicts ADR-0004 and CLAUDE.md, both of which describe the method gate correctly. Minor corrections: the offending sentence spans lines 83-85 (finding said 82-85), and the finding's cited middleware lines 14-19 are accurate. The finding's evidence quotes are real and in context. Not covered by the KNOWN/EXCLUDED list — this is a current-code doc drift, not doc polish tracked by issue #2, and note that the doc's method-gate mismatch survived the d6a6e9f doc-rewrite pass. Suggested fix in the finding matches middleware behavior (including the /api/key exemption and GET/HEAD/OPTIONS pass-through). Severity medium is appropriate: security-surface misdocumentation in the operator-facing deploy doc, but no code defect.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read docs/fly-deploy.md (lines 75-94) and middleware.ts (whole file). Confirmed: fly-deploy.md lines 83-85 state CHAT_ONLY "404s every API route except `/api/chat` + `/api/key` (middleware.ts)", which is the old route-allowlist behavior. Minor line correction: the stale text is on lines 83-85, not 82-85. Not a duplicate of exclusions: issue #2 covers showcase polish (GIF/demo vault/CI/design doc), not this security misdescription; the pre-publication review era is irrelevant since the stale text exists in the current file. README Quickstart command omits -H 127.0.0.1, contradicting the documented loopback-only perimeter (ADR-0003)

README.md:84 · reviewer: docs-drift
What it is
The README Quickstart tells a new user to run `npx next dev -p 3107`. Next.js dev binds 0.0.0.0 by default when no -H flag is given — which is exactly why every other launch path in the repo passes the flag explicitly: `npm run demo` is `next dev -p 3107 -H 127.0.0.1` (package.json line 9) and scripts/com.helm.hud.plist passes `<string>-H</string><string>127.0.0.1</string>` (lines 14-15). Yet the README's own Security section (lines 160-164) and ADR-0003 claim "The HUD binds 127.0.0.1 only ... never bind it to 0.0.0.0".
Why it matters
A newcomer following the primary quickstart gets a HUD listening on all interfaces — the one thing the Security section says never to do, because /api/queue feeds the runner's `claude -p --dangerously-skip-permissions`. Fail-closed auth limits the blast radius until HELM_API_KEY is set, but once it is, the documented perimeter ("binds 127.0.0.1 only") is simply false for anyone who started via the README command.
How to fix
Change the Quickstart command to `npx next dev -p 3107 -H 127.0.0.1` (matching the demo script and the plist), and optionally note why the flag matters with a pointer to ADR-0003.
Expected improvement
The default onboarding path actually produces the loopback-only bind the security documentation promises.
Evidence

Cross-checks confirm every other launch path pins loopback: package.json line 9 demo script is `... next dev -p 3107 -H 127.0.0.1`, and scripts/com.helm.hud.plist line 15 passes `<string>127.0.0.1</string>` (the -H arg). README's Security section (lines 159-166, not 160-164 as cited — trivial off-by-a-few) says "The HUD binds **127.0.0.1 only** ... never bind it to `0.0.0.0`", and ADR-0003 documents loopback as the perimeter.   • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Verified in current files. docs/setup.md claims to list "every environment variable" but omits HELM_API_KEY — no doc explains creating the key that fail-closed auth requires

docs/setup.md:13-34 · reviewer: docs-drift
What it is
setup.md opens with "The operator manual: every environment variable..." and README line 98 says "Every environment variable ... live[s] in docs/setup.md". The Configuration table (lines 13-34) does not contain HELM_API_KEY. No document in the repo tells the operator to generate and set this key: README line 161 and CLAUDE.md refer to it as already existing "from ~/.claude/.env", and fly-deploy.md line 40 says to copy "the value from ~/.claude/.env on the Mac" — assuming it is there. Because lib/auth.ts is fail-closed ("if (!expected) return { ok: false, status: 503, error: \"HELM_API_KEY not configured\" }"), a fresh install following README + setup.md gets 503 on every write route (/api/queue, /api/voice, /api/voice/text, /api/chat, /api/todos POST, /api/transcript DELETE) with no setup step that would have prevented it. The table also omits several other vars code reads: GITHUB_TOKEN and MORPHY_REPO (feeds/morphy-github.py), USCF_MEMBER_ID (feeds/uscf-rating.py), NOTION_TOKEN/MORPHY_DB_ID, HELM_NOTIFY/HELM_NOTIFY_EVENTS (runner), and CLAUDE_BIN.
Why it matters
This is the first wall every new user hits: voice dispatch, chat, and todos all 503 ("HELM_API_KEY not configured") and the operator manual that promises to cover every env var never mentions the variable named in the error. The fail-closed design is intentional (ADR-0002); the missing setup instruction is the drift.
How to fix
Add a HELM_API_KEY row to the table (purpose: shared secret for all write routes; default: unset = writes 503) plus a one-liner on generating it (e.g. `openssl rand -hex 32` into ~/.claude/.env). Add rows for the other undocumented vars the feeds/runner read, or soften the "every environment variable" claim to match what the table actually covers.
Expected improvement
A fresh install can enable writes without reading lib/auth.ts source; the operator manual's coverage claim becomes true.
Evidence
setup.md line 3: "every environment variable"; table rows contain no HELM_API_KEY; lib/auth.ts line 22: "if (!expected) return { ok: false, status: 503, error: \"HELM_API_KEY not configured\" };"
Verifier notes (2)

.helm-config.json's launchdPlists field gives a plain-cp install command that would install unrendered plist templates

.helm-config.json:11 · reviewer: docs-drift
What it is
The machine record's `launchdPlists` field says: "install: cp scripts/com.helm.<name>.plist ~/Library/LaunchAgents/ && launchctl bootstrap ...". But all versioned plists are now templates containing `__HELM_ROOT__`/`__HOME__` placeholders (confirmed in all 10+ scripts/com.helm.*.plist files), and scripts/install-launchd.sh exists specifically to sed-render them before bootstrapping. Copying a raw template installs a launchd agent whose ProgramArguments contain literal `__HELM_ROOT__` paths, so the agent fails to start. CLAUDE.md, README, and AGENTS.md already point at install-launchd.sh; the config record — which CLAUDE.md line 4 says to treat as "the record of how this machine is wired" — still documents the pre-template procedure. (File is gitignored, so this bites the owner/agent, not contributors.)
Why it matters
CLAUDE.md instructs the agent to treat this file as authoritative; an agent reinstalling a single agent per its instruction would install a broken plist and the service would silently fail to launch.
How to fix
Update the launchdPlists string to "render + install with scripts/install-launchd.sh (templates use __HELM_ROOT__/__HOME__ placeholders — never cp raw)".
Expected improvement
The machine record and the actual install procedure agree; no path to installing placeholder-ridden plists.
Evidence
.helm-config.json: "install: cp scripts/com.helm.<name>.plist ~/Library/LaunchAgents/ && launchctl bootstrap gui/$(id -u) ..." vs install-launchd.sh: "sed -e \"s|__HELM_ROOT__|$ROOT|g\" -e \"s|__HOME__|$HOME|g\" \"$tpl\" > \"$out\""
Verifier notes (2)

All 12 scripts/com.helm.*.plist files contain __HELM_ROOT__ (verified by grep: 12 of 12), and scripts/install-launchd.sh line 15 renders them with sed (s|__HELM_ROOT__|$ROOT|g and s|__HOME__|$HOME|g) before installing. So the documented cp-raw procedure would install unrendered templates with literal __HELM_ROOT__ paths, and the agent would fail to launch. Minor correction to the finding: it says "10+ plist files"; the exact count is 12. Also line 11's leading claim "canonical copies of every installed agent" is itself stale — they are canonical TEMPLATES, not copies (CLAUDE.md already says so). File is gitignored (machine-local record), so impact is limited to the owner/agents following it, consistent with severity low. Not a duplicate of the excluded known items (the CLAUDE.md/README/AGENTS.md docs were fixed; this file was not). Suggested fix in the finding is correct.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read .helm-config.json in full and checked scripts/. Dockerfile comment misstates the CHAT_ONLY perimeter (claims all non-chat API routes 404, but middleware passes every GET)

Dockerfile:38-39 · reviewer: data-handling
What it is
The Dockerfile's CHAT_ONLY comment says "middleware.ts 404s every API route except /api/chat + /api/key, so the tailnet surface matches the 'chat-only' contract". That describes the pre-#36 behavior; the current middleware.ts (blockedInChatOnly) only blocks mutating methods — GET/HEAD/OPTIONS pass to every API route (/api/state, /api/report, /api/transcript, /api/todos GET), which is the ADR-0004 design. The comment claims a tighter read surface than actually exists.
Why it matters
Anyone auditing the Fly image's data-exposure surface from the Dockerfile alone would conclude the vault-reading GET routes (state, reports, voice transcript) are unreachable over the tailnet when they are in fact served. In a repo whose docs are the security record, a comment that understates the exposed read surface is the kind of drift that hides a future regression.
How to fix
Reword the Dockerfile comment to match middleware.ts and ADR-0004: mutations 404 except /api/chat; GET/HEAD pass so the tailnet phone can render read-only tabs (including /api/transcript and /api/report).
Expected improvement
The deploy artifact's inline security description matches the actual perimeter, so a surface audit from the Dockerfile reaches the right conclusion.
Evidence
Dockerfile: "# CHAT_ONLY: middleware.ts 404s every API route except /api/chat + /api/key" vs middleware.ts:19: "return !(method === \"GET\" || method === \"HEAD\" || method === \"OPTIONS\");"
Verifier notes (2)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Read Dockerfile lines 38-39 and middleware.ts in full. The Dockerfile comment reads exactly as quoted: "# CHAT_ONLY: middleware.ts 404s every API route except /api/chat + /api/key, / # so the tailnet surface matches the \"chat-only\" contract above." The current middleware.ts (blockedInChatOnly, line 18) blocks only mutating methods — `return !(method === "GET" || method === "HEAD" || method === "OPTIONS")` — so every GET/HEAD/OPTIONS API request (e.g. /api/state, /api/report, /api/transcript GET, /api/todos GET) is served, per ADR-0004. The middleware's own header comment (lines 4-11) documents the method-based design correctly and even notes the old route-based behavior as "Before" — so the Dockerfile comment is stale drift from the pre-#36 route-blocking era, exactly as the finding claims. Not covered by the known/excluded list: this is current-code doc drift, not a re-derived old finding, and issue #2 tracks showcase polish, not this security-surface comment. One minor evidence nit: the finding's evidence lists OPTIONS-passing at "middleware.ts:19" — the return is on line 18; immaterial. Severity info is right for a comment-only inaccuracy; the proposed fix (reword to "mutations 404 except /api/chat; GET/HEAD pass for read-only tabs") matches ADR-0004 and the middleware header.
  • CONFIRM (impact lens, high confidence): Read Dockerfile lines 38-39 and middleware.ts in full. Confirmed exactly as described: the Dockerfile comment says "middleware.ts 404s every API route except /api/chat + /api/key" but blockedInChatOnly (middleware.ts:14-19) only blocks non-GET/HEAD/OPTIONS methods — all GET API routes pass, which is the intentional ADR-0004 design (middleware.ts's own header comment at lines 4-11 describes the read/write perimeter correctly, and even notes the old 404-everything behavior as "Before"). So the stale text is confined to the Dockerfile; the authoritative files (middleware.ts, CLAUDE.md, ADR-0004) all state the correct method-based rule, which caps impact. Not a duplicate of the excluded items (issue #2 is showcase polish, not this comment; the #36-#44 fixes are what the comment failed to track). Line numbers correct (38-39). Proposed fix is right. Severity info is appropriate — one-line doc drift in a secondary file, mitigated by correct docs everywhere else.
