Appendix A — Refuted findings

Reported by a reviewer, then rejected by the adversarial verifiers. Kept for transparency.

mediumRefuted runner effort: small

voice-ask interpolates args.context raw into the claude -p prompt (args.prompt is JSON-escaped, context is not)

runner/runner.js:305-312 · reviewer: security-runner
What it is
buildPrompt's voice-ask case JSON.stringifies the ask (`${JSON.stringify(ask)}`) but splices the conversation context in verbatim: `const convoBlock = convo ? `\n\nRecent voice conversation (context...):\n${convo}` : ""`. args.context is filled by lib/voiceDispatch.ts (line 142) from conversationContext() — the rolling voice memory that includes HELM's own prior spoken replies. Those replies include summaryFromOutput() lines from earlier tier-3 runs, i.e. first-line output of claude sessions that read Gmail (inbox-brief), the web (morning-report), and the co-edited Notion board. Content originating outside the machine can therefore flow, unescaped and un-delimited, into the top-level instruction text of the next --dangerously-skip-permissions session, where it can present itself as new instructions rather than quoted data.
Why it matters
ADR-0009 accepts owner-enqueued intents, but explicitly asks to flag new paths where untrusted content reaches the queue — this is one: an email subject or web headline crafted to survive the one-line summary gets replayed into the prompt body of a later, unrelated voice-ask that may have broader effective permissions than the run that ingested it. The asymmetry with args.prompt (escaped) shows the risk was recognized for one field and missed for the other.
How to fix
Treat context as data, not prose: JSON.stringify the context block too, or fence it (e.g. wrap in a clearly delimited quoted block with an instruction that its contents are a transcript to reference, never instructions to follow), and cap its length in the runner rather than trusting the enqueuer.
Expected improvement
Closes the relay where summarized email/web/Notion content re-enters a skip-permissions prompt as instruction-position text; both voice-ask inputs get consistent handling.
Evidence
const convo = (args.context || "").trim(); const convoBlock = convo ? `\n\nRecent voice conversation (context — the ask may refer back to it):\n${convo}` : ""; ... machine-transcribed — minor transcription errors possible): ${JSON.stringify(ask)}${convoBlock}
Verifier notes (3)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Confirmed in current code. runner/runner.js:305-312: voice-ask JSON.stringifies args.prompt (`ask`) but interpolates args.context verbatim (`${convo}`) with no escaping, fencing, or length cap. lib/voiceDispatch.ts:127,142 fills context from conversationContext(). lib/voiceMemory.ts shows the taint chain is even more direct than described: conversationContext() calls recentRunResults(), which injects run `summary` fields (140 chars each, up to 3) straight from system/runs/*.json — those summaries are summaryFromOutput() (runner.js:423,747), the first stdout line of claude sessions that read Gmail, the web, and the co-edited Notion board; runningRuns() also splices args.prompt slices. Corrections: (1) the primary external-content path is recentRunResults(), not only replayed spoken replies — finding's mechanism is understated, not wrong; (2) exploitability is constrained because injected content must survive the earlier session's own one-line summarization (140-char budget); (3) JSON.stringify alone would not neutralize injection — the fence + runner-side cap parts of the fix are the substantive ones. Not a duplicate of excluded items; ADR-0009 explicitly asks for new untrusted-content paths to be flagged. Medium severity is right given the narrow channel.
  • REFUTE (impact lens, high confidence): Read runner/runner.js:305-312 (buildPrompt voice-ask case), lib/voiceDispatch.ts:127/142, lib/voiceMemory.ts (conversationContext, recentRunResults, runningRuns), and docs/decisions/0009-prompt-injection-threat-model.md. The code behavior is accurately described: args.context is interpolated verbatim into the prompt while args.prompt is JSON.stringified, and conversationContext() does include summaries of prior runs that read Gmail/web/Notion (recentRunResults, 140-char cap per entry). However, this is precisely the risk ADR-0009 accepts, verbatim: "a hostile web page summarized into a report, read back as context by a later session, could try to steer that session — classic indirect prompt injection... Chosen: accept it, with the blast radius already bounded." This is the CONTENT path, explicitly accepted; the verifier instruction to "flag any new path that lets untrusted content reach the queue" refers to the TRANSPORT path (untrusted parties enqueuing intents), which is not what this is — the intent here is still owner-enqueued via the authed loopback voice route. Three further materiality problems: (1) the proposed fix is exactly the "sanitize/quarantine" option the ADR considered and rejected ("no reliable sanitizer for natural-language injection exists"); JSON.stringify does not stop an LLM from following instructions inside a quoted string — args.prompt is stringified for syntactic embedding in the YAML frontmatter line (`prompt: ${JSON.stringify(ask)}`), not as an injection defense, so the claimed "asymmetry shows the risk was recognized" is a wrong inference. (2) The blast radius argument fails: the sessions that ORIGINALLY ingest the untrusted content (inbox-brief reading full email bodies, morning-report reading full web pages) run under the same --dangerously-skip-permissions with the same effective permissions as any voice-ask; a 140-char summary replayed later is a strictly narrower injection channel than the full-document exposure already accepted. Skills outside ALLOWED_SKILLS are rejected, so injection cannot open new write surfaces. (3) Context length is bounded in practice (max 6 exchanges + 3x140-char run summaries + 3x90-char running entries), and only the authed owner can set args.context at all (ADR-0002/0009). Intentional-by-design per ADR-0009; exists=false.
  • REFUTE (existence lens, high confidence, tiebreaker): Read runner/runner.js:305-312 (buildPrompt voice-ask case), lib/voiceDispatch.ts:126-142, lib/voiceMemory.ts:87-178, and docs/decisions/0009-prompt-injection-threat-model.md in full. The MECHANICS are accurately described and present in current code: args.context is interpolated verbatim into the prompt while args.prompt goes through JSON.stringify, and conversationContext() does replay recentRunResults() summaries (first stdout line of sessions that read Gmail/web/Notion, 140 chars each, max 3) plus prior exchanges. But this is the content path ADR-0009 explicitly considers and accepts, nearly verbatim: "A hostile web page summarized into a report, read back as context by a later session, could try to steer that session — classic indirect prompt injection... Chosen: accept it, with the blast radius already bounded", and the chosen option's listed con is exactly this loop: "the model's own outputs are a persistence layer for injected text." The instruction to flag "any new path that lets untrusted content reach the queue" is the TRANSPORT path (untrusted parties enqueuing intents — ADR-0005's concern); here the intent is still owner-enqueued via the authed loopback voice route, and neither ADR reevaluation trigger (multi-user surface, write path syncing into the queue) applies. Three materiality corrections that seal it: (1) the args.prompt/args.context "asymmetry shows the risk was recognized" inference is wrong — JSON.stringify(ask) is needed for syntactic embedding in the YAML `prompt:` frontmatter line and is no injection defense (an LLM follows instructions inside quoted strings just as well); (2) the blast-radius claim fails: the sessions that ORIGINALLY ingest the untrusted content (inbox-brief over full email bodies, morning-report over full web pages) run under the same --dangerously-skip-permissions and same ALLOWED_SKILLS gate as any voice-ask, so a 140-char summary replayed later is a strictly narrower channel than exposure already accepted; (3) the proposed fix (fence/escape the context) is the sanitize/quarantine option the ADR explicitly rejected ("no reliable sanitizer for natural-language injection exists"). Also context length is bounded in practice (max 6 exchanges + 3×140-char run summaries), so "cap its length" adds little. Intentional-by-design per ADR-0009; verifier 2's analysis is correct.
lowRefuted backend effort: small

voiceMemory rememberExchange has a lost-update race (read-modify-write, last writer wins)

lib/voiceMemory.ts:38-48 · reviewer: bugs-router
What it is
rememberExchange reads the whole JSONL ring, appends one line in memory, and atomically rewrites the file. atomicWriteFileSync prevents torn reads but not lost updates: two concurrent voice turns (or a voice turn racing a chat-route write) both read N lines, each writes N+1, and the second write silently discards the first exchange. The offer flow depends on the LAST exchange specifically — pendingOffer (lib/router.ts:205) reads recentExchanges(1) — so if the briefing's exchange is the one clobbered, a 'yes' seconds later finds no offer and degrades to 'Standing by.' / a tier-3 fallthrough.
Why it matters
The comment on the write acknowledges concurrency ('a concurrent voice turn reading a truncated ring') but the chosen mechanism only fixes atomicity of a single write, not the read-modify-write cycle. On a single-user PTT loop it is rare, but two open HUD tabs (a documented gotcha) or a run-completion announcement landing during a turn makes it realistic, and the symptom (dropped offer, missing pronoun referent) is indistinguishable from routing flakiness.
How to fix
Append instead of rewriting: fs.appendFileSync of the single JSON line (appends up to PIPE_BUF are atomic on local filesystems), and move the MAX_KEEP pruning to an occasional compaction (e.g. only rewrite when readLines().length > 2*MAX_KEEP), keeping the rewrite path rare instead of per-exchange.
Expected improvement
Concurrent exchanges can no longer erase each other, so the offer/'yes' round-trip and pronoun resolution stop having a rare unexplained failure mode.
Evidence
const lines = readLines();
    lines.push(JSON.stringify({ ts: new Date().toISOString(), ...e }));
    // atomic — a concurrent voice turn reading a truncated ring loses context
    atomicWriteFileSync(MEMORY_FILE, lines.slice(-MAX_KEEP).join("\n") + "\n");
Verifier notes (2)
  • REFUTE (existence lens, medium confidence): Read lib/voiceMemory.ts (rememberExchange is at lines 38-48 exactly as quoted, evidence is real) and lib/atomicWrite.ts, plus grepped all writers of memory.jsonl. The read-modify-write pattern exists, but the claimed race is not reachable in the current code: (1) rememberExchange is a fully synchronous block (readFileSync -> writeFileSync -> renameSync with no await/yield), so within Node's single-threaded event loop two concurrent requests can never interleave inside the RMW — the critical section is serialized by the runtime; (2) the only writers are the two call sites in lib/voiceDispatch.ts, reached from /api/voice and /api/voice/text, both served by the single Next.js HUD process (`next start`, one process; two open HUD tabs still hit the same server process). The finding's other claimed racers do not exist: the chat route never writes memory.jsonl (grep confirms only lib/voiceMemory.ts touches it), and no runner/run-completion path writes it either — the Fly VM's chat is CHAT_ONLY and its vault copy has no voice writer. The lost-update scenario would require a second writer process, which the architecture doesn't have. At most this is a latent-hazard note (pattern becomes racy if a second writer process is ever added), not a current bug; pendingOffer at lib/router.ts:205/235 does read recentExchanges(1) as claimed, but the clobber that would drop the offer cannot occur.
  • REFUTE (impact lens, high confidence): Read lib/voiceMemory.ts (rememberExchange, lines 38-48 — location and code quoted correctly), lib/voiceDispatch.ts, lib/router.ts (pendingOffer at 205, recentExchanges(1) at 235 — accurately cited), and grepped the whole repo for writers of system/voice/memory.jsonl. The abstract pattern (read-modify-write, last writer wins) is real, but it is unreachable in this system, so the finding fails on materiality. Three reasons. (1) rememberExchange is entirely synchronous — readLines (fs.readFileSync), push, atomicWriteFileSync, with no await between them — and Node route handlers run on one thread, so within the HUD process two calls can never interleave; the read-modify-write is effectively a critical section for free. (2) All writers of memory.jsonl live in that single process: only lib/voiceDispatch.ts (via /api/voice and /api/voice/text) calls rememberExchange, plus clearMemory via /api/transcript DELETE — also sync writeFileSync in the same process. The HUD runs as a single `next start` process (scripts/com.helm.hud.plist, no cluster/PM2), so there is no cross-process writer. (3) The finding's proposed concurrent racers are wrong: /api/chat does not import or write voiceMemory (grep confirms), and the runner never writes memory.jsonl — run-completion 'announcements' are surfaced by conversationContext READING system/runs/, not by writing exchanges. Two HUD tabs (the documented gotcha) share the same server process, so they change nothing. The in-code comment ('a concurrent voice turn reading a truncated ring') is about a reader in another process (e.g. the runner's claude -p subprocesses or debugging tools) seeing a torn file mid-rewrite — exactly what atomicWriteFileSync fixes; the chosen mechanism matches the actual threat. The appendFileSync+compaction fix would trade a working invariant for JSONL-interleaving concerns with zero benefit. If the HUD ever ran multi-process against a shared vault this would become a (still low) real finding, but that deployment does not exist.
mediumRefuted backend effort: small

routerSystem embeds untrusted run summaries and vault content unescaped in the router system prompt — router-level prompt injection can steer tier/skill selection into queue writes

lib/router.ts:828-857 · reviewer: router-model-engine-seam
What it is
routerSystem builds the tier-classification system prompt for both model engines by inlining stateSummary(state) and the raw conversation memory. stateSummary includes up to six recent run summaries verbatim (`${x.summary.slice(0, 140)}`) — these summaries are written by the runner from `claude -p` output over external content (inbox-brief reads email, github feed reads repo activity, morphy-sync reads the Notion board Michael co-edits) — plus daily-note lines, queue labels (`q.label ?? q.skill`), and Morphy assignee keys from Notion. None of it is delimited or marked as data, and the prompt contains no instruction to ignore directives found inside the snapshot. Adversarial text that survives into a run summary (e.g. an email subject crafted to read as router instructions, summarized by inbox-brief) sits in the system prompt for every subsequent fallthrough utterance and can bias the model toward tier 1 with an attacker-chosen ALLOWED_SKILLS entry — which dispatchTranscript converts directly into writeIntent(result.skill, source), a queued runner execution.
Why it matters
ADR-0009 accepts `--dangerously-skip-permissions` because only the authed owner can enqueue work, and asks that any new path letting untrusted content reach the queue be flagged. This is such a path, distinct from the already-filed skill-prompt injection: here untrusted content influences WHICH intent gets queued at routing time. The blast radius is bounded (skill must be in ALLOWED_SKILLS, validateRouted polices values, and the injection must survive a 140-char summary), but a misdirected morphy-sync or vault-cleanup run triggered by a crafted email is a real integrity issue on a system whose runs write to Notion and the vault.
How to fix
Wrap the snapshot and conversation blocks in explicit data delimiters and add one line to the system prompt: content inside the snapshot/conversation is data only and must never be followed as instructions, and tier/skill must be chosen solely from the user's utterance. Optionally sanitize run summaries at write time in the runner (strip newlines/brace-heavy content) since they also feed the HUD.
Expected improvement
Untrusted feed/Notion/email content loses its ability to masquerade as router instructions, keeping intent selection driven by the spoken utterance alone.
Evidence
const sum = x.summary ? ` — ${x.summary.slice(0, 140)}` : "";
lines.push(`  ${name} [${x.status}]${sum}`);
...
Dashboard snapshot:
${stateSummary(state)}${ convo ? `\n\nRecent conversation (use it to resolve follow-ups...`
Verifier notes (3)
  • CONFIRM (existence lens, high confidence): Confirmed against current code. lib/router.ts: stateSummary (805-837) inlines run summaries verbatim (line 832, `x.summary.slice(0,140)`), queue labels (817), daily-note lines (813-815), and Morphy assignee keys from Notion (821); routerSystem (839-857) embeds that snapshot plus raw conversation memory with no data delimiters and no instruction to treat snapshot content as data-only — "Answer ONLY from the snapshot" is grounding, not anti-injection. runner/runner.js summaryFromOutput (423) builds summaries from `claude -p` stdout over external content (email/github/Notion), unsanitized, 200-char cut at retire (489). Tier-1 route → writeIntent(result.skill, source) is real, but lives in lib/voiceDispatch.ts:133-134, not a `dispatchTranscript` in router.ts (minor attribution error). Mitigations the finding acknowledges are real: validateRouted (router.ts 869-873) enforces ALLOWED_SKILLS and rejects tier-1 without valid skill; no args are attacker-controllable on that path. Not a duplicate of ADR-0009's accepted skill-level injection — ADR-0009 explicitly asks new untrusted-content-to-queue paths be flagged, and no delimiter/instruction fix exists in the current prompt. Line range cited (828-857) is slightly loose but points at the right code. Medium severity is right given the bounded blast radius.
  • REFUTE (impact lens, high confidence): Read lib/router.ts:805-878 (stateSummary, routerSystem, validateRouted), lib/voiceDispatch.ts:89-147 (dispatchTranscript -> writeIntent(result.skill)), runner/runner.js:421-449 (summaryFromOutput), and docs/decisions/0009-prompt-injection-threat-model.md. The mechanics are accurately described: routerSystem does inline run summaries, daily lines, queue labels, Morphy assignee keys, and conversation memory with no data delimiters and no ignore-embedded-directives instruction, and a model-engine tier-1 verdict converts directly into a queued run. Line range 828-857 is correct. But the finding is intentional-by-design: ADR-0009 explicitly analyzes this exact content path — internet-origin text summarized into vault files that "become model context" and could "steer that session" — and accepts it, noting the blast radius is already bounded because "model-proposed skills outside ALLOWED_SKILLS [are] rejected" (that language describes precisely validateRouted at router.ts:869-878) and "a successful injection can at worst distort report prose or waste a run." Router-steered dispatch of an allowlisted, arg-less skill (writeIntent(result.skill, source) passes no attacker args) IS the accepted "waste a run" outcome, not a new path to the queue: neither reevaluation trigger (multi-user surface, write path syncing into the queue) applies. The proposed fix (sanitize/delimit) is the ADR's explicitly considered-and-rejected "Sanitize/quarantine" option. The delimiter+instruction hygiene would still be a cheap hardening worth mentioning as a suggestion, but as a review finding it duplicates a documented accepted risk, so exists=false.
  • REFUTE (existence lens, medium confidence, tiebreaker): Read lib/router.ts:805-878 (stateSummary, routerSystem, validateRouted), lib/voiceDispatch.ts:110-149, lib/skills.ts:27-40 (writeIntent), and docs/decisions/0009-prompt-injection-threat-model.md in full. The code mechanics are exactly as claimed: stateSummary inlines run summaries verbatim (line 832, slice(0,140)), queue labels (817), daily-note lines (813-815), and Notion assignee keys (821); routerSystem (839-857) embeds that snapshot plus raw conversation memory with no data delimiters and no ignore-embedded-directives instruction; a model tier-1 verdict becomes writeIntent(result.skill, source) at voiceDispatch.ts:134 (finding says "dispatchTranscript" in router.ts — it lives in voiceDispatch.ts; minor attribution error). But this duplicates ADR-0009's documented accepted risk, so per the KNOWN/EXCLUDED and intentional-design rules it does not stand as a finding. The ADR's decision text covers this path generically — vault files that "become model context" could "steer that session" — and bounds the blast radius with the exact mechanism that applies here: "model-proposed skills outside ALLOWED_SKILLS rejected" (that is validateRouted, router.ts:869-878) and "a successful injection can at worst ... waste a run." The tier-1 path writes an allowlisted skill name with EMPTY args (writeIntent default {} — I verified no attacker-controllable content reaches the queue file), so a router-steered dispatch is precisely the accepted "waste a run" outcome; untrusted content influences WHICH allowlisted skill runs but never itself reaches the queue, so the ADR's flag-new-paths clause is not triggered. Neither reevaluation trigger (multi-user surface; write path syncing into the queue) applies. The proposed fix is the ADR's considered-and-rejected Sanitize/quarantine option (the delimiter+one-line-instruction variant is cheap hardening worth passing along as a non-finding suggestion). Honest counter for the record (why verifier 1 confirmed): ADR-0009's Context section names only the report skills and chat brain, not the router prompt specifically — but its decision language and blast-radius bound are general and squarely cover this. Siding with verifier 2: intentional/accepted, exists=false.

job-applications.py applied_7d window mixes second-granular cutoff with day-granular UTC dates, so the count depends on the launchd run time

feeds/job-applications.py:54-64, 93-95 · reviewer: unswept-feeds
What it is
parse_day() maps an `applied` date (YYYY-MM-DD) to epoch seconds at UTC midnight of that day, and job_stats() counts records with `cutoff <= ts <= now` where cutoff = now - 7*86400 at second precision. A record dated exactly 7 days ago has ts = that day's 00:00Z; it is inside the window only if the feed fires before the same wall-clock time-of-day as midnight-plus-zero — e.g. with now = 12:00Z, cutoff is 12:00Z seven days back, so the 00:00Z-stamped record from seven days ago is already excluded. The effective window is therefore 6-to-7 calendar days depending on when com.helm.jobs fires, and since Daniel logs dates in local ET while they are interpreted as UTC midnight, the boundary shifts a further 4-5 hours. The idempotent day bucket then freezes whichever count the first run of the day happened to compute.
Why it matters
applied_7d is one of the two top-directive numbers on the Vitals tile; a record silently aging out a day early (relative to how a human counts 'last 7 days' of dated entries) is exactly the count-vs-reality drift class for a momentum sparkline. It also makes the metric non-reproducible: re-running the feed at a different time of day on a fresh vault yields a different number for the same store.
How to fix
Compare at day granularity: derive today's UTC (or HUD_TZ) date, compute the cutoff as `today - 6 days` (or 7, pick and document), and count records whose parsed DATE is >= cutoff date — i.e. quantize both sides to days instead of mixing seconds and days. Update the boundary test in feeds/test_job_applications.py to pin the chosen semantics at the exact 7-day edge.
Expected improvement
applied_7d becomes a stable, human-matching 'entries dated within the last N calendar days' count, independent of the launchd fire time.
Evidence
d = datetime.strptime(head, "%Y-%m-%d")
        return d.replace(tzinfo=timezone.utc).timestamp()
...
cutoff = now - window_s
...
week = sum(1 for ts in by_key.values() if ts is not None and cutoff <= ts <= now)
Verifier notes (2)
  • REFUTE (existence lens, high confidence): Read feeds/job-applications.py (parse_day lines 54-63, job_stats lines 86-96; the cited cutoff/week lines are 93 and 95), feeds/test_job_applications.py (fixed clock NOW=2026-06-19 12:00Z, boundary tests at days_ago(6) and days_ago(0)/-2), and .helm-config.json (com.helm.jobs runs daily 07:00 local). The cited code is real, but the claimed consequence is refuted: with ts always a UTC midnight and cutoff = now - 604800s, the set of counted dates is exactly {utc_today - 6 .. utc_today} for EVERY run time strictly inside a UTC day (smallest midnight >= D+T-604800 is D-518400 for any 0 < T < 86400). The count therefore does NOT depend on when com.helm.jobs fires, the window is not "6-to-7 days" — it is always 7 calendar dates including today — and re-running at a different time of day yields the same number. The only exceptions are a run at exactly 00:00:00Z (measure-zero; the feed fires 07:00 ET) and the ET-vs-UTC date skew, which only shifts the window for runs between 20:00-24:00 ET — the 07:00 local schedule never falls there. The finding's proposed fix (day-quantized cutoff = today - 6 days) computes the identical counts the current code already produces: the "record dated exactly 7 days ago" it says ages out early is the 8th calendar date, which the fix would also exclude. At most this is an info-level style note that the day-quantized semantics are implicit rather than explicit; not a bug.
  • REFUTE (impact lens, high confidence): Read feeds/job-applications.py (parse_day lines 54-63, job_stats lines 86-96, main lines 133-139), feeds/test_job_applications.py, and scripts/com.helm.jobs.plist (StartCalendarInterval 07:00 local, RunAtLoad). The mechanism the finding describes (second-granular cutoff vs UTC-midnight-stamped dates) is factually present, but its central impact claim is wrong. Because every record timestamp is quantized to a UTC midnight, the set of midnights satisfying `now - 7*86400 <= ts <= now` is IDENTICAL for any run time strictly after 00:00:00Z within a given UTC day: exactly UTC days T-6..T, i.e. a stable 7-calendar-day window (today plus the 6 prior days). The count therefore does NOT depend on when com.helm.jobs fires — the finding's own example is the counterexample: with now=12:00Z the day-7 record is excluded, but it is equally excluded at 00:01Z, 06:00Z, and 23:59Z; only a measure-zero run at exactly 00:00:00Z would include it. "Effective window is 6-to-7 calendar days depending on fire time" and "re-running at a different time of day yields a different number" are both false — the metric is fully reproducible per UTC-day bucket (bucket T always gets count of records dated T-6..T), so the idempotent day bucket freezes the same value regardless of which run wins. What remains is only (a) a semantics choice — "last 7 days" = today + 6 prior, a normal convention already pinned by the test at lines 66-67/73 (days_ago(6) in, days_ago(20) out) — and (b) a UTC-vs-ET day boundary: the window day rolls at 20:00 ET instead of local midnight, but the scheduled run is 07:00 ET (UTC date == local date), and even a RunAtLoad evening-login run just correctly pre-computes the next UTC day's bucket with that bucket's own consistent T-6..T window. Nothing here is count-vs-reality drift beyond a ≤4h day-boundary offset inherent to the documented UTC day-bucketing (module docstring lines 23-26). The proposed fix (quantize both sides to days) is harmless but fixes a non-problem — the seconds/days mix already behaves day-quantized because one side is always midnight. Finding is materially wrong as stated; at most an info-level doc nit ("window rolls at UTC midnight, 20:00 ET").

Appendix C — Method & coverage

Scoped reviewers each owned a subsystem × dimension slice, briefed on the project's intentional invariants so designs aren't reported as bugs — only violations of them. A completeness critic audited coverage and spawned extra reviewers (4 gap reviewer(s)). Findings were semantically deduplicated, then adversarially verified: two independent verifiers per finding (an existence lens that re-reads the code, an impact lens that hunts for mitigations and severity inflation), plus a tiebreaker on splits. Every finding cites file:line and a verbatim evidence snippet.
